To my sister Val, for believing



And



The man with eyes the color of rocks on the riverbed, for showing me things 
I couldn't see by myself.
Chapter 1

"Left or right?"
Alan Belmont looked at the statue of an Erudite from ages past. Its sleeves were frozen in stone, hanging to the ground. Its palms faced the ceiling, waiting for a divine command that would never come. Each hand pointed down two corridors that both extended as far as Alan could see. He had come through one that looked no different; the walls adorned with the paintings and tapestries that detailed the history of Galea, a world famed for its learning and arts.
He looked down one path, noting windows that stretched to the ceiling, casting light upon the bodies of the temple guards and Sanctum soldiers scattered on the floor. Their blood mingled and soaked into the carpet underneath. He was glad it was still too early to smell the decay.
"Did you check the map?" A woman appeared behind him with a layout of the temple displayed in the air. "We had ample time in darkspace to look it over." She slid by silently, her calf-hugging boots making no sound as she walked over the carpet.
"I took a glance," Alan said, "but this place is too big and we only need to find one person. Our contact hasn't been responding." He held his pistol with one gloved hand and rubbed his stubble with the other. He wondered if the statue in front of him held any clue, but its eyes were closed and its mouth was shut. "After all," he continued, "if I knew where to go, what would you do, Aki?" he joked. 
Aki dismissed him with a wave of her hand. She studied the map glowing from her wrist- a maze of multicolored boxes that intersected with other shapes, outlining the temple complex and its buildings. She traced a path with her eyes, following the corridors and rooms. "Left," she said.
Alan turned and started down the hallway, away from the mess of bodies that lay down the other hall. "The guards must've tried to defend that area, thinking they could hold them off in tighter spaces," he remarked. His boots left deep impressions in the carpet as he jogged.
"Good plan, poor execution," Aki said. "The soldiers sent to retrieve an offering aren't stock Sanctum." She swept the area with her gun as they ran, looking for any movement. She hopped around the bits of broken statue on the floor, her short hair bouncing in time. The ceiling had been blasted through, now missing in most places, letting a mixture of light and salty air inside.
Alan looked up to see a Galean fighter in the distance, its boxy frame leaving a trail of flame and smoke as it was shot down by two bolts of plasma launched by the Sanctum ship chasing it. An explosion followed as the outdated fighter crashed into a building, sending bits of metal raining into the nearby sea. The shockwave forced Alan to steady himself on the remnants of a column. He shook the plaster out of his hair and heard shouting ahead, the voices punctuated by screams. "I think we're close," he said. He saw Aki dash forward, her body covered in a tight black suit that blended into the shadows.
At the end of the hallway, an arch made from a giant pair of sculpted hands invited them to enter. As they went through, the shouts became louder. Alan noticed that here in the antechamber, the debris was larger, large enough to hide behind. Chunks of stone had fallen, exposing a reinforced ceiling high above them designed to withstand attacks even from orbit. He knew, however, that the Sanctum Empire no longer used such weapons.
Alan ducked through and Aki followed. They went to opposite ends of the room, crouching to avoid the superheated plasma blasts volleying over them. The fighting had become trench warfare; the Galeans held their position behind a barricade of furniture and debris, while the Sanctum soldiers shot back from across the other side. Alan slid down and hid himself behind a fallen slab of rock, next to a Galean guard that held a hand over his stomach. The wet spot underneath the guard's charcoal uniform grew larger as he tried to breathe. Alan held a hand over his, trying to staunch the flow of blood. The guard winced.
"Is the Erudite behind that door?" Alan asked. He looked at the set of wooden doors that towered over them in the antechamber. 
The man nodded and gasped, finding it hard to speak. "And?Seth." The man closed his eyes and focused his remaining energy on breathing. 
Alan glanced down the row. The Galean forces were falling fast. He caught a glimpse of Aki, surfacing from her cover and firing two shots. He saw two sprays of blood cover the wall and heard two bodies fall to the floor on the other side.
Alan opened his com. "Aki, Seth is in the other room."
"I guessed as much," she responded. "Looks like he barged through the guards and sealed the door from the inside, leaving his troops to defend." She popped up and fired again. "We don't have much time. A Javelin has been sighted entering the atmosphere at this location."
Alan played with a smooth piece of metal in one of his many pockets. "We only have one left, should we save it for inside?" he asked.
"Only if you want to kill the Erudite in the process," she said. She stopped firing and ducked behind a marble slab, covering herself with a painting as plasma splattered against the wall behind her. Some dripped onto the canvas and the oils burned green and red. "I still have my Sheet," she said, throwing away the flaming art.
Alan nodded. He was already assembling the weapon from parts ferreted out of three pouches on his pants. With a pinch of his fingers, two silver crescents came together to form a ball. He checked the pulse of the Galean next to him and felt nothing. Risking a glance, he saw the Sanctum forces as some of them stood up, preparing to jump over their own cover and close the space between them. "Are things clear on your side?"
"No friendlies left here," she said.
"Deploying Ardor," he said.
 Aki ducked. Alan pressed a button on the completed ball and lobbed it high above him towards the center of the room. He pulled himself under a table, clutching his knees and tucking in his head. He tapped a command into his wristband, pressed it to his chest, and then took a deep breath. A silvery film flowed outward from his suit and covered him, tightening around his limbs and armor and hardening against his back. Aki had flattened herself into a hole between slabs, a similar silver lining covering her boots as she pulled herself under the marble and disappeared. 
The ball hung in space as Sanctum soldiers ran underneath it. The surface of the ball rippled once and receded, revealing a blue core that pulsed white, a moment that Alan thought was strangely beautiful when he saw it for the first time. The core shrunk to a pinprick and imploded, releasing a burst of light. Alan closed his eyes and felt a wave of intense heat wash over him. The silver film glowed orange as it took the brunt of the burn.
He opened his eyes. All that remained of the table were the ashes the clung to him as he stood up. The Sheet was burnt, the edges eaten by embers that crept up his body and fluttered away. Aki came to join him as he surveyed the damage. A crater stood where the center of the antechamber used to be, surrounded by sooty prints in the shapes of bodies. The door that led to the inner chamber was blown off its hinges, lying charred on the floor. He ran to what remained of the frame, pressed his back against it and peered inside. 
The Erudite of Galea was cowering in the corner of his audience chamber, his thin hair matted with sweat as he clung to a pillar behind the holy dais where he normally governed. The ceiling was missing here as well. Within the sunlight another man stood in the middle of the chamber, dressed in robes that weren't fit for battle. He moved so fast that all Alan could see were blurs of purple and blue as he danced between what remained of the elite guard of the Erudite, striking with only his hands. Alan recognized him instantly. This was Seth, First Prince of the Sanctum and Voice of the Empire. He stood at least a head above the other soldiers, an impressive feat considering Galeans were known for their stature. Yet despite his size, Alan couldn't follow his movements. His fist seemed to hang at his side, but a moment later it impaled one of the elites in the chest. As the man staggered and fell, Alan saw a hole where the man's heart used to be. 
Having Seth here was an opportunity Alan couldn't pass up. He nodded to Aki. She aimed and fired a bullet at Seth as he was preparing to impale another particularly large elite guard. As soon as the shot rang out and the vibrations rippled through the air, Seth threw the man aside and spun away as the bullet sped past him. The bullet only took out a chunk of plaster from the wall. Alan aimed another shot right after Aki, seemingly into empty space. He watched as it connected with Seth's shoulder as the prince appeared; Seth had dodged one bullet only to hit another. It impacted and shattered inside his arm, slicing through muscles and sinew. Seth stood still as he looked at the wound. The blood seeped through the fabric of his sleeve, turning the blue into black. He lifted his head and roared in anger. Alan took the opportunity to fire two more shots at him, but Seth dodged them with ease, leaving only a shadow of himself every time he disappeared and reappeared at a different location, coming closer with every turn. Alan stepped back and watched as Aki slipped behind them and headed towards the Erudite, helping him to his feet. Alan continued to shoot, but Seth had stopped moving forward and held still. Alan looked at Aki with the Erudite near the back of the circular room, seeing no other way to escape other than through the door he was slowly backing out of.
He thought it was strange that Seth would stop, for the First Prince was known for his ruthlessness and didn't rest until his enemies were dead. Alan heard a rumble above them, the sound of ship engines. A moment later, what remained of the ceiling was splintered and sucked out. He looked up. Instead of sky, the underside of a transport emerged, its smooth silver hull designating it a Sanctum ship.
Seth was nowhere to be seen. Aki only had a moment to deflect the fingers that were aimed at her heart before another hand came and swept her aside. She collided with the back wall and fell to the ground. As he swatted her away, Seth grabbed the Erudite, who was mumbling incoherently. Alan still had his pistol trained on Seth, but couldn't shoot and risk hitting the hostage. The air around Seth and the Erudite started quivering, as if there were waves of heat surrounding them. They lifted off the floor and were pulled up through the antigravity beam, along with rocks and bits of debris. Alan couldn't believe they could equip such a small ship with such a beam. There was still much to learn from their enemies, he thought.
"Do you have a shot?" he said into his com.
Aki nodded, recovering her breath. She lay on the ground and looked up, aiming at the back of Seth's rising head. She fired. The bullet sped towards its target. But when it hit the beam the bullet slowed, then stopped, until it spun lazily along with the other debris.
Seth and the Erudite disappeared into the ship. As it started climbing, Alan opened another channel.
"Claudia, are you there?" he asked.
A crackle of static, then a male voice responded, "The High Adjudicant is currently synchronized with the Aurelius. This is Second Medium Simmons."
"Seth has taken the Erudite and they're leaving by transport ship." Alan looked up through the hole at the vessel speeding away. "Looks like they'll be heading out of system."
"We haven't detected a Sanctum ship preparing to shift," Simmons said.
"I'm looking at them right now," Alan said, "and they're going to shift. We can't risk losing the Galean Erudite to the emperor. The Baldur is close isn't it? We can use their armament." The ship had enough long range missiles, Alan thought.
"I'll check." A few seconds passed before he responded, "The AIs have decided that we cannot risk starting a war with the Galeans. Your request has been denied."
Alan clenched his fist. "Understood," he said, his level voice hiding his disappointment. He continued watching as the ship sped away until all that remained of it was a bright blip that vanished into the clouds, taking Seth and the Erudite with it. 
Alan's eyes widened when he saw the other ship descending towards Galea. "Tell me Simmons, what do you plan on doing about that thing up there?" he asked. Though he had seen a few during his battles with the empire, the Javelin-class warship was sent only to the most resistant territories. It was a behemoth of metal shaped into an octahedron, a spearhead. Where each triangular face met at the edges were deep grooves brimming with recessed plasma turrets. A full squadron of fighters waited inside it. To Alan, it seemed like overkill for a city that had already all but fallen.
The warship cast a shadow across the capital city of Galea, the bottom point burning red as it entered the atmosphere. Alan knew that once it was through, it would quickly destroy whatever pockets of resistance were left. Even now, its grooves started to glow blue as it built up charge.
"We've identified the ship as the Javelin-class warship, the Edict, last seen in the battle over Phalos," Simmons said. "The Baldur has arrived and we're evacuating as many as we can from other major cities on Galea. The rest will need to find their own way offworld. We don't have enough resources to wage a battle while coordinating rescue operations."
"Leaving another world to die?" Alan spat.
"Insubordi-" 
Alan tapped his com and cut him off. "Quiet Simmons," he said to himself. "We share the same rank."
Aki had pulled herself up and limped next to him. "Call the Umbra?" she asked.
"Already on its way," he responded. He watched as the remaining Sanctum fighters left the isolated temple and headed towards the main city further inland. He was updating his position when a large chunk of the fallen ceiling behind them started shaking. Startled, he and Aki both aimed their guns on it. A muffled voice came from underneath it.
Alan put his gun away, found purchase on the cracked floor and braced his knees. With a grunt, he pushed against the rock slab with his back, straining to lift it. He felt his legs tighten and burn with the effort. From underneath him, a large pair of hands followed by two burly arms appeared. A face emerged; Alan recognized him as the elite guard that Seth almost killed earlier. With a final heave, they pushed the slab off. The man rolled out from under it and balanced on his knees. Aki kept her gun trained on him.
The man spat dust out of his mouth. "The Erudite?" he choked out in a baritone voice. He pushed himself up with hands so large that Alan was sure he could crush his head without effort. This bear of a man seemed larger now that Seth was gone. He towered over them both, standing on legs as thick as Alan's torso.
Alan shook his head. "He's been taken." 
But the Galean could only stand for a moment. The man staggered and sat on the ground, holding a hand to a deep gash on his thigh. Aki lowered her weapon and tore a piece of fabric from one of the dead elites and wrapped it around the wound.
"Thank you," he said. "I am Argus Volgren, one of the guards of the Erudite of Galea." He looked at them. "My saviors are?" he asked.
"I'm Alan, and this is Aki," he said, pointing to her as she tied a tight knot around Argus's leg. "I believe you called for us earlier. We're from the Einhart."
"The Einhart! Thank you for coming," Argus said. "With your ships, we can go after them. Surely you have some way we can find His Sagacity!" His excited movements caused a fresh stream of blood to trickle from his leg.
Alan put a hand on Argus's chest, shaking his head, but the large man continued. "They couldn't have gotten far. Did you see where they went?" He tried to push himself up and looked around, searching for some sign of the Erudite's gold and red robes.
"He was taken by Seth onto a stealth ship," Alan said. "It's too late for the Erudite. When we received your distress call the invasion had already begun." Even with the drugs that coursed through Alan's veins, he was still saddened to the see the hopeful light fade from Argus's eyes.
Argus hung his head in shame. "I apologize on behalf of the Erudite," he said. "Galea has always been a center of learning, collecting information from many of the known worlds, a neutral land that believes that knowledge should be free and available. We have never participated in any of the conflicts that occurred in other areas, and we never thought we would be attacked in such a fashion," he said.
"Is there anything special about the Erudite of Galea?" Aki asked.
Argus held his back straighter, his voice clear and his words rehearsed. "He is the guiding light, the principal magister of the twelve schools, the great scion of the arts and leader of the peop-"
"There's no need for the speech. The man is gone and he isn't here to hear it," Alan said.
Argus sat down on the floor. A sigh escaped his lips as his failure to protect his leader fell onto his shoulders with a greater weight than any slab of stone. He took a breath and said, "The Erudite was a jerk. He was never popular, and his policies pushed away the few that would support him. But, it was still my job to protect him, and I couldn't fulfill my duty to do so."
"You did what you could," Aki said. "This isn't the first time the Sanctum Empire has come to a world to only take a few, though they will make the populace believe otherwise." She looked at the broken throne on the dais. "Was there anything the Erudite could do that others could not?" she asked.
"Now that he is gone, there's no need to keep it a secret anymore," Argus said. "We Galeans believe that knowledge is the greatest attribute an individual can have, and it is a waste when one dies and takes it with them to the grave. The Erudites have always transferred a select portion of their knowledge and being into their successors so that their descendants wouldn't make the same mistakes their forebears did. It's a tradition and technique that has been practiced here since the beginning of our recorded history, and it's an ability particular to the Erudites of Galea and their bloodline. Though it doesn't seem to have helped much in his case." He looked up wistfully. "His flaws could also be attributed to this tradition; the knowledge came with the vessels that once held them, and the vestigial remnants of the minds of the Erudites before him tore at his psyche like birds to carrion, inflicting their own opinions and viewpoints." 
Argus gazed towards the city in the sunset, watching as Sanctum fighters swarmed its skyline like flies around a corpse. The husks of buildings lay on their sides half-collapsed, as if they were hands stuck in rigor mortis.
Alan knew the look in Argus's eyes. "Remember it while you can," he said. "Or maybe it's better if you forget altogether." He recalled an evening in his own past, when he realized all that he knew was no more.
"I know most of the landmarks," Argus said. "I played in a park over there, as a child," pointing to a column of smoke, "and I trained over there on our military grounds." Alan followed his finger to a smoldering crater. "It's funny, even the most forward-thinking worlds have some backwards customs. But I'll keep them. I'll keep these memories close to me." His hands dropped and he clenched them into fists. 
He knelt on his good leg before Alan and Aki. Even on his knees he wasn't much shorter than they were standing. "You have saved my life," he said to them both. "And since we share a common enemy, I pledge what remains of it into your service in the hopes I can find the Erudite and put an end to his captor." He spoke with his head bowed.
Aki looked at Alan. "We may work together, but my goals are different from his," she said. She backed away and headed through a hole in the wall to keep track of the Edict and its descent. 
Alan helped him up. "Don't you have obligations here? This is your homeworld," he said. They followed Aki out.
Argus's face had become stone, his features unreadable. "Before the Sanctum came, I told the people I needed to of the invasion. What they did with the information was their choice. Here, upon Galea, I am limited. What can a grain of sand do to stop the tide?" He looked at Alan. "We guards dedicated our lives to the Erudite. My only obligation is to atone for my failure," he said.
From above, Alan heard the hum of engines. The Umbra came in from above, its elliptical shape black against the setting sun. Four variable hybrid quadrupole engines rotated around it, their cylinders glowing blue and white as they held the ship aloft. They were connected to the main body by electric purple tethers that crackled and popped as they heated the air around them. At Alan's command, the tethers shifted to the bottom of the ship, bringing the engines with them as they reoriented their position. The ship began to descend.
"We need to leave before the Edict arrives and turns what remains of this city to dust," Alan said. Already, most of the Javelin-class ship could be seen. Lances of plasma shot from its sides, melting the fallen buildings. "Seth got what he came here for and there are no more defenses left to hold the empire off." He stepped over the wall and headed towards the Umbra as it prepared to land on a small rocky patch.
"Look!" Aki said. Alan and Argus turned to look where she was pointing. An explosion rocked one of the sides of the Edict high above them, halting the bombardment and sending out plumes of fire from one of the hatches.

Chapter 2

"Left or right?"
It was Lydia's first time in the bowels of the Javelin-class warship, the Edict. As a consort of the emperor, she had only walked within the bright halls of the ship, a ship reserved for dignitaries and nobility. She wasn't used to the darkness of the service corridors through which she now blindly felt her way. The only light came from lamps built into the ceiling above, so high that they barely illuminated the ground she ran across. She had made her way through the maze of turns and pressure doors as best as she could, her sandals slipping on the wet floor when fear overtook her, when she saw shapes without substance in the darkness. Vents released jets of steam into the air that coated her hair, turning it into an ebony mat that slapped against the back of her blouse. Her memory and adrenaline had brought them here, but as she faced a choice between two equally gloomy corridors, she knew she was lost. She kept one hand against the wall to steady herself as she made her way forward. With her other hand, she guided her daughter, Ashra. 
Lydia asked her again. "This is what I see, one light and a choice between two identical corridors. Can you sense where there are others?" 
The princess Ashra was a child that only came up to Lydia's waist, yet she had the same dark hair and light skin that she had inherited from her mother. Though she was blind and mute, she had ways of seeing that which no one else could, and a way of communicating that was rare even among the royals of Sanctum. The princess thought it was strange to see her mother outside of their arranged appointments, but she had come when Lydia beckoned.
<Mother, I do not see why we are running from our own people,> she said. Ashra's voice sounded like the leaves of a tree rustled by a light breeze, skipping the ears and heard directly by the mind. <They chase because they were ordered to, but I do not know why we run.>
Lydia knelt down and held her daughter by the shoulders. "They are chasing us because they want you. Now that you're older, your father wants to turn you into another tool of the empire. They will beat the humanity out of you until all that's left of my daughter is a shell that obeys, like all the other children. I cannot let that happen." She stood up and squeezed Ashra's hand, "We don't have time, but we can leave here, we can leave forever, if we leave now. What do you see?"
Ashra hesitated. What her mother was afraid of should've been an honor. She was, after all, a princess of the Sanctum, even if she wasn't treated like a daughter of the emperor. Still, she would trust her.
<Left,> she said. <We should go left. There are people there, near the edges of the ship. To the right there is nothing but darkness, but behind us,> she turned and looked back as if she could see through the murk. They were still a ways away, but they moved with purpose and their steps didn't falter. <They are not far,> she said.
Lydia pulled Ashra close, felt her daughter's hand upon her hip, and they headed through the darkness. Lydia recognized the passage from the crudely drawn map she had received earlier. She kept her fingers connected to the surface of the wall, feeling the smooth stone until one of her rings snagged on a vertical slit. She released Ashra's hand and felt inside her skirt pocket for a card that was no bigger than her thumb. It was a final gift she received from one of her servants a little earlier, a eunuch that had served her faithfully for the last few years. Though they were supposed to meet before she left, he never appeared and Lydia had left alone.
She pressed the card into the slit, took her daughter's hand and stepped back. A screeching came from above as thick slabs of metal dropped from the ceiling on hidden rails. The two crouched and huddled together as the slabs collided with the floor with a blast of air that forced Lydia to shield her eyes. Foam sealant oozed out of the sides of the plates, filling the air with an acrid scent as it fused the plates together along with the floors and walls, creating a vacuum seal against decompression. It would buy them enough time.
"Let's go," she said. She grabbed Ashra and led them down another set of dark hallways. She had found her bearings, and with one more turn, they arrived at a dead end. Her hands searched along the wall, patting it up and down until she found an indent and pressed it with her finger. She heard a click and the wall panel slid to the side on invisible tracks, flooding the area in front of it with light. Lydia squinted and shielded her eyes, but Ashra didn't react, for the princess saw nothing.
Lydia looked around the corner, and seeing no one there, stepped out with Ashra. As soon as they left, the panel slid back soundlessly and sealed itself with a hiss. 
The hallway they entered was smooth and white, with graceful curves that wrapped around a long panel of mercurial glass that doubled as the wall. The energy shield that surrounded the Edict took the brunt of the force of entry into Galea's atmosphere, painting the air outside in shades of orange and red that mixed in with the sunset. Beneath them, all that remained of the capital city were spires that stuck out of the ground at odd angles, the scorched earth underneath them visible through their melting frames. Escape craft carrying refugees launched from the surface, leaving trails of wake with their ion engines. Some made it out of atmosphere and gathered enough speed to shift to darkspace. The rest were destroyed by Sanctum fighters or the Edict itself, their debris raining down on what remained of the city.
Since her capture, Lydia had seen it many times. The Sanctum Empire went to worlds with technology, with resources, with people, subjugating and acquiring what it could in an effort to expand and dominate. The empire would justify the deaths of the escaping Galeans one way or another, perhaps even going so far to suggest that their souls were at peace and one with the holy emperor; but what the empire didn't want was people hiding in the far reaches of space who would remember this day. 
She remembered when her own homeworld of Phalos had fallen. Now, she and her daughter were close to escaping the Edict, the great warship that was also their prison. Ashra would know what it was like to walk the ground of Phalos, as Lydia once did.
In the empty hallway she knelt next to her daughter, using her hands to comb and straighten Ashra's dark hair, doing her best to wipe the sweat and dirt that had covered them during their escape through the tunnels. Ashra's white silk dress was torn at the sides from a fall earlier; Lydia brushed off the grime that clung to it. "We're close," Lydia said, allowing herself to feel hope. She knew this area of the ship. This path would lead to the bay that held the escape craft she was looking for. With the preparations to conquer Galea, she hoped that the guards normally stationed in front of the bay would have other duties.
She took a deep breath. From the hem of her skirt, she unhooked a knife she had smuggled earlier and held it behind her back. She and Ashra walked with measured steps, their footfalls loud against the floor.
After turning a corner and seeing the same two guards stand in their usual positions, flanking the sides of the escape bay, Lydia steeled herself.
The two soldiers assigned to watch the escape bay were not happy where they were. Bloodlust coursed through their veins. They wished to be with their comrades as the first terrestrial raiding party. They wished to be part of the battle, to bring glory to their emperor, to spread the truth of the Sanctum Empire.
Despite their own desires, they stood guard at the bay, prepared to kill any soldier that dared run away. As they saw the royal consort and her daughter approaching, the guards bowed low, their faces held in rigid solemnity, their trunks parallel with the ground. They thought nothing of the two appearing. Perhaps the consort wanted to show the child the might of the empire firsthand.
They remained bowing as Lydia walked next to one of them, appearing to gaze out the window. When he saw the knife it was too late. In one motion, Lydia released her daughter and sliced through his neck. He clutched his throat as blood escaped through his fingers. He fell to the ground with a thud, the last of his life pooling out onto the floor.
Consort or not, the other guard reacted quickly. He ran towards Lydia and tackled her, pinning her under the combined weight of his body and armor. The knife was knocked out of her hand and clattered to the ground.
"Ashra!" Lydia cried out right before the guard clamped his hands down around her throat.
Ashra stood silently next to them. Her hair quivered as she trembled. In the past she had caught hints of her mother's life before the empire, but she never imagined she would kill another Sanctum in their bid to escape.
Lydia tried to call out again, but the guard's hands were strong and no air escaped her lips. She saw the edges of her vision darkening. She thumped against his armor, her fists useless against the metal. The interval between taps became longer.
Seeing it in the world she lived in, Ashra felt her mother's life slipping away and she made the decision any daughter would.
The guard's consciousness was a mix of colors, the red of his adrenaline infusing everything around him. Ashra focused on him, easily slipped into his occupied mind, and felt for the right synapses. Imagining herself as a vine, she wound herself through his neurons and bundled a select few together, knotting the impulses that shot through them.
The guard's hands loosened from Lydia's neck. The only thing that moved were his eyes, still filled with bloodlust, but now tinged with confusion. Lydia reached out and found the smooth handle of the knife with her fingers. She grabbed onto it and then plunged the knife between the cracks of his armor, felt as it slid past bone and into his heart. He grunted once and was still. Ashra mouthed a silent scream as if she felt the dagger plunge into her own body; the princess withdrew from his mind a moment too late. 
Lydia pushed him off to the side and coughed. The imprint of his hands was still on her neck as she drew in ragged breaths. Ashra had collapsed from the effort and pain and she lay still on the floor. Lydia wrenched the knife free, put it back into her skirt, and scooped Ashra up with both hands. She stumbled past the two bodies and made her way into the escape bay.
The bay was illuminated with a thin strip of lights. The doors to each escape craft lined up in neat rows that stretched as far as Lydia could see. She plodded ahead, counting each vessel, looking for a dimly lit number she had memorized earlier.
When she found it deeper inside the long bay, it looked no different than any other escape vessel: a small pod that would comfortably fit two, with a circular bench covered in plush red lining. A console made of light flashed once and appeared in front of Lydia as she placed Ashra onto one of the cushions. It expanded around the child, snugly embracing Ashra to the point where she wouldn't be able to move, protecting her against the rough travel ahead. 
Lydia dug in her skirt and took out a pendant in the shape of a half-moon with a clear blue jewel suspended in its center. Wrapping it in a small piece of cloth, she put it on Ashra's lap. In time her daughter would earn the right to wear it, a right she herself did not have, but that time was not now.
She busied herself with the coordinates of her homeworld, glad to see that she had chosen right and this was the modified escape craft with a darkspace drive.
Ashra stirred drowsily and mumbled, <Mother?>
Lydia continued inputting coordinates and path calculations through the unfamiliar console, cursing to herself as her shaking hands made mistakes.
<Mother,> Ashra insisted, <there is someone else here. It is strange, not one, but not two. I cannot see who->
On the inner surface of the escape pod, reflecting the dim hallway behind them, she caught the reflection of a flash of metal. She ducked and felt the blade whiz above her head, taking a few strands of her hair with it. She turned and saw nothing, but thrust her foot out and kicked into the air. Her sandal connected with something solid. The rippling air flew back into the dock and landed with a thud. Tendrils of electricity crackled around it as the cloaking device overloaded from the impact. A figure appeared on the floor.
Lydia brought out her knife as it stood up. It was sleek and covered from head to toe in a tight suit that changed colors as it sought to blend in with the surroundings.
A helmeted head emerged, black visor obscuring the face and reflecting its surroundings. It nodded towards the knife, still slick with the guards' blood. A sweet, female voice rang clear. "I finally have a reason to kill you, consort," she said, hissing the last word. She looked at the escape pod. "Killing a guard and running away with a princess?he wouldn't be happy." Lydia knew the voice and the way it would laugh and sing, as if it were the only way to hold its body together. It belonged to Lady Vijera, also called the Lady Gemini. Lydia knew that she would not be leaving the dock alive.
Lydia dove from the escape pod onto the dock. She aimed for Vijera but only fell on air as the lady leapt backwards. Back inside the dock, Lydia slammed her fist against a panel on the wall. The door slid over the escape craft entrance. Facing Vijera, she lunged forward with her knife, attempting to pierce the helmet she wore, but the assassin sidestepped and drew a long blade. Vijera parried the attack and smashed Lydia in the head with the hilt. Lydia fell and hit the ground with the back of her skull. Stars blossomed across her field of vision. As she tried to push herself up, a laughing cry sounded above her and she felt something slide through her abdomen, out her back and into the floor underneath her. It was followed by a burning pain and forced a trickle of blood to flow from her mouth. She looked at the shaft of metal that protruded from her stomach. The helmeted head came close and Vijera whispered in her ear. 
"So close. So very, very close. Poor Lydia." Vijera twisted the blade and Lydia cried out. "Where were you going? Where were you going, so far away?"
Lydia gritted her teeth and spat out blood in response, leaving crimson traces running down the visor. With a laugh, Vijera took it off, revealing a face that was white and flawless, radiant in the darkness. She leaned in until Lydia could feel her breath against her ear. "You don't have to tell me, consort. When I'm finished with you," she said, looking at Ashra pressed against the seat of the escape craft, "I'm sure she'll tell me everything, once she learns what a bad person her mother was." She drove the blade in deeper, smiling as Lydia clenched. "Well?if she could speak," Vijera said with a sneer. Standing up, Vijera removed the sword, sending waves of pain coursing through Lydia.
She raised the sword up, ready to sweep it down in one graceful arc through Lydia's neck. But Lydia fought through the pain and kicked up with all her might. Her foot caught Vijera in the stomach as she was bringing the sword down and the lady fell backward.
With her remaining strength, Lydia stumbled to the door of the craft, leaving a bloody handprint smeared across the glass. "Not in this lifetime, Vijera," she said. She looked at Ashra restrained by the chair, her tiny shoulders shaking with sobs as she felt her mother's pain. Lydia held this final image of her in her mind and thought of the love she had for her daughter. She thought she saw Ashra's trembling subside a little as she slammed her fist into the panel next to the escape pod. A second pressure door slid down. She heard the escape craft launch with a gentle thump. She smiled, even as Vijera howled behind her and drove her sword in again, this time through Lydia's heart.
Lydia had not wanted to use it, but now that her daughter had escaped from the Edict and her own life was forfeit, she pulled out the last thing the kind eunuch had given her. She would leave this world on her own terms.
As the escape pod jetted away, Ashra felt her mother shrink from her mind. When Lydia's star dimmed forever, the darkness enveloped her and she passed out. Though she could not see it, her black hair turned white, swirling around her like snow.
All that remained of her mother was a spark in the world of her mind, of the Empyrean. She held it close, willing it to live again. As she thought these thoughts, the light began to grow and take the shape of a seed, smooth and white. 
Vijera pulled Lydia's body away from the panel and watched her crumple to the ground. She glowered at the empty space where the escape pod once was, and only saw the purple light when it rolled out of Lydia's hand. She turned and ran, but her feet had only taken her so far when an explosion rocked the escape bay, destroying the surrounding craft and sending a large plume of fire into the Galean sky. Although Vijera ran faster than any regular human, the blast caught up with her, shredding the back of her suit and throwing her against the wall.
She barely came to her senses when the air started whipping around her and pulled her back. Her fingers wrapped around a doorframe, keeping her anchored as the hole in the hull sucked air and debris into the sky beyond. A crate barreled towards her; she kicked it away and waited for the wind and fire to subside before she released her grip. With blood running down her side, she limped over to the hole where Ashra's escape pod was earlier, gazing upon the sea of clouds and catching glimpses of the destroyed city below. 
She pressed a hand to her leg she called her ship. A star seemed to fall from the heavens, bright against the sunset. A trail burned behind it as it entered the atmosphere. As it slowed, the light dimmed and all that remained was a black dot, the outline of her personal ship, floating closer to Vijera as she steadied herself on the edge of the hole. It was a small craft designed for a single occupant, no more than a pair of flared wings and an open cockpit. She thought it was sleek and beautiful, similar to herself. 
Vijera heard the sound of metal warping and collapsing. Risking a glance behind her, she saw white tendrils snake through the floor of the Edict. They went through the plating as if it didn't exist; the metal armor vanished when the tendrils touched it. Unable to maintain its integrity, the damaged floor began to sink into itself. 
She didn't wait to see anymore. She put one foot into the narrow cockpit and felt it dip slightly under her weight. Her damaged knee couldn't support her weight and she collapsed into the ship. Despite the pain, she still smiled, savoring the death of the consort. Wincing as the chair made contact with her back, she adjusted herself until she was facing the setting sun. Overlapping layers of glass appeared above her, one piece sliding forward from another until the cockpit was covered by a clear crystalline shell. Proximity warnings screeched in her ears, indicating further explosions inside the Edict, but she ignored them as she sighted Ashra's escape pod in the distance. Her hands manipulated the navigation panel in front of her. In response, a line of blue ion flame erupted from under the wings as she chased after it.
Chapter 3

Alan boarded the Umbra with Aki and Argus behind him. They went up the ramp, through the crew compartments and then entered the cockpit. There were only two chairs; Alan took the one on the left while Aki took the other. He pressed his palm against a burnished metal table set under the flight deck windows that stretched around the cockpit. The ship scanned his biometric readings. Once he was verified, the command console was etched into existence by light, displaying the surrounding conditions and various parts of the ship. The yellow glow reflected off Alan's face as he manipulated the light console, his fingers working with a diagram of the cockpit they were in. Inside the console, he shifted their seats to the right with a swipe of his hand. The seats he and Aki sat on moved in response, placing Alan in the center. In the diagram, he pinched to the left of him, where the ground would be, and pulled up a trail of yellow that formed itself into a seat.
Argus watched as a small hatch opened up from the floor. An outline of the chair was imprinted in light, the seat and the back drawn into space by blue lasers. A tiny black cloud made of nanomachines streamed out of the hatch. They assembled the chair layer by layer using raw resources stored inside the Umbra. A stand erupted from the ground like a miniature tower. Plush foam materialized out of thin air, porous and yellow. They finished by wrapping it all up in a layer of black cloth.
Alan gestured to the seat, telling him to sit at the newly-created secondary weapons console. Though the chair could barely contain his bulk, the big man did his best to fit. His own light console appeared outlined in blue, giving him an overview of the armaments aboard.
For a ship so small it packed quite the armory. He studied the diagram and separated the layers of the ship from each other. Within its stealth frame was a layer of missiles, grouped based on their cores. Four stationary laser turrets drew power from the darkspace drive near the back of the ship. A complement of magnetized electric field generators, similar to magnetic pulse drive system that allowed the engines to be manipulated with complete freedom, were scattered throughout the hull. These he could use to attract an object, or if he switched the polarities, deflect oncoming metal projectiles. However, it seemed like there was one thing missing.
"Any plasma weapons?" Argus asked.
"Ineffective at long ranges with our power output," Alan responded, sitting himself in the pilot's chair. "And," he added, "the Einhart aren't too fond of using the same weapons the empire uses."
Argus noticed a hexagon in the bottom right corner of his panel. "What does this do?" he asked.
"Never press it unless I tell you to," Alan said. "The Umbra will be useless afterwards."
"And right before?" Argus asked.
"Hopefully whatever it is we wanted destroyed will be dust, and we can just float until someone rescues us. The darkspace engine is our main source of power, but it can be a weapon in a pinch." Alan sat back and zoomed in on the flame that had spurted out of the Edict. It was subsiding, replaced by heavy smoke that poured from its hull. He thought he saw a flash of white inside the smoke but couldn't be sure. "Aki, look for anomalies around the smoke. Did anything make it out?" 
"Scanning," she said, moving her fingers through her light console. "Unknown wave form detected."
"Magnify," Alan said.
The screen enlarged, showing a white sphere hanging in the air, its radiance shining even through the layers of smoke that strove to obscure it. It fell slowly to the earth, drifting as if being blown by a gentle wind. It wound its way to the space below the Edict and hung there. Twisting black lines ran across the sphere's surface, making it look like a seed. It split, and Alan had to look away as he was blinded by a brilliant flash. When he opened his eyes again, the seed was no more. In its place were white lines that crisscrossed over one another, like lightning frozen in time, all branching from a single point, roots that found purchase in the air. 
The Edict had also noticed the ball of light beneath it. Alan watched it turn and aim its battery of turrets towards it. Each cannon launched a stream of plasma towards the shining mass beneath the ship. The rays disappeared as soon as they impacted the white roots, and Alan saw no change. Nothing stopped the roots from growing longer. They undulated and extended their reach; their tips reached the fallen buildings of the Galean capital city, plowing through smoldering beams and concrete.
Once the roots were set, a shoot of light rose up from the mass, twisting and winding towards the sky. When it brushed against the enforced hull of the Edict above, it broke through with no resistance. The light carved a hole through the ship as it continued its ascent, leaving an empty path behind it, as if whatever it touched simply disappeared.
Once inside the ship, the trunk of the light tree widened, and from this trunk branches started to form. They teased their way through space, metal and people, without regards to who or what they were. Sheets of glass shattered as the branches found their way to the exterior of the ship. The crewmembers that ran into one of the shining boughs were killed instantly, the atoms of their bodies pulled apart and dispersed by the wind and venting atmosphere. Some people fell to the ground in pieces as the branches sliced through and separated one limb from another.
Alan watched from afar as a tree made of light, taller than any building built on Galea, destroyed a Javelin-class warship. These ships were technological marvels that were the pride of the Sanctum Empire's fleet, and they had conquered dozens of worlds before their might, Alan's homeworld being one of them. Yet, the destruction of the ship was so fast and complete that no escape pods launched from its gutted frame. The trunk of the tree must have gone through the core of the ship, he guessed. No power was left and only hazy red fires could be seen jetting sporadically from the breached areas of the ship.
In a moment, it all faded. The white light, the roots and the tree it had become, vanished. All that was left again was the seed, and as Alan zoomed in on the image, he watched it fall apart, thinning into motes of light that scattered into nothing. Lifeless and without thrust, the Edict fell from where it had floated, the remaining gravitational fluxes inside pulling it into itself, making it look like a pair of crushed pyramids. It fell as if in slow motion, but Alan saw the distorted air whipping behind each of the corners and knew better than to remain on the ground.
 "Hold on," he said. Harnesses wove their way across his body as he repositioned the four engines around the Umbra, watching them swing around on their electric tethers and rotate. He eased the ship upward with his fingers inside the light panel, controlling the individual thrust of each engine, making minute adjustments based on the haptic feedback. Tight blue energy spiraled from each of the four engines. The ship rose smoothly, and Alan got a view of the warship as it crashed into the flaming wreckage of the once great capital of Galea. A dome of dust erupted from the impact site, spreading outward and threatening to engulf the temple of the Erudite and the Umbra with it.
Alan looked at Argus. "That light tree, was that a Galean weapon?"
"I don't even know if that was a weapon," Argus said. "It seemed like the ship just happened to be in the wrong place at the wrong time." He looked at Alan. "If we had something like that, you can be sure we would've used it at the beginning of the invasion, not at the end."
"Then what was the source?" Alan said. "Aki, switch to infrared and ignore the heat signature from the impact."
The screen shifted and the dust disappeared, replaced with a hazy purple background with blooms of red and yellow that faded as Aki removed the fallen Edict and the burning city from view. All that was left were two pinpricks of red and white speeding away from the wreckage. Alan zoomed in on the image. One flew at a steady speed on a straight course, while the other was erratic and shaky but much faster. If Alan was going to catch up, there wasn't time to go into orbit and risk the two shifting to darkspace. The Umbra would have to go through the dust.
"Shields," Alan said.
Argus fumbled around the controls, looking for any oblong indicator that might've governed a shield or protective device. As he searched, a shimmering layer came across the front of the ship, spreading from concealed generators on the hull. Individual purple squares patched themselves together from the front, briefly blocking their view, and spread upwards and out of sight. As they connected, they lost their coloring and the ravaged landscape of Galea reappeared.
"Shields active. Adjusting strength midflight for incoming projectiles," Aki said. "An estimated three minutes before they are exhausted."
Alan pushed forward with his arms and they dove into the storm. The ship rattled as it entered the swirling dust. Aki heard crackles of electricity as she adjusted the shield to deflect debris that flew in their path, strengthening parts and weakening others as necessary. Argus had always been uncomfortable in the air; he always wanted to keep his feet on solid ground. He never liked the idea of his life in the hands of a pilot, but Alan flew with a steady hand, always keeping his eyes on the two dots. Though their targets traveled fast, the Umbra was faster and gained. As they passed through the center of the impact site, secondary explosions shook the air around them. Alan guided the ship and rolled with the turbulence. For a moment, Aki's hair hung straight up from her head as they flew upside down. Alan righted the ship, and Argus saw giant pieces of melted metal, the remnants of the Edict, draped over the buildings like a shroud.
They could still see nothing but dust when a rhythmic beeping chirped over the noise. "Incoming from Claudia," Aki said.
"Take it," Alan responded, his eyes never leaving the route that only he could see.
Static buzzed over the speakers, replaced by a smooth female voice. "Alan, we detected a giant burst of delta waves from the other side of the planet, where you are. What did you see?" she asked.
"A giant tree," he replied.
"A tree?"
"Yes, a tree made of light." Alan twitched his fingers inside the light console and the three of them were ripped to the right as a hunk of concrete flew past them.
"Traces of the delta waves are still in the area," Claudia continued, "but the source is accelerating and will be out of detection range in thirty seconds. Can you track it?" 
"On it."
"And the Erudite?"
"Taken by Seth. You might want to ask Simmons what the AI decided upon."
He heard her sigh. "Damn it, Simmons," she said. "I'll deal with him later."
"Understood," Alan said as he barely dodged the remnants of a Galean fighter that was blown into the sky with the explosion. A wing hit the Umbra and warning sirens rang.
"That last hit drained a large part of our shield reserves. Recalculated as ten seconds remaining," Aki said.
Alan responded to Claudia. "I'll give you a full report and hopefully something more when we dock with the Aurelius. Umbra out."
As they headed near the edge of the storm, the dust began fading and Alan could make out parts of the sky without infrared. He glanced at Argus. "I'm shifting weapons control over to you. Take out whatever is chasing it." Alan flicked two switches and set weapons to the left console where Argus sat. Just in case, he kept his own fingers resting on the launch triggers, ready to resume control should the Galean fail, or worse, betray him.
Argus nodded and cycled through his options. There was no more dust or debris as they started to clear the atmosphere of Galea and climbed higher. The stars were shining brighter in the darkened sky. He settled on the fastest missiles. Though they had less concussive power, he wouldn't need too much. He aimed at the chasing ship and fired the three missiles in quick succession. The ship they were aiming for, a small black vessel with flared wings and a single pilot, anticipated the projectiles. Slits above its wings retracted, releasing formless gray clumps that spun in the wake of the ship. Each clump separated into smaller marble-shaped pellets. When the missiles neared, the pellets turned crimson and elongated into needles. 
The needles flew towards the incoming projectiles. One needle lodged itself in a missile's plating, turned into a liquid and dissolved the metal underneath it. Another set of needles crammed inside, flooded the circuitry, and melted the guidance core of the missile. The missile fell back to Galea, disarmed. The second missile fell in the same manner, but by then Argus had primed the set of lasers aboard the Umbra. He shot a steady beam of light that burned a path through the red needles. With his left hand, he guided the last missile behind the laser. It dodged a needle and impacted; detonating and blowing a wing off the ship. The small fighter spun away wildly out into space.
"Nice shooting," Alan said.
"The escape pod is nearing darkspace shift speed," Aki said. They all focused their attention on the remaining target.
"Didn't think they could fit an engine on an escape pod," Alan said. A black ring appeared around the escape pod, blotting out the stars and distorting the edges of the pod as the light bent around it.
"Initializing magnets," Argus said. He left the four magnets necessary for the engines under Alan's control and directed the rest towards the escape pod. The black halo slowly faded as the pod lost the speed and energy necessary for the darkspace shift. Argus kept an eye on the pod as he brought it closer to the Umbra. "Where do you want it?" he asked. There was no place to bring it into the ship.
"Keep it outside. We'll tow it back to the Aurelius," Alan said. They picked up speed as Argus stabilized the pod behind them.
"Contacting the Aurelius for newest coordinates," Aki said. "Updating location while in darkspace."
Alan's fingers flew across the light console, highlighting different parts of the ship. Four thumps echoed around them as the tethers of the engines that had been rotating around the Umbra shortened. The engines fastened to the hull.
"Bubble constructed. Dark matter vesicles prepped. Darkspace engine engaged," Aki said.
"Shift," Alan commanded.
The four engines and the main booster glowed black, and then shot them into a dimension of folded and layered time and space. Inside the cockpit, the stars turned red then black as the ship left the visible color spectrum.
Alan dug inside one of his pockets for a small bottle and pulled out two green pills. He put them between his teeth and bit down, feeling the liquid flood his mouth. The Virifen pills tasted bitter as they always had, but he had done it for years and came to enjoy the flavor. He found comfort and peace as the back of his head tingled.
Though the stars never seemed to get closer, the Umbra sped away from Galea. In a flash of light, the ship and the escape pod it towed behind it were gone.

Chapter 4

Darkspace was a wondrous place, and Alan never tired of the jump. The darkspace engine, separate from the four engines that propelled the Umbra through normal space, was hidden away behind layers of shielding and steel deep inside the ship. Most of the time it ran as a generator that provided energy to the systems onboard and supplied the gravity inside the ship. But when activated with a touch from Alan through his light console, the darkspace engine hummed with life, surrounded by black lightning as it altered the space around it. 
A volume of normal space, called the bubble, was preserved around the ship and the escape pod behind it. But in darkspace, where light and other waves were distorted, all that was visible was the engine, floating alone. The darkspace engine remained in darkspace while it was being ferried from one point to another, acting as the link between the dimension it resided in and normal space.
The electricity subsided as it collapsed an area between normal space and darkspace. The Umbra materialized around it, surrounded by a shield that protected it from the physics of a dimension that no scientist from any world or empire fully understood.
"The Uchida sonatas," Alan said to the ship. He removed his hands from the light console. It flickered once and disappeared, leaving behind a surface of brushed metal. Soft music began tinkling through the cockpit as the harness that held him retracted into the seat. The captain's chair was quickly dismantled as nanomachines took it apart molecule by molecule. Alan stood up and stretched, feeling several of his joints pop, his shoulders stretching the limits of his armor as he pressed his arms towards his head.
Argus gazed at the swirl of colors that glanced off the outside of the bubble, creating a fractured rainbow that stretched across the length of the ship. "I've only been in darkspace one other time," he said, his voice tinged with sadness and awe. "Before I was a guard for the Erudite, I accompanied a Galean ambassador to another planet. That was before the Erudite decided we could be self-sufficient, before he decided to close our borders to the outside and the ambassadors were made superfluous."
"That policy didn't work out too well, did it?" Alan said. He beckoned for Argus to follow him into the crew quarters.
Argus wanted to say something, about how he had lost all he had ever known in less than a day, but he was in the company of those he didn't know and decided to remain silent. Despite his training, his heart still ached for the place he had always thought of as home. He took those emotions and locked them away, kept them in a dusty area of his mind that he would try not to visit. As he stood up, he felt a jolt of pain run up his leg and remembered his previous injuries.
When he arrived, Alan was busy brewing something inside the cramped kitchen. Next to it was a small table. Three cups pushed their way out of its surface, made from the table itself as it generated the cups from its own material and then separated them with rings of light. Alan poured a pungent brown liquid into two of them. Argus caught hints of cardamom along with other spices he had never smelled before. Alan raised his cup to him. "To living another day," he said. He tilted his head back and tried to down his drink with one gulp. Some liquid dribbled out of his mouth as the scalding concoction burned his tongue. Argus raised his cup, tiny in his hand, but said nothing. He took a sip. It was bitter yet refreshing, bringing Argus to his senses and relaxing his sore muscles. The pain in his leg eased up a little. 
He watched as the thin and hard armor plates decompressed with a hiss around Alan. They fell to the ground, revealing a suit underneath that was even tighter against the soldier's body, outlining the taut muscles underneath. He didn't look that old to Argus, but his eyes and the way he carried himself suggested lifetimes of experience.
 "Is darkspace still as hard to shift into as before?" Argus asked. "Despite Galea being a center for cultural knowledge, our engineering was sorely lacking."
"The basics remain the same, though the Einhart, combined with Auroran help, have made some improvements. Our scientists on the Aurelius have made progress with the time distortion and bubble flexibility, resulting in fewer casualties than before. You wouldn't normally find a darkspace engine on a ship this small, but since our missions are a little more?urgent, they put one in."
"May I ask what it is your group specializes in?" Argus asked.
"Reconnaissance. Information gathering. Where just a few people would be better than an army. We tend to operate outside of the typical chain of command."
"Oh? In that case, who do you report to?" Argus took another sip of the brew. He felt the heat course through his body, a welcome feeling amidst the coldness of space.
"Claudia Einhart."
"The High Adjudicant!" Argus said, surprised. "Leader of the Einhart?"
"The one and only."
"And she was the one on the com just now?"
Alan nodded.
"If I had known!" Argus held up a hand to his forehead in disbelief. "Are the rumors true?" he asked.
"Rumors surround her like mist," Alan replied.
"You know, the one?" Argus hesitated, his voice dropping to a whisper. "Is it true she sent a whole subfleet retreating with just three ships?" 
"That was before the Aurelius was made. You've done your reading," Alan said, impressed.
"Though I couldn't take part, I went to great lengths to keep on top of the war that went on in the other ends of space. In fact, I always wanted to meet someone from the Einhart, though under different circumstances."
"Yeah, she did rout that subfleet with just three ships. A risky maneuver, but she's always been an excellent if not brutal strategist." Alan massaged one of his shoulders, bruised from the battle before.
They looked up as Aki came in, walking with a fluid grace that made her seem like she knew her way around the inner workings of both ships and men. "I've recalibrated some sensors. If anything happens to that pod we're towing, we'll hear about it," she said, nodding her head towards the back of the ship. She took out a flask and poured a dark green liquid into the remaining cup. She blew on it with gentle puffs to cool it off.
"This is Aki Fushimi from Aurora," Alan said. He turned to her. "What do you think Aki, should we keep him?" he asked jokingly.
Aki looked Argus over. "He's done well so far. Let's see what other tricks he has up his sleeve."
Argus nodded his thanks.
"While I work on behalf of the Einhart, Aki is here for different reasons," Alan said.
"And what reasons might those be?" Argus asked.
"I'm more of a consultant," she said. She sat on the last chair, crossed her legs, and took another sip of her bitter drink. "My sister was captured by the empire a long time ago."
"I'm sorry to hear that," Argus said.
"She was careless," Aki responded, her voice controlled and practiced. She spoke with a hint of the Auroran accent, the words layered with silk as they left her lips. "There's no hope of getting her back, so I've been assigned to terminate her. Signs of Auroran technology have been seen in some newer Sanctum weapons, so we believe she's been leaking information."
"No Auroran would willingly give up your secrets to the Sanctum Empire," Argus said. "The empire could afford your services, I'm sure."
"No, no agent would," she agreed. "But it's not willingly. You know of Lady Vijera?"
"Yes, the Lady Gemini. I've read about her." Argus said.
"There's a reason she's called that," she said. 
Argus's eyes widened. "Your sister? She merged with your sister?"
Aki nodded. "My sister, Rin. Her will is strong and she fights it." She let a smile flash across her lips. "It's said that the Emperor himself has had to use his own strength to keep my sister under control."
"We never knew who Vijera merged with," Argus said. "We only knew of her as the most unstable of the children."
"Vijera wasn't ever stable. Even before the merge my sister was as beautiful as she was strong. Nobody could ever keep Rin down and Vijera was no match. Merging with Rin created a lunatic, but a lunatic with the skills of an Auroran assassin. I am here to assist Alan, since he seems to come across her often," she said. Alan pulled back the collar of his suit, revealing a long scar across his shoulder. "Until she's taken care of," Aki said, "I'll be around. If you ever see her, let me know where she is." She got up. "I'll prep a medbed for your leg. Come to the back when you're done." She got up and went through a door that led deeper into the ship.
Alan waited till she left. "You should see her with a rifle. Light-based or metal, she is an amazing markswoman," he said. He leaned and whispered, "But she can't operate the weapons on the Umbra worth shit. I'm glad you're-" Argus shot his hand out and pulled Alan's head to the side as a knife spun through the air, missing Alan's ear by inches. It landed into the table with a thud, its edge bright against the dark handle. "She also has great hearing," Alan said, smiling.
After they finished their drinks, the table absorbed the cups back into itself, filtering out the waste and transferring it into the ship's biogenerator. The biomass would be recycled for other uses.
Argus got up and winced as his leg throbbed.
"We'll take care of that in the back," Alan said. "Come on."
Argus felt his eyelids getting heavier. The adrenaline was leaving his system, and coupled with the blood loss, he found himself lightheaded as he stood up. He grabbed a chair for support. Alan came over and put a hand underneath his shoulder to prop him up, though his legs buckled under the large man's weight. 
"Just?a few?steps?over there." Alan struggled to speak and move at the same time. He half-set and half-tossed Argus into the medbed. Aki returned and put his feet up so that his whole body was inside it, though he barely fit. A clear green shield came over Argus. The medbed analyzed his leg, listing a series of medicines and procedures. Argus nodded his thanks. The last thought he remembered was how grateful he was these two had helped him.

Chapter 5

Sanctuary, the throneworld and foundation of the Sanctum Empire, was one of the empire's greatest achievements. Light shone from above, washing over the deep valleys and even deeper forests in a layer of light.
The small planet was in the shape of a disk. It was mostly untouched, a pristine home for its unique inhabitants. A large bird, called a rukh by Sanctuary's few humans, flew near the treetops. Its wings skimmed the edges of trees and knocked leaves free as it searched for prey on the ground. Bright blue plumage that mimicked the sky made it invisible from below. Upon seeing a big furry animal dozing in the shade, it flapped its wings once and dove towards the ground with talons outstretched, thinking it had found an easy meal.
A tree, seemingly no different than the others, shook its leaves once and parted its branches. A gaping maw emerged from the top. Sharp teeth gleamed for a moment before the whole trunk stretched and shot up. They clutched the diving bird by one of its wings and dragged it inside its mouth. The bird struggled and squawked, but the branches returned, their leaves and sprigs weaving into each other, creating a net that made escape impossible. The cries of the bird were abruptly silenced with one snap of the arboreal's jaws. A clump of blue feathers floated to the ground and the tree stopped moving. Ever hungry, the arboreal balanced the corpse of the furry animal on one of its roots, moving it up and down in a simulation of deep breathing.
But the forest had its edges. In the middle of Sanctuary was a city. The nobility and their servants lived within, and all prayed to the emperor once when they awoke and once before they slept. All inhabitants of the city were sent as tributes, a reminder to their respective homeworlds that the empire always had at least one of their own as hostage.
The homes and buildings that dotted the city all faced in one direction, bowing as if in homage. And in that one direction there stood a palace, tall and mighty, the curved roofs of its towers challenging the sky. Floating gardens obscured the view of the palace from the rest of Sanctuary, and in the center of the palace was the tallest tower, the citadel.
Inside the citadel, Seth, Voice of the Empire, knelt upon the floor. Sunlight streamed in through the chamber for there was no ceiling to block it. It illuminated a crystal throne, a prize from another world, rumored to lengthen the life of whoever who sat in it. He continued kneeling as he heard the slurping, wet noises that signaled the beginning of the merge. Though he himself had done it twice before, the sounds always sickened him, as flesh dissolved and was broken down into its most basic of components. Yet the sounds also brought with them a sense of excitement, of a future limited not by what one was, but only by what one would be.
He risked a glance upward and saw the face of the Erudite of Galea, frozen in a mask of fear. The rest of his body was also paralyzed, encased in a block of ice. Only his eyes could dart back and forth, looking for help that would never find him.
The Erudite had been arrogant, Seth thought, and he deserved to lose his position. And to be merged with the emperor himself! Seth felt the honor might've been too high for such an incompetent ruler, but his father had a reason for everything he did. Even with the power of three minds, Seth had only begun to understand some of the emperor's plans, plans that were convoluted, complex, and baffling. Yet the result was always another territory under Sanctum control.
The merge was starting. Cocooning was always a delicate process, needing the utmost physical and mental control. A thick membrane had already wrapped around the emperor and started to cover the Erudite. Seth remained kneeling through the entire process, entertaining himself by finding patterns amongst the tiles of white stone, decorated with renderings of the orbits of planets and the formation of stars. 
At last the sounds stopped. Seth stood up and looked at the current incarnation of the emperor, a purple chrysalis that stood taller than he did. It was in the shape of a drop of water, and Seth wondered if it looked that way because of how large the Erudite had been. The purple became muted as a thick layer of frost spread out from the top and made its way down to the bottom, covering it in jagged protrusions. Seth put his hands around the cocoon, and his skin burned as it touched the ice. With a gentle push he lifted it up, cutting himself on the icicles as he did so. The cocoon floated upward, past three curved spires that jutted up and away from the top of the palace. Along the cocoon's bottom, a rim of frost began to appear and separated. Each granule of frost pulled water from the air and expanded into a shard of ice. They stuck together, forming a crown that turned underneath the cocoon.
Seth watched as the cocoon settled in the center of the three spires, held aloft through the emperor's power. Light cast itself upon the ice cocoon. The refracted beams of light shot across the throneworld, creating a dazzling jewel that sat atop the citadel. Rainbows danced across the landscape as the ring of frost underneath slowly rotated. All would know of the emperor's glory as it cast its brilliance across the land.
Back on the ground, Seth looked at his hands, watching as the cuts from the ice sealed themselves together. The bleeding stopped as muscles and sinews grew back. His skin fused over the wounds and no trace of the damage was left; all that remained was a thin line of blood. He expected a servant to have brought him a towel by now, but he remembered the throne room was still partitioned off. No one outside of the royal family could see the merge.
He stood next to the throne and laid his hand upon the side of the chair, resting it on a protrusion of quartz. His foot tapped a pattern into the stones behind the throne, feeling each tile sink into the ground as he pressed it. With a click, the walls that surrounded the throne room descended, retreating back into the sides of the tower with a rumble.
The chamber became a large platform as the walls fell away. Seth stood out in his purple robes, his shoulder still stained red from the bullet Alan landed, the only one he could remember in recent memory. Surrounding him below the steps were prostrate figures; knees bent under their stomachs and palms flat against the floor. They were covered in the black shrouds that all nobility wore within the palace.
Here, at the top of the citadel where the wind was most fierce, those that did not kneel or plaster themselves to the ground were blown off the platform. But Seth stood tall and strong. Though his robes rippled and billowed around him, he did not bend and he did not yield.
Seth, the Voice of the Empire, spoke. "His holiness the emperor, ruler of the Terra Sanctum and the worlds under his command, has broken the confines of his mortality and is in cocoon." His voice was powerful and resonant, cutting through the wind itself. All who heard it wished to be closer to the source of such sound, even if it announced their own demise. Though the nobility came from different worlds, their hearts were moved. In their fervor, some of them murmured in ecstasy or wept in the presence of the emperor, blinded by the rays of light refracted from the crown.
"I, Seth," he continued, "the First Prince of the empire, will be the voice of the emperor in his stead." When no bolt of ice came from the cocoon to strike Seth down, the nobility believed him. They touched their foreheads to the ground to show respect for the interim ruler.
The nobles scampered aside as Seth walked to the edge of the platform that held the throne. Its view and height were unparalleled by anything else on Sanctuary. Seth himself had thrown a few people off of the precipice, from a height so far up that even he could not hear their bodies shatter upon the gardens below. He looked past the forest of arboreals and the city that lay beyond it, beyond the streams and rivers that plunged off the sides of the disk. He thought he could do a better job of ruling than his father did. He would prove it to his father, the rest of the family, and even the low nobility with their faces against the stone. What his father could not accomplish he would, for the fires of ambition burned brightly in his merged soul, and he would not rest until there was no more resistance to the empire; until he could rightfully claim the position of emperor as his own.

Chapter 6

"This is Alan Belmont of the Umbra, requesting permission to dock with the Aurelius."
Alan and Aki sat next to each other at their light consoles. Argus remained blissfully asleep inside the medbed.
A female voice responded. It was so controlled, Alan wasn't sure if it was an AI or a human he was talking to. "Please describe the item in tow behind your ship," she said.
"It's an escape pod, the source of the delta waves above Galea. Check with Claudia." Now that he was so close to setting foot on the Aurelius, Alan chafed at the bureaucratic procedures. 
Just the docking bay alone spanned the entire view of the Umbra's cockpit, but Alan remembered when it was nothing more than an idea. From its inception, the Aurelius had been built as a floating city, a necessary center for the Einhart as their rebellion had gained traction. It had become such a hodgepodge of different buildings and sections that, in its entirety, it could never enter a planet before entry stresses tore it apart. It followed a rough pattern, but haphazardly added circular habitation platforms, each housing thousands, sprang out at sharp angles.
In the center of the mass stood three transparent domes made from hexagonal plates, each one looking like a gigantic version of an insect's compound eye. Under each dome were fields of vegetables and fruits that could be grown in a week, along with protein synthesis farms that used engineered bacteria to produce chains of complex nutrient additives.
At the bottom was the command module, the largest of the Garuda-class supercarriers of the Einhart, the core of the Aurelius. Though it made up less than an eighth of the total space of the complex, it had enough energy to power a facility twice the size of the city it held on its back. It was hidden away behind layers of plating, the first of which had begun to open. The triangular slats spun away into thick walls, revealing another layer of metal. Six sentry drones, long and white with glowing red sensors atop bulbous heads, detached from the inside of the slats and flanked the Umbra. Light flooded the cockpit as they scanned the ship.
The voice returned. "Please release your cargo and lower your shields." Alan flicked some switches within the light console and the magnets spun out of alignment. The escape pod floated free.
Three of the sentries left and charged their own magnets, pulling the pod into the middle of the circle they formed, then started spinning around it. When they reached a speed where they all began to blur together and the escape pod couldn't be seen, laser blasts from their heads eliminated trace particles and contaminants upon it. They escorted it to another portion of the ship while the three remaining sentries did the same thing with the Umbra. Ship sensors picked up focused heat signatures as remnants from their journey in Galea were vaporized.
"Scans show you have an unexpected life form aboard the Umbra. Please explain."
Alan looked back at the crew quarters. "He was one of the Erudite's guards and may have valuable information concerning the empire. He sustained injuries to his leg when we were on Galea; the medbed onboard stabilized him, but I'd like to give him a full physical aboard the Aurelius."
"Understood. A medical team will be waiting." A pause, then the voice softened into someone Alan recognized. "I'm glad you're back, Second Medium. Your usual spot has been reserved for the Umbra in Dock B. I'd offer you the tractor, but I'm sure you don't need it."
Alan smiled. "So it was you, Bri," he said. The remaining three sets of shielding retracted into the walls of the Aurelius and Alan guided the Umbra forward. "I was debating whether or not it was a computer. It's hard to tell the AI from the humans nowadays."
"Sorry Alan. We're under higher security here ever since the sudden attack on Galea and can't take chances. We've been picking up their survivors as their escape craft arrive, but there haven't been many."
"I understand, Bri. Everything good at home?"
"Now that you're back," she said.
Alan could hear the smile on the other end. Behind the layers of plating, the dock had come into view. Alan guided the Umbra into the cavernous belly of the Aurelius. Recessed lamps flooded the giant chamber with light, illuminating the other much larger warships inside. Gravity was disabled inside the docking bay and the crew floated within it, bringing supplies and equipment to and from the ships with minute thrusts from the jet packs located in their suits.
