"Lydia killed two guards and was stealing Ashra away," she murmured.
"Don't play dumb with me. Death is all you can do, and you sow it everywhere without consequence to the fruit it bears. The consort Lydia was an asset, and she produced a princess that was to be the best of us. And not only have you killed one of the few women capable of bearing his children, but you also allowed the most precious daughter to be captured by our enemies."
"I was unprepared for Ashra's awakening," Vijera said. "And she had help." Her eyes remained downcast, but confidence crept into her voice. "I will find her. I will bring our sister back to us."
"No, you will not," Seth said. "You have failed already. If you weren't related to me and still loved by Father I would've thrown you off the top of the citadel like a common noble." Vijera knelt in deference as he continued. "Do not forget I am the First Prince. I have survived two merges with princes that were far more difficult than an assassin from Aurora. You have failed, Vijera, and I will correct your mistake." 
A plan had begun to form in his mind. "You will take my place on Abyssinia, and you will kill, because that is what you are good at, and it is the only thing you can do. Show them the talents you acquired from Rin Fushimi," he said. "Make them fear us again. Spare the lower scientists, for they do the work, but destroy the commanders for they are treacherous. I am not heartless." Seth was satisfied. "Find out where they have sent the information, and make sure there is no trace of their betrayal. The other worlds cannot know that we have been deceived under our very noses." He turned away. "Go, now."
Vijera stood up and left, concealing her rage at being ridiculed by showing only her back. She walked away with measured steps that cracked the tiles of the stone floor.
Seth called for a servant. "Bring me everything we know on Galean customs," he said.

Chapter 14

Akiko Fushimi, or Aki, as everyone outside of Aurora called her, pulled out the rubbery glove that looked and felt like skin. The holographic projection had already been setup on the floor. A convincing image of Simmons floated in the air. As she put on the glove, she accidentally swept her hand through the image, causing it to distort for a moment before it snapped back into place. Fooling the sensors that led into the holds of the Aurelius was no easy task. She chastised herself silently for her carelessness. She flexed her fingers, feeling the fake skin adhere to her own. A thin layer of oil covered the fingers and palm. She pressed her hand against the panel while using her other hand to input her destination. The sensors read Simmons's handprint, matched it with his DNA, and Aki quickly stepped back into the hologram of Simmons, completely hiding herself inside its light. Hampered by the weights she applied to herself to match his bulk, she wasn't as graceful as she normally was, but she was inside before the sensors noticed anything outside of the normal parameters for Fitzgerald Simmons. The lift started to descend.
Earlier, with Alan's permission, Aki had created a copy of Simmons's hand when she met Alan in the one bar that he always went to when he was back on the Aurelius. He had a drink that was untouched, made even fuller as the ice inside melted and pushed the liquid up to the edge of the glass. He sipped only because he had to, grimacing every time he swallowed. It was a strange ritual. Perhaps he liked being around people outside of the military, or perhaps it was because he could find the privacy he wanted in a crowded place where no one would notice him. Aki leaned towards the latter. The bar was filled with patrons she hadn't seen before, including some Galeans that had just arrived on the Aurelius. Those that still had the means to drowned their sorrows in drink.
Alan met Aki at the bar to make a request. A request outside of regular channels since he couldn't go himself. Aki did this as a personal favor to him, but she would've gone even if he didn't ask. There were many things she wanted to ask the princess, and now that she had the approval of one of the few people aboard this ship that appreciated her presence, she went with nothing clinging to her conscience. She had the feeling Alan knew what she wanted, and did it more out of friendship rather than work.
It wasn't difficult to get Simmons's DNA. The speck of blood she drew when she pushed her blade against his neck was more than enough, and he was the careless sort to leave handprints over everything he touched, including command consoles when he was angry.
The lift was slow as it made its way down to the holding cells, probably a result of nothing more than heavy traffic from the other lift compartments in the vacuum tube. She took the time to review the tactics she had come up with in her mind. There would be at least two sets of guards; one guard in the doorway and two in the inner chamber where Ashra was held. The first guard was the most difficult. She would need to keep him standing as if nothing were wrong until she could reach the inner chamber. That would require a paralysis technique. She could always go with an electrical discharge, but that would require embedding a transmitter into his flesh. It would be painful and she didn't want to hurt her current allies. There were always the needles coated in nerve toxin, but that could lead to permanent paralysis. No, in the end she decided she would do it the old-fashioned way, as she learned from her training on Aurora. The other guards in the inner chamber she could incapacitate with a reverse rising dragon followed by a diving falcon and blooming lotus fist.
The lift stopped. The guard looked up from his post and stood up straighter when he saw Simmons appear. He snapped a salute. "Sir!" he said.
The guard only caught a blur of movement. Simmons disappeared into a speck of light. After that, he saw a pair of eyes, dark and narrow. By the time he had enough sense to reach for the gun at his side, he felt pinpricks strike his calf, back, chest and shoulders. Though he felt the pistol grip, he couldn't close his hand around it. His fingers were frozen in place. They only twitched when he tried harder to move them. He wanted to look down, but found his neck was paralyzed as well. The only thing he could do was swing his eyes wildly back and forth.
Aki didn't know the code, the guard certainly wouldn't tell her, and Alan wasn't able to see what this guard had input earlier. She was left with one choice. She pressed a point on the guard's shoulder, feeling her nail dig into his flesh. His hand shot up in response to the pressure point trigger, as if he were a marionette. Two more presses along his ribs and he was facing the door leading to the inner chamber. The reflex for the right elbow joint was located in the lower back. She crouched and tapped the point like she was playing an instrument. She heard the pounding of his fist on the door above her. His eyes, wide and full of fear, would add to the deception.
The door opened and Tairus came out with his pistol raised. He checked the corridor and saw his comrade frozen in place. He didn't see the assassin underneath him. Aki pushed off the ground, her fist held above her head. It impacted with Tairus's chin, jarring his brain inside his skull. He crumpled to the ground. Aki's leap brought her higher, and she repositioned herself in midair against a wall. She kicked herself towards the remaining guard. She covered the distance in a heartbeat, avoiding the electric barrier that held Ashra. If she had a blade, she would've cut the last guard's throat open, but he was an ally, so she landed behind him. With her hands clasped into a club, she smashed her fist into his head, then opened it and struck her palms into the base of his skull in two rapid strikes. She caught his slumped body as he fell and laid him gently on the floor.
Aki stood up and breathed. The first guard still stood on the threshold between the chambers, his arm raised and his fist curled as if he were still pounding on the door. Aki pressed a point on his shoulder. The blood flowed normally again and the signals that traveled from his brain reached the rest of his body. However, a moment later she pinched another point on his shoulder and he collapsed as quickly as the others. She pulled him inside and closed the door behind her. Prying each of their mouths open, she slipped small, tasteless lozenges under their tongues that quickly dissolved.  They wouldn't remember any of this.
Ashra had watched the action through the borrowed eyes of the guards. She jumped from one to another as each guard was knocked unconscious. When the last one fell, she was without sight. In the Empyrean, only Aki's star remained. It was similar in shape and color to a part of Lady Vijera, so Ashra guarded her thoughts and movements around the assassin. 
As if knowing how she felt, Aki said, "To show you I mean no harm, let us speak as equals." The light barrier that surrounded Ashra flashed once then disappeared, leaving only yellow rays that faded to nothing. Aki moved away from the control console and sat in the chair in front of Ashra and crossed her legs. "You and I, we are both outcasts here," she said. "I, by duty, and you, by birth."
Though the barrier had disappeared, Ashra remained where she was. <You would not risk betraying the Einhart for something trivial,> Ashra responded. <What is it you want?> She kept her mind to herself, only allowing her voice to reach Aki. Who knows what would happen if she tried to see through her eyes? This woman did not play by the same rules as everyone else. She may have been playing a different game entirely.
"My sister," Aki said. "We were interrupted earlier, and I came here to find out if you knew anything more."
<You are not a member of the Einhart. Who are you?>
"If you're worried, know that I am not a threat to you. Not now at least. I am Akiko Fushimi, an agent from Aurora. I have a contract with the Einhart to seek out and kill Lady Vijera, thus, I am currently a friend. But the Einhart have information that they're not willing to share with me, information you may know. So I did what I needed to see you." 
<To see me?>
Aki decided to tell Ashra the whole story. "A while ago, Vijera captured my sister, Rin. As a result, the empire has their hands on Auroran technology, tactics, and other secrets. This must be stopped. She's my sister, and it's my duty above anyone else's to subdue her. Know that our enemy is the same, Princess Ashra, and if you help me find her, you will be avenging your mother as well." She spoke with confidence and authority. Most importantly, Aki spoke to Ashra not as a child, but as one as capable as she was.
Ashra didn't know if she could trust her. <Your sister is strong,> she said. <From what I saw in the Empyrean, she has resisted merging a part of her mind with Vijera. So something did not go as planned.>
"While the Aurorans have many sources of information, the Sanctum Empire is the major group we know the least about. What are the details of the merge?"
<I have not done it, but it is a capability that is passed through my father's bloodline. They have tried to keep the information hidden from me, but I explored the minds of others, of visiting dignitaries, of officers and those above them. I pieced together what happens. During a merge, a member of the royal family will go missing, sometimes for years at a time. Their absence is noticed by others.>
"What happens when they're away?"
<They hide themselves somewhere, on some backwater planet or an abandoned husk of a city. There they will consume the parts of the individual that they want and discard the parts they do not need. The physical body of the target is surely absorbed, but more often than not, it's their minds, their knowledge and abilities, that are the true goal of the royal.>
Aki considered this. "Why do they go missing?"
<They are defenseless,> she said. <During the merge they are covered in an organic film. If you cut it open, a mess of body parts would tumble out.> Her nose wrinkled at the thought. <A merge takes time and concentration. The stronger individual wins, dominating until nothing is left of the other person. According to some visitors on the Edict, Vijera was never the same after her merge, so Rin may have beaten Vijera in one way or another. They also mentioned that Seth has been absent from the affairs of the empire, and that he has only recently returned.>
"Yes, he's returned. We met him," she said, remembering the bruises that followed.
<Oh? I haven't seen him myself, but they say he is worthy to rule in Father's place.>
Aki considered Ashra for a moment. "Would you like to rule?" she asked. "As a princess, you're in line to take the throne, aren't you?"
<Being in the line of succession brings with it many threats. I am not only a target of the empire's enemies, but also a threat to fellow members of the royal house. I am weak, with this wretched body that can only hear and feel. I have no voice of my own; no way to affect change. I am not fit to rule; not in the way my father and brother are,> she said.
"I believe you're stronger than you think you are," Aki said. "You've seen the death of your mother, and you've been thrust into an unfamiliar place with unfamiliar people. Yet you are still in one piece." She grabbed the cube that floated in the air beside them. She flipped through scenes of war, watched the empire dominate one battlefield after another, both before and after the formation of the Einhart. "You've seen this?"
<I've seen it all, and I've seen enough,> Ashra said. She stood up and stretched her arms and legs. 
Aki appreciated the Auroran cut of her white dress. It was formalwear, stiff from heavy starching, but it sat well on her small frame. The sleeves were long and almost touched the ground, waving about as she moved. But the cloth sash that held the dress together was lopsided. When Aki spied the back, she noticed it was tied incorrectly. That was the problem with fashion, she thought. Traditional Auroran styles were a la mode, but misappropriated without respect to the source.
"The dress you're wearing is beautiful; it's from my homeworld of Aurora," she said. "However, it seems like the Einhart don't know how to put it together. Allow me to make it proper." She walked over to Ashra, proving that the barrier was no longer active. Aki stood in front of Ashra and waited until the girl nodded her consent. Aki knelt behind her and undid the ugly knot from the back, pulling out a long length of hardened silk that was twice as tall as the princess. The fabric was difficult to work with, but Aki remembered the strong yet graceful strokes required to tease the fabric into the desired shape. Considering how few Aurorans left the homeworld, she wasn't surprised that no one aboard knew how to properly tie it. Aurora was still under its own jurisdiction, and its population had little reason to leave. The influence of the Sanctum Empire or the Einhart was minimal, other than the influx of credits as groups on Aurora were contracted to assassinate members on both sides. If she remembered right, it was an Auroran that failed to assassinate Claudia years ago. Though he was sloppy and careless, she learned from the mistakes of those that failed before her.
"What have you been shown?" Aki asked.
<A side to my family and the empire that I did not know and did not want to know.>
"Is that regret I hear?" Aki took the fabric in both hands. It was stretched out like a river of gold, embroidered with mythical beasts in hues of red and black. She wound it around Ashra's waist, pulled it tight and then wound it around her again.
<No,> Ashra said. <No regret. Too much information is better than too little.> She felt more at ease as Aki helped dress her. It was similar to her mother's touch during the short times they had to visit. The feeling of another woman's hands was both familiar and comforting, but there was also sadness there, lurking deep in a part of her mind she didn't want to explore. Aki was not Lydia, and she wished more than ever her mother were alive to answer the questions she had left unanswered. <I was taught that war was a last resort; that the majority of the worlds that joined us did so out of their own free will.>
"I take no sides in this war. I only go where I'm sent. But from what I've seen, no world gives up its identity, its sense of self, without fighting for it. Violence is the most efficient way to acquire and exert power, but the worst way to keep it." Aki held the separate folds of fabric together with her fingers and pinched them in to make two wings of cloth that unfurled out of Ashra's back.
<From what I have seen, the empire has only ever used violence.> When Aki continued to adjust the bow on her back and gave no response, Ashra knew she was right. <I always had the feeling that my guards and tutors hid much from me. They kept me isolated. They controlled who I saw, what I learned, when I could leave my quarters. Even now, I only go from one prison to another, always of someone else's making.>
Aki fastened the last edge of the belt. "Done. You look like a proper princess now. And if your eyes weren't so big, you'd fit right in on Aurora." The belt had turned into a butterfly bow. The whole dress felt tighter and sat properly on Ashra's shoulders and back. "You are freer than you were a moment ago, so take advantage of it."
Ashra had memorized the layout of her cell and took small steps around its perimeter. She was careful not to step on the guards that were still unconscious on the floor. <I know how much your sister means to you, Ms. Fushimi,> she said. < I wish I could help, but I do not know where Vijera is. The movements of my siblings are kept secret and I was never privy to such information. My best guess is that she would be on Sanctuary, if she hasn't been sent to another world to wreak havoc there.>
"Sanctuary, the throneworld?" Aki asked.
Ashra nodded as she took more confident steps around the room.
"Do you know where Sanctuary is?"
<I do not. I have never been there.>
"You do know that the Einhart will ask you where it is. They'll expect you to know its location." Aki stood up and stretched her legs.
<I know, but I cannot give them an answer when I have none to give.>
"Be prepared for them, princess."
<I'm sorry I could not be of more assistance, especially after you went through the trouble of incapacitating my captors.>
"There is nothing to apologize for. I came here only to check if you knew anything else about my sister. I'm glad I came." She looked at the guards. "They were a good exercise. But unfortunately, they will be waking up soon. The price of non-damaging concussions," she said, a hint of unfulfilled want in her voice.
She went over to Ashra, who only came up to her waist. She put a gentle hand on the child's shoulder and Ashra knew that their time together was over. She calmly headed back to the center of the room.
"Ah, one more thing," Aki said. "This is from me." She pulled out a simple knife made from one piece of metal. Its grip was as thin as the blade, with four round holes for easy wielding. "Careful, don't cut yourself," Aki said. "You may lack the strength to stab, but the blade has been dipped in poison, my own special blend, and drawing blood is enough." She held the knife by the blade and put Ashra's fingers through the grip. Ashra clutched it, holding it close to her heart. Aki took Ashra's other hand and put the sheath into her palm. The princess felt the engraved flowers across the smooth surface. The blade slid in soundlessly.
"A girl should always have a knife," Aki said.
<Thank you,> Ashra said. <But I have nowhere to put it. This dress, beautiful as it is, has no means of concealing anything. The Einhart saw to that.>
Aki put her hand inside the belt and opened up the small pocket she had hidden within the folds of the fabric. Ashra smiled when she felt it and slipped the knife inside.
"And, I was told to give this to you," Aki said. She pulled out a small bundle wrapped in cloth. She placed it in Ashra's hand. Ashra gasped when she felt it. Her fingers ran across the crescent surface, like half a moon, its stylized rays radiating out in thin lines of silver. A blue jewel in the shape of a teardrop was suspended in the center of the half-circle. It was slightly warm when she held it in her palm.
Placing Ashra back into the center of the room, Aki activated the barrier and the air hummed with electricity once again. She was arranging all the guards when she felt a question brush against her mind.
<I thought I lost this when my mother passed. Why did he give it back to me?> Ashra asked.
Aki finished returning the guards back into their original positions. "You should ask him yourself," she said. She quietly slipped out of the doorway and melded with the shadows.
When the guards awoke, they found that they were sore in some areas and had headaches that rivaled the mornings that followed their wildest nights. Tairus moved his mouth and his jaw felt sore. But, the princess was still inside the barrier, and she sat quietly as she always had. When they questioned one another, they realized they didn't know why they had all been unconscious at the same time. No one could remember what they were doing before. They considered filing a report, but when there was nothing to file other than mutual embarrassment, they decided against it and kept it as their own secret. Though, after the event, Tairus would always tense up when Aki was near, and he wouldn't know why.

Chapter 15

It wasn't easy for Seth to fit in. Even among the big and bulky Galeans, he was still a head taller and had to hunch to look the same height. Hunching was something the First Prince did not do well. 
Earlier, the probes had located numerous Galean escape vessels traveling in darkspace. It was easy to board and overtake the smallest one without anyone else noticing. There had been only one occupant; Seth killed him quickly in his sleep. After he broke the man's neck, he pressed a palm against the dead man's face. He mapped out his facial features with his fingers, and Seth's own face changed in response. His lips became slightly wider and his eyes grew rounder. A few days' growth of stubble sprouted across his jaw line and two elongated earlobes completed the look. Though he loathed losing his beauty, he knew he could have it back when he retrieved the princess and brought her to Sanctuary.
 With the transformation complete, Seth launched the deceased Galean out with the rest of the rubbish. He sabotaged the escape craft and sent out a distress signal. Other Galeans, more than happy to save one of their fellow worldmen, picked him up. They said that they were going to the Aurelius, whose coordinates they learned before the attack. The Einhart were there to provide for those with no more homeworld in exchange for work and loyalty. Seth added to the hope these people had. He cheered when they made their promises of revenge against the empire that destroyed them. Secretly, he despised them for their lack of realistic thinking. The empire has swept aside and assimilated civilizations far greater than yours, he thought. We only lost the Edict and it had nothing to do with Galean efforts. Still, he observed everything and learned mannerisms quickly, remembering details with his augmented brain. He would shut down whenever anyone asked too many questions, saying the trauma was too much. They would leave him alone to grieve for family and friends he never lost. Seth was a consummate actor, and by the time he reached the Aurelius, he had picked up their slang and customs, and was treated as one of their own. But after he boarded the flagship, he slipped away and disappeared and no one saw him again. Most forgot about him, for despite his height, nothing else about him had really stood out.
Seth had his contact aboard the Aurelius set him up with a spare room and a fake identity. He then began his search for the princess.

Chapter 16

By the third night, word of Ashra had spread. The leak must've been one of the engineers. Though he hated Simmons, Alan knew that the man would never breach the security of the Einhart in this way and risk his own position as a Second Medium. But blame could be assigned later.
It had started two hours earlier, when the message scrolled across his palm.

Get down there now.
-C

Argus was standing next to him when he read it. He grabbed him and went to the nearest pipe transport. When Alan arrived in the isolation cell, the door to the inner chamber was open. Aki's techniques couldn't have lasted this long, Alan thought. A man ran past them in the other direction, headed for the lift the two had just gotten off of. The man's eyes were wild and fear clung to him as he barreled past them.
Alan took the scene in at a glance. The barrier that imprisoned Ashra was no longer there. One man lay on the floor, his back bent in an unnatural position. Black lines carved their way across his face where his veins should have been, necrotic and full of congealed blood. He was clearly dead, yet spasms still ran through his body out of reflex, exhausting the remaining muscle fibers. It was Aki's poison, but she was up above poring over lab notes. Another man was on the ground, crawling away as fast as he could on his arms; his legs had been engulfed in a white light-
"Ashra!" Alan pushed Argus back and dove out of the way of the quickly expanding white light. She was floating in the air; the red marks remained from where the man had grabbed her, where he held her up and throttled her by the neck. The man was now on the ground, yet still she hung there. Her white hair swam around her; her blank eyes were open as she hovered above him, suspended by an unseen force. The white light expanded and the man cried out in pain. He made a little progress crawling away with two hands. Alan saw that what remained of his legs were two stumps, the shape of the wounds perfectly matching the curve of the seed of light. They bled profusely and he would be losing consciousness soon.
Alan ran two steps toward Ashra. With a push, he jumped and tackled her from the air, hugging her tight to his chest as they both fell. He turned himself in midair so that he landed on his back. The wind was knocked out of him when he hit the ground. He kept a tight grip on Ashra. Small tendrils of light started snaking out of the bottom of the white sphere, one of them piercing through the chest of the man crawling backward. He died in an instant, his head lolling to the side. Anything the light touched simply ceased to be. The floor was disappearing as Alan pushed backward with Ashra in his arms.
She stared blankly ahead. "Ashra, wake up!" he said. He scooted back with his feet as the orb expanded. "You don't need to do this." His back slammed against the wall. He stroked her hair and held her close. He didn't know what would happen when the light touched her, but he was pretty sure what had happened to the others would happen to him. "Ashra, you're safe now," he whispered. He put two fingers to her forehead, as she had done to him earlier, and repeated the phrase in his mind. You're safe. I'm here, you're safe.
He wanted to curl his legs up away from the light, but he kept them outstretched to protect Ashra, as if to block its progress with his foot. The light touched the bottom of his boot. There was no heat, but he could feel his foot getting lighter as the sole of his boot was removed layer by layer.
Ashra's head shook once, as if she had woken up from a dream. The shock of seeing the light seed in front of her jolted her awake. In response, the ball of light pulsed and expanded. Alan winced in pain as the light ate through his boot and the bottom of his foot.
Ashra came to her senses. She pressed her hands together and the light shrank. It receded and collapsed into itself until it was nothing more than a small dot. With a flash, the dot burst into motes of light, almost like dust, then disappeared. The light seed left a crater in the ground, revealing the circuitry that ran underneath the floors. Sparks flew between exposed wires.
Argus came in and jumped around the hole to get to them. Alan stayed with Ashra on the floor. He fought the pain as he moved his leg. The bottom of his right foot felt like it was on fire. It left a trail of blood wherever he dragged it. "Ashra, what happened?" he whispered.
She breathed and collected her thoughts. <The guards left and three men came in. They deactivated the barrier and brought me out.> She was shaken up. Alan saw the red handprints on her face and guessed the rest.
<They said, 'bring them back.' They told me to give them back their homeworlds, their families, but I didn't know where they were from. Why did they think I could?> She turned to Alan. <I looked into their minds. They had so much pain. Honest pain, the kind that stays rooted in the soul and is impossible to forget. I managed to paralyze one with the knife Aki gave me, but when the other grabbed me?> she trailed off and tears formed around her eyes. <I didn't want to start anything; I wanted to be a good girl. But I couldn't breathe.> She dragged her hand up to her neck.
"It's okay," Alan said. "You're safe now."
<I?I know.> He felt her shake in his arms. It started as small tremors that brushed her hair against his face. Her breathing was rapid and shallow. He hugged her tight as tears fell onto his shoulder. <I know,> she repeated.
"I shouldn't have brought you here."
In between breaths she said, <I'm glad you did.>
Though he wanted to rest here with Ashra for another minute, for another hour, he knew that their time was short. One of the assailants had escaped. The man would go into the hub to tell everyone what had happened. They would be back soon.
Argus stood above them. Alan took the hand he offered and lifted Ashra up with his other arm. He tried putting weight on his foot. Though he hobbled, he could still take a few small steps forward.
He looked at Argus. "Take her to my quarters and lock the doors. Arm yourself, and don't come out until I tell you to." He gently let Ashra down and Argus took her hand.
"What are you going to do?" Argus asked.
"Prevent the inevitable," Alan said.

***

That was two hours ago. In that time, his foot was healed in the med bay, he received a new pair of boots, and an emergency session of the Zodiac Council had been held. Claudia appeared to him as a hologram; her corporeal form was integrated with the ship as she conferenced with other council members across the stars.
"What do you mean, interrogated?!" Alan fumed.
They were inside the High Adjudicant's chamber above the bridge, where she oversaw all of the Aurelius, but none could see or hear her. She stepped back from the window, her toga drifting and flowing with her movements as if it were real. She viewed herself as a goddess of wisdom, but Alan always thought a goddess of war was more appropriate. Her identity of self was fundamental to the image that floated before him. It wasn't too different than what she really looked like, except perhaps softer and more rounded at the edges. Her words were still just as sharp. 
"I may lend my name and the vast majority of my resources to the Einhart, but I am still bound by the rules of the Zodiac Council," she said. "That is the thin line that separates us from the Sanctum Empire, Alan," she explained.
"But interrogation! It's too much; she didn't start it. They came to her and she acted out of self-defense. She's only a child."
"I also believe that she is of more use to us alive. She may lead us to more information. And though I can see she's only a child, the other members of the council cannot. Ashra has clearly demonstrated her capabilities as a weapon, and now we know why the empire wants her. She has killed two of our men aboard the Aurelius. You know as well as I do she will be hated by everyone when word spreads, if it hasn't already. The people are seeking blood and the council has decided to give it to them. We know of no way to harness her powers without inviting destruction upon ourselves, so interrogation was their only remaining option. It was not a unanimous vote, but it was the majority, and so it is their suggestion that shall be executed."
"Executed," Alan scoffed. "Poor choice of words, Claudia. You know what they do at interrogations. You know that they will torture her until she can sustain no more, then they will parade her through the hub, where those that are gathered, and for her there will be many, will pelt her with abuse and filth, and then she will be publicly executed to the cheers of the crowd."
"You don't need to explain to me what happens in the hub," Claudia said. Her voice was calm but there was an icy bite to her words. "I helped establish the rules. Interrogations have been the best means of extracting information. It is the threat of violence, not the actual act of, that has gotten us the knowledge we have sought in the past."
"But she doesn't have it. She doesn't have the knowledge. She doesn't know where Sanctuary is. I've asked; others have asked. I believe her. She has told us all she knows." Alan sat down on a chair facing the desk and let out a sigh. "Is there any way you can stop this?" he asked.
"There are things that are out of even my power. I cannot pardon the crimes of another."
"She has committed no crime, other than being born to the wrong family. To the wrong side."
"And that is why the Zodiac Council was so adamant in pushing their agenda. We have a princess, a member of the royal family. After Galea, her public torture and death would bring a greatly needed morale boost. It would show all of the Einhart that we have the ability to destroy not only their soldiers, but their leaders, their most precious royals as well. They don't care that she's a little girl; they care that she's a Sanctum princess."
Alan dismissed her arguments with a wave of his hand. "Sometimes I wonder why I'm fighting," he said. "Why can't they realize that she's flesh and blood? Just like everyone else here?"
"You're in no position to say that," Claudia said. Her hologram sat on the desk. "You have killed countless Sanctum soldiers with no remorse. You were, and are, driven by revenge, and it has not been so long for many of those here."
Alan was silent. He had no response because she was correct. He put his head in his hands. "When's it going to happen?" he asked, his voice muffled by his palms.
"The council has just adjourned and the secretary will be inputting the commands. It should take no more than ten minutes for the guards to retrieve her from her cell."
"Her cell? I told you she's not?"
"I know and you know. The council doesn't." She hopped off the edge of the table, and Alan could've sworn he saw a spring in her step. "The favor you called in should be done by now. You'll find it at the end of dock 6-S."
Alan didn't know how she knew, but she was, after all, the High Adjudicant. He was already out the door before Claudia's image winked out of existence.
His feet pounded down the carpeted hallway that led to one of the lifts between the bridge and the rest of the ship. He entered, scanned his palm, and confirmed the location of his apartment. When the lift started to move, he brought up the schematics of the Aurelius, noting that dock 6-S was in a relatively unpopulated area, next to the munitions depot. But it was still far away. He opened a channel to Argus.
"Argus, is she still there?"
A moment of static, followed by, "Yes boss, she's fine."
"Get her dressed in civilian clothing, and you too. Find something in my closet that fits you and get a gun. Also, there's a drawer with a lock on it. Break it and find a small marble. It should be black; looks like it's made of glass."
He heard Argus rummaging through his stuff in his messy quarters. "I can't find anything here. Your room is as cluttered as your mind," Argus said, and Alan wished he had cleaned up earlier. "What is this, some new breed of vegetable?" Argus asked. Alan heard gagging and the sound of the package being resealed. "Not new. Rather old," Argus said in between gulps of air. Alan thought back; it might've been the cuzich, the long, green vegetable undoubtedly covered in a layer of fuzzy mold. Alan had left it on his desk before leaving for Galea.
"Just look for it," Alan said. "Take care of Ashra first. I'll tell Aki to meet us. Alan out."
When the lift arrived, it took every fiber of Alan's self-control to not run. Not wanting to raise suspicion, he walked quickly and silently in case anyone else happened to be there.
He opened the door and found Argus. The big man wore khaki shorts and an ill-fitting t-shirt that was ripped near the biceps when he put his arm through it. Ashra was covered in a cloak. "She wouldn't take the dress off," Argus said. "Said that there were things she needed to keep safe." 
Alan nodded his understanding. "Did you find the marble?" he asked.
Argus shook his head. Alan pushed past him. The lock on the cabinet was broken without tools; the doors were pried open with sheer force and Alan marveled at Argus's strength. Alan dug through the cabinet and threw weapon parts and unopened bullet boxes to the ground. "Damn it," he said when he couldn't find it. With his hands on his hips, he looked around his small apartment for an object he knew he had.
"Boss, our time is short. Is this truly necessary?" Argus asked.
Alan dismissed his question with a wave of his hand. He opened up a closet and looked at the top shelf.
"Aha! Here it is." He reached inside a drawer. When he turned to face them, he held a black bead between his fingers and made Ashra feel it. "This will constantly transmit your position to me. If you need us, smash it on the ground and I'll see where you were last. These normally come in pairs, but," he looked back inside the drawer, "I only have one."
Alan knelt down and tucked it into the complex belt Aki made earlier.
<Thank you,> she said. She had never heard of anything like it before.
Alan nodded and the three went to the lift.

***

"My Lord First Prince, her escape pod is not where it used to be."
Seth, Voice of the Empire, sat huddled against a wall, wearing the rags that made him look like any of the other refugees that sought shelter. No one took a second glance at the lonely man with his head between his legs.
"Where is it, then?" he whispered.
"An authority higher than myself has blocked anyone from accessing its location. It must be Claudia." His informant's voice was intelligible but garbled, scrambled across a thousand relays before it reached him.
"I didn't come here to sightsee," Seth said. "Tell me where Ashra is."
"My apologies My Lord, for I do not know. But there may be a way to find her. There was a spike in delta waves below in the isolation chambers. The ship has been detecting faint traces of those waves with the new sensors that were recently installed."
"Enough talk. Show me."
A map of the ship scrolled across his eyes. A hazy mist of red could be seen where the ship recorded the delta waves. They were concentrated heavily in the bottom of the Aurelius. But there, along one of the pipe lift routes, a red dot moved down.
Seth got up and disappeared into the dark alley he had been sitting in. He left the rags he wore on the ground.

***

Aki met the trio when their lift arrived. She replaced her tight suit with loose-fitting clothes, but underneath it, Alan could see the outline of pouches and guns. He had rarely seen her in anything outside of her uniform, but she moved with grace and seemed comfortable in whatever she wore.
"This way," she said. Going through a densely populated area wasn't the best route, but it was the shortest, and they didn't have time. The munitions depot was still another floor below them, but due to safety issues the transport lifts didn't go there. The escape bay was still further beyond that, but first they had to get through the hub.
Surrounded by the three biospheres, the hub acted as the civilian center of the ship. When they entered, Ashra almost slipped on the grime. The walls were wet from condensation coming from the pipes that ran across the ceilings high above them. Inside the hub it was always night. Tiny storefronts with neon signs as large as their entrances sold all manner of strange things collected from different worlds. The goods that came into the Aurelius were highly regulated by officials, but with enough credits and the right connections, one could get almost anything.
Aki led the way, watching for anyone with too much curiosity. She wove through the crowd like a fish through water; a deft turn of her shoulder or a gentle push deflected the traffic that came her way. But there were many people heading in every direction, and she had to slow down and wait as some of them bumped into Alan, who was encumbered by a small girl wearing a hood that covered her face.
Relentless vendors held up trinkets along with the dried husks of animals and plants. One said to Aki, "A new necklace for the pretty lady? Finest ore from Batten!" She waved him aside and continued forward. Some would whistle after her, saying lewd but flattering things. She ignored them as well.
Ashra had never been to a marketplace like this one before. She heard vendors hawking fresh fruits and fried pastries. There were the scents of cooking, sweat, and the bitter smell of spirits mixed with an undercurrent of sewage and rot. It was a fascinating experience; far removed from the sterile halls she was raised in. She wished she could've stayed longer, if she were someone else. Someone who could appreciate the sights with her own eyes and converse in the dialects of different cultures with her own tongue.
Though the crowd bumped into Alan and paid no attention to the girl, they parted as Argus made his way through. Argus could recognize the other Galeans by their height as they stood out from the crowd; there were maybe one or two. He yearned to talk to them, to ask if anyone else made it out, but he had a job to do.
The stench of rot became stronger as they wound their way through the hub. They emerged off to the side of a round pavilion, where a young man was stripped naked and steeped in his own waste, locked behind a cage of light, similar to the light that had held Ashra just hours ago. He silently endured as cuffs cut into his wrists and chains held him suspended from two tall posts. His feet barely touched the ground. Even if he wanted to cry out, he would have had trouble through the blue gag stuffed into his mouth, the color denoting his Sanctum affiliation. His interrogation had ended a couple days ago and not much of the crowd remained, but there were individuals that would stand outside his cage and pelt him with words and humiliation for lack of anything better to do. Street urchins would dare each other to get as close as they could to the cage. They would almost reach him before he snapped at them with a turn of his head and unfulfilled violence in his eyes. But he was losing energy, having been without water and food ever since he was strung up, and the most he could muster was a strained bobbing of his head. High above him was a holographic sign that rotated in the air. "Sanctum." There was no name, no accusation. Once he had been labeled as the enemy, as the other, he was no longer human. He may have been a spy, or he may have been a simple soldier captured from the last battle. It did not matter to the public, who only wanted something to keep their hate strong.
"Barbaric," Argus muttered under his breath.
Ashra took notice. She had been diving in and out of people's minds for short periods of time, gleaning what colors and sights she could without being detected. She looked through Argus's eyes and saw the scene he saw. She had felt the man's presence once before, on the Edict. She recalled him being sent as a spy, because of how innocent and young he looked. But friend or foe, no one deserved such a fate. She said a silent prayer for him, hoping his torment would end quickly.
The hologram above the man changed and Argus looked again. All he needed to see was an image of Ashra's face, the Sanctum emblem, a series of numbers, and a credit sign after it to know what it meant. "That's a rather large ransom isn't it?" he said.
Alan looked up. "Damn. That was less than ten minutes."
"The one time your government is efficient," Aki said.
They maintained their speed, hesitant to call attention to themselves. They stuck to the edges, away from the center of the hub and the largest crowds. But after Aki ignored one vendor who was trying to push on her some ridiculous hat that was supposed to be the latest fashion, the woman didn't waste any time. She turned to Ashra and kneeled, offering her the same item. "Little girl, this hat is much prettier than a cloak," she said. Before Alan could stop her, she pulled off the hood that covered Ashra's face. She saw the princess's face and the woman knew. With the reward the Zodiac Council was offering, she and her stolen goods would never need to return to the streets. She made a vicious grab for Ashra but fell to the ground when Alan's fist collided with her head.
"Move!" he said. Aki stepped aside and Argus came forward. The big man started with long steps, pushing people out of his path as gently as he could. The steps gradually turned into great strides that were felt as tremors through the ground. Though he was not a sprinter, Argus's height and thick legs gave him speed and force to use. He gave people one warning to move out of his way before he trampled over them. He hoped that they would think it was some kind of emergency, and not that they had the Sanctum princess with them. But as he pushed and tossed aside those that wouldn't get out of his way, he caught some glances behind him that worried him.
Ashra had already stumbled once, so Alan scooped her up in his arm. She was light, almost too light, and he wished that he had asked Aki to also smuggle some food in for her. She wasn't malnourished, but she weighed so little in his arms. He was afraid Argus's wake would blow her away.
Aki brought up the back, running with one hand held near her waist, ready to fend off anyone too curious or greedy. She had hidden needles inside the jade bracelet on her wrist, and she now took them out and held a needle in between each of her fingers. Whenever she saw a suspicious face or heard a knowing gasp, she threw one of them at the offender. They would scrunch their faces up in pain before feeling a million insects crawl upon their skin as the toxin entered their bloodstream and caused them to hallucinate. Most were too busy getting out of the way of the giant hurtling towards them to notice the people who followed behind him, but Aki was running out of needles.
Argus looked back without breaking stride. "How much longer?" he asked.
Alan checked the map. "Make a right at the next alley. We can cut down the stairs to the munitions depot."
They had to cover a long strip of ground. Aki risked a glace back. A sizable mob had built up behind them, chanting for Ashra. The mob wasn't fast but Alan was hampered by the princess and their going was slow. The howling of the crowd grew. He heard an undertone of anger, overshadowed by zealous avarice.
As the men leading the mob gained on them, Aki pulled out a small sachet and threw it behind her. The pressurized smoke erupted and a hazy darkness covered the area, temporarily slowing the crowd down, but she knew it wouldn't keep them away for long.
Argus almost overshot the corner. Alan put Ashra down and reached out a hand to stop him. When Alan grabbed Argus's arm, his own was almost torn from its socket by the large man's momentum. "Here!" Alan cried out. 
Argus looked right at the last moment. Without stopping, he pivoted on one foot and threw his weight and momentum into a locked door. It crumpled beneath his shoulder, flew off its hinges and embedded itself into the concrete wall of the staircase. The crash had stopped his charge, and he ushered the three of them past him. The staircase was narrow and they had to go down one after the other. After they were through, he stayed behind. "I'll take care of them here!" he said. He watched as motion-detecting lights turned on as the others went down and vanished from sight.
He turned around. The doorway was narrow and he blocked most of it with his bulk alone. The people that chased them were closing the gap quickly. Argus could hear the bloodlust in their cries. He looked around for any weapons, but all he saw were metal carts filled with food, abandoned by their owners when they saw Argus approaching. He grabbed one in each hand as if they were as light as empty baskets and pulled them to the staircase entrance. He held one by its handle at his side. A man wearing clothes too fashionable for his age came into view, leading an angry mob of around thirty people behind him. Argus grabbed the cart handle with both hands and spun on one foot, using the cart as a counterbalance. He spun four times, gaining more speed with each revolution. He aimed low. With a final glimpse at his target, he let the cart fly. Like a food-laden missile, it skimmed the surface of the ground before colliding with the man. The cart broke a few ribs as it impacted, sending him and those behind him flying backwards. They landed on the floor and didn't get up.
Argus watched the cart go. A blur leapt over the cart, jumping an impossible distance towards him. Argus wouldn't have noticed it if not for how the light seemed to bend around its form, like heat waves that distorted the air. It was well camouflaged, but it looked like the shape of a man, a man that seemed familiar to him.
Argus brought out his gun and fired two shots at the figure that flew overhead. One went wide and ricocheted off the ceiling. The other hit its mark as the figure twisted in midair. A trail of blood appeared next to Argus. But the figure continued on its trajectory and landed inside the staircase. With its invisibility destroyed by his bullet, Argus saw a man covered in a tight black suit. The man disappeared down the stairs.
Argus accessed his com. "One got through. Look out behind you," he said.
"Just one?" Alan asked. He was panting on the other end. 
"Yes."
There was the pattering of running feet. "Almost at the escape pod. Rendezvous below," Alan said.
"Understood. Argus out." Now all he had to do was deal with the remainder of the mob. He aimed his gun at the ceiling, brandishing it as a warning. 
The crowd stopped in front of him. One by one, they each pulled out their own weapons. Some were plasma-based from Sanctum, while others were types Argus had never seen before. All were aimed at him. He hung his head and let out a long sigh. Life was never easy. He grabbed the remaining cart and held it up as a shield as they opened fire. It was peppered with ammunition from different worlds and began leaking a fragrant sauce. With the cart in front of him, he took two steps backwards down the staircase behind him. Not giving the crowd time to catch up, he pulled on the door he had slammed into the concrete earlier. After a couple of hard wrenches it came free, loosening chunks of cement that fell around him. He smashed it back into its frame and wedged the cart between the narrow walls, ramming the cart with his weight to make sure there was no space between it and the door. Furious but futile pounding came from the other side. He made his way down the stairs, his broad shoulders brushing against the walls.

Chapter 17

The munitions depot was a long hallway filled with unused ordnance. Weapons were stacked in shelves, some rows reaching so high that Alan couldn't see the tops of them. Some of it was held in crates and organized by shell size. Unused missiles lay in neat rows, waiting to be loaded into launch tubes. Judging by the layer of dust on the floors and weapons, very few people came down here; probably the reason why Claudia chose this isolated portion of the ship, he thought.
Alan heard it before he saw it. Above the stacked towers of weapons was the silhouette of a man. The man leapt from stack to stack, pushing off the walls and landing gracefully on the tops of the boxes. Beads of blood fell to the ground as he moved, leaving crimson drops that splattered around them. Alan barely pulled Ashra aside when the figure came crashing down, its outstretched arms aimed for the princess. Alan took two steps backward and the man's hands closed on air. The man stood up from his crouched position to his full height, easily two heads taller than Alan.
Aki was ahead of them. She stopped, turned around and threw her remaining needle at the open wound on the man's chest. Alan and Ashra ran past her.
"Petty tricks," the man said. Though his face was different, Alan recognized the voice, the Voice of the Empire, and he knew it was Seth. Next to him, Ashra finally knew who the blue perpetual in her Empyrean was. She was pulled along as Alan made his way deeper into the depot. Alan hated leaving Aki behind, but he had no time to consider other options.
Seth raced forward, but Aki held her own against him. After being knocked against the temple wall in Galea, she knew his tactics better. She dodged one fist after another, always trying to pull out one of the weapons she had hidden on her. But Seth gave her no chance to do so. One stray step and one of his massive fists or feet would take her out of the fight. There was no room for error, no room to be sloppy. 
She danced between the rows of crates, using each one to conceal her movements as she jumped between one stack and the next. Seth was not so graceful and smashed them to pieces as she ducked and twirled. The crates spilled unfired rounds and torn pieces of plastic around her. She relied on her fast kicks to keep his attention, to prevent him from going after Ashra, but she knew it was only a matter of time before she ran out of boxes to hide behind. The escape bay was hidden behind this maze of organized armaments; she only hoped Alan would have enough time to reach it.
It was this stray thought that caused her to lose track of Seth's knee. As she jumped back to avoid Seth's grab, he pushed himself off the ground and his knee connected with Aki's solar plexus. Blood escaped her lips as she smashed into two towers of crates. She slid across the floor with her remaining momentum and blacked out. Seth didn't bother to finish her off; he ran past the few remaining boxes to catch up to Alan and Ashra. 
Ashra struggled to keep up with Alan's pace. They went past rows and rows of similar shelves, but all Ashra could see was the yellow light in front of her, holding her and guiding her. Behind her was the blue light, ever closer, its pull ever stronger.
Alan was glad to see that there was no door that separated the escape bay from the weapons depository. The corner of the room dead-ended into a small alcove that held only three small ships. Two were easily identifiable as belonging to the Einhart. These were oblong and dull gray; escape vessels that could take many at once. Connected to the wall furthest away from them was Ashra's pod. Behind the raised door, Alan could see the red form-fitting cushions and navigation panel were still intact. 
"I don't know what your mother was planning," Alan said, "but I hope it's safe where you were going." He prayed the miniature darkspace drive inside it was still functional. They were about to enter the bay when Seth caught up with them. He leapt forward and landed in front of Alan, blocking their path. Alan quickly retreated a few steps, keeping Ashra behind him. He kept his hand on Ashra and his eyes on Seth, watching as the prince rose to his full height. As Seth focused on the princess, his face began to change shape. The lines and wrinkles around his eyes and mouth disappeared, the crags and valleys rising and filling out until all that remained was smooth alabaster. His skin was once again flawless. His eyes were filled with the same malice and cunning Alan had seen earlier.
Seth looked at Ashra and spoke to her. "Come back, Ashra, Princess of the Void." His intoxicating voice filled the air and Ashra's ears. "Your place is with the empire, among the royals. Now that you are of age, you belong in Sanctuary, to rule over it and all the other worlds along with us, your family. It is your duty to your father the emperor and all the peoples that shall bow to you. Come back to us." He held out a hand. He would've turned that hand into a fist through Alan's gut if he could, but he didn't know what Alan would to the princess. Seth needed her alive and safe. That meant he had to charm her.
"Don't listen to him," Alan said. 
Seth ignored him. "You will always be an enemy here, always hunted," he said. "You have already seen how they treat you and the other Sanctum. Come back to your family, Ashra. Your mother was a fool to leave us; she didn't know what her actions would do to her daughter. Look at what happened. You, prisoner to our greatest foe!" He stretched his hand out further, waiting for her to take it. "Come back to where you belong."
She stepped out from behind Alan, her face unreadable. <You are my brother?> she asked, broadcasting her thoughts so that both Seth and Alan could hear her.
"I am Seth, the First Prince, Voice of the Empire. You are my sister."
She gravitated towards Seth, pulling harder now, stretching Alan's arm out. Alan was stuck. He couldn't run past Seth with Ashra in his arms. The only reason he was still alive was because of the distance they had from the prince. Once Seth could step in between them and remove Ashra, his advantage, and his life, was lost. "Straight behind you," he whispered to her.
She wiggled her fingers in his palm. He didn't know if she understood, but all he could do was trust. He let her go.
She ran forward. Alan was faster. He launched past Ashra and crashed into Seth with his shoulder, knocking himself and the prince off balance. Though Ashra was tempted by Seth's words, she didn't stop. She ran straight past them. 
Alan and Seth wrestled on the floor. Seth quickly gained the upper hand, pinning Alan to the ground and leaving bruises on his shoulder. From his position on the ground, Alan heard someone coming. He turned his head and caught a glimpse of Argus dragging something large and metal behind him, making sparks fly from the ground. With his last spurt of energy, Alan kicked Seth off of him and rolled away. 
Argus came up, flexed his shoulders and swung the missile in a large arc. The side of the missile cone crashed into Seth's torso. Alan saw it connect as if time had slowed. Seth's ribs compressed slightly to absorb the impact. In the next moment the prince was gone, leaving a trail of broken boxes and scattered ammunition in his wake.
Alan rolled onto his stomach. Simple commands ran through his mind. Hands down, push up, pump legs. The royals never stayed down for long. He rushed to Ashra's side, grabbed her hand, tiny in his, and guided her towards the escape pod. 
"You are your father's daughter, but you are your own person as well, Ashra," Alan said. "Your family doesn't burden you anymore." He checked the systems on the escape pod. "Live your life and be happy," he said. "That's the only thing a dad should wish for his kid."
He picked her up and placed her on the cushions. They began to puff up around her.
Ashra hesitated. In the last three days she had come to enjoy the presence of this man very much. She steeled her courage and reached out to him while she still could, this pale yellow light that had always been close to her in the Empyrean. She didn't know why she did it, and she didn't know what it would do, but she leaned over and kissed him on the forehead.
Alan was concentrating on the diagnostics when he felt a tingle travel from between his eyebrows and spread along his skin, as if an electric current had run down his body and ended at the tips of his toes. With a shake of his arm, Alan shook it off and regained his footing. "Be safe," he said. He input the final command. The door sealed and the escape pod launched, shaking the small bay with the force of its departure.
He opened a line to the High Adjudicant.
"Claudia, can you hide Ashra's ship from our sensors?"
"I don't know what ship you're talking about," Claudia said. He smiled, knowing Ashra would be safe.
Alan heard gunshots and knew he didn't have much time. Argus fired off round after round. Seth, now unhampered by the throng of people, sidestepped each one with ease and blew past the large man without even bothering to disarm him. Alan remained in the bay, pistol drawn and ready. It only took a moment for Seth to register Alan's smug look to know that Ashra was already gone. He dodged each of Alan's bullets, dove into one of the escape vessels and launched it. A second later, Seth's own ship, which had been waiting in darkspace, reentered normal space next to the Aurelius. Alan glared at it, but a part of him was impressed by the precision shift.
It looked to be a modified cruiser, designed with a focus on stealth and speed, which would explain how it evaded the Aurelius's sensors. The escape vessel had disappeared inside of the cruiser. Normal space engines located in its rear were changing configuration, glowing white and blue as they prepared to pursue Ashra. 
"Seth's ship is located right outside the bay," Alan said.
"Seth? The prince?" Claudia asked. Even she sounded a little surprised.
"Yes. He was here to collect Ashra. You better hurry if you want to catch it."
Claudia, still connected to the ship, relayed the message and coordinates to Simmons, who currently stood as the right helmsman. 
"Destroy the ship!" Simmons commanded. "Without the First Prince the empire will be leaderless."
Trace his ship, Claudia corrected privately, the words scrolling across his palm from his wristband.
"Belay that order," he said. "Launch the tracers. If we can find where Sanctuary is we can end this war."
Like a swarm of insects, a group of small spearheads shot into space, designed to burrow into hull plating with their sharp tips. Each was equipped with a long distance transmitter. They boosted forward on their single-burst engines.
Seth's ship had only started to pick up speed when the tracers shot after him. He released a series of small toroid mines behind him. The donut-shaped mines arranged themselves into a defensive matrix in the wake of his engines. One of the tracers came close and a mine detonated. It wasn't a concussive blast, but rather an electromagnetic pulse that stopped a whole swath of the tracers dead in its tracks, turning them into nothing more than floating pieces of metal.
Seth still had to maneuver to outrace the rest. By the time the last of them clunked uselessly against the ship's shield, Ashra's pod had already disappeared. He cursed and pounded the console, leaving two fist-shaped indentations in the steel. The only thing left was to report back to his father when the emperor emerged. He shifted into darkspace.

Chapter 18

"All the surveillance cameras in the munitions depot were offline," Claudia said. "Though, that was by my order." She was drying off with a towel when Alan went to see her. She was immaculate in her green suit, but her long blonde hair was still wet, flowing past the seat of the chair she sat in.
"Seth must be very good at infiltration," Alan said. He took the seat across from her.
"Yes, he must be. Still, to think Seth got aboard this ship. As a refugee no less." She looked up at him. "It points out many flaws we have in our security."
"The Einhart has always taken on refugees in their time of need."
She ignored him. "And how did Seth know where to find her? That bothers me the most. We have always had traitors in our midst, but this one ranks higher than I feared." She turned to him. "So Ashra is gone, yes?"
"She won't be coming back."
"I would've liked to have known more about a weapon such as her, but we learned a lot from her short time here. In case we ever encounter the princess or something like her ever again, Dr. Guren is working on ways to counter her abilities. We also have the technology from the Edict to help us out." A thought crossed her mind. "Speaking of technology?" She pulled up a schematic of Ashra's escape pod, and maneuvered it so that it floated beside her. For a moment, Alan was afraid Claudia still knew where Ashra was, but then she said, "Before she left with the escape pod, Guren managed to find out more about its darkspace drive." Alan's mind relaxed.
It zoomed in onto the spherical fullerene and the darkness it enclosed inside of itself. This darkspace drive was similar to what the Umbra had, but it was simpler and smaller. Its lines were cleaner, removing the bulky excesses that were required for stabilizing the core and instead replacing it with geometric shielding. It relied on energy rather than physical materials. 
"It's still functional like this?" Alan asked, rotating the image.
"Yes. And since it lacks the clutter, far more accurate jumps can be made. At least that's what the prototype has demonstrated. We modified two existing engines with these specifications and installed one on the Umbra. I thought it would be useful, considering the nature of your missions. Think of it as a gift."
"Thanks. I'm sure we'll put it to good use." Alan traced its lines with his finger. "Who made it?"
"Very few people have the skills and knowledge to do this," Claudia said. The image of the darkspace engine was replaced by the projection a planet, rough and craggy. A storm raged on its surface. Alan wondered how she did it without any gestures or visible commands. Perhaps Claudia was still connected with the ship somehow even after she left the integration chamber.
"We have always had ties with the empire, whether we wanted to or not," she said. "Abyssinia is technically a Sanctum holding. But some of their researchers are sympathetic to our cause, and their wallets are sympathetic to our credits. Regardless, Abyssinia is one of the forefront worlds for scientific research. Research we need."
"Sanctum has gone lax, or they're spread too thin to control their territories," Alan said.
"I'm surprised it's taken the empire as long as it had to rein them in. The emperor must be in cocoon after taking the Erudite, leaving Seth to do as he pleases."
"I think that's the case," Alan said. "Should Seth take the throne, we'd have a larger problem on our hands than we do already." He turned back to the projection of the planet. "What have you heard from Abyssinia?"
"Nothing," Claudia said. "And that's the problem. They've gone silent, and our negotiations with them concerning their new light-based weapons have gone cold."
Alan knew what was coming. "My mission?" he asked.
"Find out what happened," Claudia said. "Though we may have lost a resource, every setback hides an opportunity. We relied on peaceful commerce to get what we wanted before, but if there's something amiss on their research station, we have the chance to obtain things that credits can't buy."
Alan considered the ethical implications but let them slide. This was war and Claudia always had her reasons. He was there to follow orders. He popped another Virifen into his mouth, but had trouble swallowing it. They had started tasting bitterer recently.
"It's a good thing that they're under Sanctum rule," she said. "If there is even the remote chance we can locate Sanctuary, the throneworld, we can finally bring this war to them, rather than wait for the next territory to fall," she said. Alan nodded.
 "You will be given a platoon consisting of light infantry along with a technologist," she continued. "We cannot be perceived as a threat or we risk losing what information they do have. You are reconnaissance, and you will be offering assistance on behalf of the Einhart. Officially, Sylvan Winters will be leading this excursion, but you will have ultimate command as Second Medium. He, along with the rest of the crew, have been briefed on this point. 
The image of a man with thinning white hair appeared. "Our contact has always been Dr. Ballard; find him and find out what happened. His last transmission, a few hours ago, put his location here." She added the marker to his map of the planet. "People are cooperative when their lives are at stake, and he should be no different. Let Sylvan do the talking. You are my left hand, and will remain in the shadows until necessary."
She slid forward a clear tube containing a small metal spike that was held aloft by a magnetic field. The surface of the spike was shaped like a smooth cone. It was covered in small holes, and underneath it, Alan could see bundles of tiny cables within the spike.
"Your data mine. The largest one we've ever made, so take care of it. There are some new modifications, including an EMP once it's finished to clear your tracks. You can read the manual during transit."
Alan took it and slid it into his pocket. "You're expecting a lot of data. We'll be lucky if we find enough to fill half of it."
"One never knows, but we are not in the business of luck. We make our luck," she said. She stood up. Alan quickly followed, his arm automatically snapping into a salute. 
"May the Fates watch over you," she said.

Chapter 19

Alan rested on his bed. It was no more than a hunk of metal riveted to the wall of the Umbra with form-fitting gel cushioning thrown on top of it. Still, he had slept on worse and had no trouble falling asleep, especially after the energy he expended making sure Ashra escaped. With their upcoming mission, he knew rest and sleep were just as important as a good firearm.
Though the princess was gone, he saw her in his dream. In the final moments before sleep overtook him, the last thing he remembered was the sensation of falling. He expected a spasm to shake him awake, but none came.
When he opened his eyes, there was no light. He was floating, but whether he was facing up or down he could not tell; there were no stars to guide him nor ground to stand on. But when he looked at himself, he could see a pair of hands resting on his chest. He moved them and noticed they were his own. They were lit from within, as if the light from a moon was captured and released inside his body, shaded with a pale yellow.
As soon as he thought about Ashra, a figure appeared kneeling on top of the darkness in front of him. The figure grew brighter, and a hill sprouted from under its knees, teeming with fresh grass until it reached a sandy dune that encircled an island. That was followed by water, cool and clear, stretching as far as he could see. His feet had found purchase on the edge of the island, his boots making indents in the sand.
The figure stood up. It was Ashra, but different. Her eyes, complete with pupils and irises, twinkled with sense and seeing. She spoke in a voice that rang clear, fitting of the child it belonged to. It had substance and echoed around them instead of just in his mind.
"Alan? What are you doing here?" she asked. There was confusion in her eyes, but no fear. "I never knew anyone could visit me here."
"I?I don't know," he responded. "I was falling asleep. Falling?and then you appeared." He looked around. "Am I dreaming? Is this real? You look real." He knelt down and felt the sand, letting it run through his fingers. "It feels real."
"I think you are dreaming," Ashra said. "But that doesn't mean it's not real." She stood up in the Auroran dress Alan had sent her off in. "This is where I live. Where I spend my time," she said. She gestured to the night sky above them. "I call it the Empyrean." Alan could make out the edges of the island on the other side, faint in the darkness. Flower petals, fragrant, soft, and pink, fell down on them from above. Alan looked up and saw that a tree grew from the center of the island, its trunk gnarled and twisted. He came close to Ashra, brushing past her as he reached out to touch the tree. She was substantial and alive, as real as could be. The tree's bark felt rough under his hands.
"This tree has always been here," she said. "It was once just a sprout, but it has grown as I have grown."
"It's beautiful," he said. With one look he knew it was the same tree that sprouted on Galea. He guessed that its seed was the same shape as the one that appeared in Ashra's cell on the Aurelius. But here it was not made of light; its bark was brown and its light pink flowers gave off the faintest perfume.
She nodded in agreement. "You may enjoy it more if you were more comfortable," she said. She pointed to his feet and pockets, still bulging with equipment.
Alan looked down at his boots, still slowly sinking into the sand. He tried to remember the last time he walked somewhere without purpose, and he couldn't remember when that was. Yet while he was here, he didn't want to wear these boots. As the thought formed in his head, his boots disappeared and his bare feet replaced them. The sand was warm and the granules started filling in the spaces between his toes.
He looked at her, confused.
"This is my world, my universe," she said, spreading her arms and spinning, the way a happy child might. "When I was born, this was only emptiness, and for a long time I lived in darkness. I was called the child of the void by those who knew of me. But as I grew and understood those around me, these lights appeared above, dotting my black sky with all sorts of colors." 
Alan looked up at the pinpricks of light that faded in and out of the sky, as if a cosmic weaver was sewing with thread that cycled through the colors of a rainbow. Ashra continued, "Many have wondered how I, blind though I am, could know what color was, what beauty was. But they don't know that I have these stars. I can pluck each one out of the sky, just like this." She reached up and pulled a star towards her as if it were no more than a ripe fruit on a branch. "I borrow their sight, and in doing so, I have come to know what colors are and how people see them." She played with the star in her hand, rolling it around her palm like a pebble. "I have noticed," she mused, "that most people have the same favorite color. It's just what one person calls green, another person calls blue, and what one calls purple another may call yellow."
She brought the star to her eye. "I only see people who are close to me. Their stars fade when I am further away." She stood on her tiptoes and put it in front of Alan's eye. He saw the inside of another ship, unfamiliar characters manipulated by hands that danced across them with familiarity.
She released the star and it floated back into the sky. He watched as it ascended and settled back into its place, rotating with the others. 
"Now that you are here, I finally have the opportunity to see you with my own sight," Ashra said. She came up to him and stood up on her toes, while Alan knelt down and put his face close to hers. "You have the most beautiful eyes," she said. "I haven't seen their kind before, but then again, I don't have the chance to look into people's eyes often. What color are they?"
"I think they're mostly gray, with some other colors thrown in. I haven't really looked," Alan admitted. He gazed towards the center of the sky above the tree. There was an empty space surrounded by larger stars that didn't move. They sat firmly in their places and watched the other stars revolve around them.
"What are those?" he asked, pointing to them.
She followed his gaze. "I call them the perpetuals. These perpetual stars were some of the first to appear here. By their light I could see myself, and so I could make everything else you see here." She grabbed one of the perpetuals, a deep blue one, and tried to pull it down. It didn't budge. "I believe they are my family and my relatives. I cannot see through their eyes as I can with others. Perhaps my father saw to that." She pointed to one of them; a star that shone like it was covered in purple ice. "That one has always been there. Next to it, there once was one that was pink like the skin of a peach. But after my mother's death, it's disappeared. All that remains of her perpetual is the dark hole there," she said, looking at the emptiness Alan noticed earlier.
Alan was awkward during moments like these. "I'm sorry," he muttered.
"You needn't be," she said. "She wanted a better life for us. I am sad that she had to die for it, but her dreams and wishes live on through me." She stood up. "Thanks to you, I know now the true extent of the atrocities committed by my family and the empire. Though it was difficult, I am glad I was the outcast, the unwanted and useless child, so that I could see the galaxy with eyes untainted by their lust for power."
She walked over to the water's edge, near where Alan was standing. She kept going, her feet making small ripples as she walked across the surface of the water. "I wanted to thank you," she said, "for saving me and finishing what my mother set out to do. This world makes dreams into reality, or as close as it can be. Just as you did not need your boots," she said, pointing to his bare feet, "nor do you need the past that burdens your mind."
Alan's eyes became steel and his lips grew firm. "My past is my own, and it belongs in the past," he said.
"I do not know what happened, but it is clear you have seen much more than you should have in your years."
Alan smiled briefly and looked at her. "And what would a child like you know of time?" he asked.
"Time stretches here, as it does in dreams," she said. "And so I have had much time to think and much time to observe. But it is only in these past few days that I have begun to act. So I offer you the only thing I can."
 "We're at war," Alan responded. "I'll have the luxury of time after we defeat the empire."
"There's always time, especially here. I'm not asking you to tell me what haunts you. I only ask for you to imagine what it would be like if it didn't follow you anymore." Her eyes narrowed, and Alan felt like she could see the entirety of his being. "It is like a shadow that clings to you, extinguishing your light that is so bright. Remember what it was like before the pain. Imagine if you didn't need those pills anymore."
"How did you??" his eyebrows furrowed in confusion, but his stubbornness won over his curiosity. "I could never be over it," he said. "I could never let it go."
"Imagine," she said. "Just imagine. I'm not asking you to be happy. I'm not asking you to forget. I'm asking you to remember. To remember with the love and joy you once had."
He looked down at the ground and searched inside of himself for a part that he had been afraid of. How long had it been? Three or four years? It couldn't have been more than that. He had not bothered to remember because he didn't want to. He put his hand on those memories. He wanted to open the lock that bound them. But his hand quavered; his will was unsteady. He withdrew.
"No," he said aloud. "They belong in the past. They have no place in the present."
Ashra tilted her head to the side and studied him. "Your thoughts are enough. You have moved the pebble that blocks the dam," she said. There was no hint of disappointment or judgment.
A vibration rattled across Alan's wrist, surprising him. "How could I be getting a message in this place?" he wondered.
"Time is warped and bent here, but your body still feels and your mind still responds," Ashra said. "I'm afraid you're needed elsewhere." She nodded towards his wrist.
