The Maiden Orana was weaving more strands when she felt the instincts of the spider leave her. Her irises lost their red rings and faded to amber, the color they were before she was joined to the spider. She looked down. The spider's head was no longer there, just a cavity. 
She felt heavy. She tried, but could no longer command her legs to hold her up. The spider fell, leaving a deep imprint on the grass from its weight. The abdomen landed with a thud. Blood seeped into the white markings on the back. 
Orana had been looking forward to this day for years. It was with pleasant acceptance that she felt her heartbeat slow. She and the spider were joined in both life and death. The spider completely left, leaving only the human behind.
Ashra had been hiding a distance away, near the entrance to the cave where Orana once dwelled. She had been gathering the stars of the fallen soldiers and runners, preparing to make a drasil, but she hadn't been fast enough. She heard the spider fall to the ground.
<I fulfill your wish.> In the Empyrean, Ashra gazed upon Orana's fast fading star and split it into two halves. She put the human half, so much like her mother's, back into the sky, granting Orana a few more moments of life. She took the spider half, an ancient soul that had seen many seasons on Phalos, into her palm. This was the final one she needed. She added it to the white mass she had in her hand. Zava, crouched at the top of a tree, was told to keep his eyes on the Sanctum tower in the distance. Despite the fighting that happened around him, his bright eyes never wavered.
Ashra used Zava's sight and hurled the ball as far as she could towards the Sanctum outpost. It manifested itself as a bud of light that appeared at the top of the tower.

***

The marquis was in the basement of the tower complex. He listened through his neural implant as the technicians reported their findings. "Sir, a spike in delta waves again," one said. 
"Location?" he asked.
"One locus in the west, near Major Killian's position." The technician pored over more data. "Wait, a second locus has appeared?" the technician paused, making sense of the data. "The second locus is above the antenna, sir."
"This antenna?" he asked, as if there were any other.
"Yes sir." The technician's voice was calm but he clenched and unclenched his fists in nervous anticipation.
The marquis weighed some options in his head. He could leave the tower and leave the others to figure it out. His life was, after all, more valuable than everyone else's here. But if he were to be the only survivor of Phalos, Seth would certainly kill him, maybe even personally. That was a fate worse than whatever death awaited him here, even with those bloodsucking insects around. What were delta waves anyway?
"Everyone out!" he commanded. "Make sure to take the equipment you need to contact the throneworld. Gather near the wall of the outpost!" He shouted these last words behind him as he had already disappeared down the hallway and was pressing the button for the lift that would take him to the surface. The others passed him by with their portable light console cores and satellite relay equipment as they went up the stairs next to him. He looked at them, then at himself. He begrudgingly joined them.
Though it was far away, Ashra felt the seed. She coaxed it to grow, feeling the hard edges crack and soften under her touch. 
Above the tower, roots spread out from the tip, seeking their way closer to the ground. As if they drew nourishment from the air, the top of the seed broke in half. A single bud emerged. It grew from a stem into a stalk, and as Ashra danced, the stalk lengthened and expanded into a trunk. Branches made of light covered it like a head of hair, the black veins inside fueling its growth. A tree, with its roots, trunk and leaves, hung floating in the space above the tower, brighter than the two moons that rose behind it.
Ashra stopped dancing and the tree stopped spinning. She was tired but she would continue. She would honor the maiden's death and the deaths of everyone who had fought to protect her; she would honor her mother and do what fate did not allow Lydia to do. With the last of her strength, she brought the tree down. From its position high in the sky, the drasil descended gracefully. It touched the red beacon atop the tower. From that moment on, the beacon would never again mar the moons' light with its blinking. Sheets of steel wound tightly together with powered coils were reduced to individual atoms and then split further down into oblivion as the drasil engulfed them. The tree continued down without a sound. When the roots touched the earth, the ground itself was rendered into nothing.
Orana looked upon the tree of light, glad to see the drasil had returned to Phalos. It stood tall and proud. When it disappeared, as it would, as would everything, nothing would remain of the Sanctum. She was content. Ashra would be a fine priestess. With that thought, the maiden slumped forward and died.

***

Ashra expended all of her energy. She put every thought and fiber of her being into that tree. She knew the pulse of life underneath it; she felt every leaf and piece of bark. 
Ashra sunk the drasil into the ground and didn't let go. Her mind became one with the tree, and the stars in the Empyrean were eclipsed by light.
She fell backwards into the cave. Her mind went white, then sunk into the void.

Chapter 33

When Ashra awoke she could see. As a result, she thought she was dreaming. Everything looked real, but more than real. There were colors she had never seen before, colors her human mind couldn't process. 
The water she swam in was clear. Powerful muscles drove her forward. When she caught sight of her body, long and curling behind her, she understood that she was a kind of serpent that rode the waves.
She never had eyes like these before. She moved herself deeper into the stream until she could see the rocks on the bottom. They were just rocks, but her eyes saw their colors as no human ever could. The slate gray of the stones, mixed with jades and some hints of amber. She didn't know where she was and she didn't know what she was, but she had seen that particular mix of colors before. Of rocks on the riverbed. She thought back to Alan, to the one time he visited the Empyrean. When he brought corporeal form to the pale yellow perpetual. To when she looked at his eyes. They were the same color, the color of rocks on the riverbed.
She felt a whisper in her mind, like the scent of blossoms. Inside it was the voice of a woman, similar to her own and similar to her mother's. <You have returned,> the voice said. 
For the first time, Ashra knew what it was like to have someone speak directly to her thoughts. <I have never been here,> she responded. As she spoke, her consciousness left the serpent. She floated above it, up towards the surface, and then out of the water. But nothing had eyes up here, she thought. What was she seeing with?
<You have not been here, but this is where you belong,> the voice said. <Your mother never managed to come, for she was taken before she could make the journey. But you; I do not remember one as young as you.>
<Izmir?> Ashra said. <You are the slumberer?>
<My granddaughter is smart too.> Ashra heard the smile in her voice, though Izmir's voice was weak and brittle. Izmir continued, <I have waited for another to come. I feared she would not appear after Lydia was taken. But she did well; she had you. And with what help I could send, you have come back to us.>
<It this?is this place real?> Ashra asked.
<As real as you are, and as real as I used to be. We are hidden deep within Phalos, in a place where no human has been. But we, priestesses with minds that roam the earth and the stars; we can come here. Though, my mind isn't what it used to be. I have not left the grove since the death of my body.>
Ashra saw for the first time with eyes of her own. It might've been something floating in the air inside the grove, something that acted as rods and cones that could interact with the neurons of her mind. She didn't know. But she could see with eyes she herself controlled, and that was greater than the why.
She saw the Empyrean realized outside of her mind. But where it was always night inside the Empyrean, here it was day. There were no perpetuals in the sky, just the sun.
She looked down. It wasn't a river she had been swimming in. It was a wide moat that encircled a small island. The sand on the edges grew darker as the water lapped at it. In the center was a tree. It was not her tree, but it was similar. Bark covered patches of it, but some parts were worn away with age. The parts that showed were white and smooth. This tree was taller; its branches were spread thin and only a few leaves remained. Whatever fruit it bore had fallen away in seasons past.
<Why am I here?> Ashra asked.
<Only the priestess who gives herself entirely to her art can make the journey here,> Izmir said. Her voice sounded distant and frail, growing quieter with every word. 
<So I am the priestess,> Ashra said. A silent affirmation echoed through her head. <Izmir,> she continued, <I have a question that only you can answer. Were you complete? Or were you born like me, blind and mute, doomed forever to only listen to others?>
<I had sight and voice,> Izmir said. <Though by the time I made my first drasil I was already a woman.> She paused, as if recalling a hazy fact. <When the emperor took Lydia, I guessed at what he would do. He made it so that you would find the way faster, by removing what wasn't necessary. There has never been a priestess as young as you, nor one forced to grow up so quickly.>
Nor one as lonely, Ashra thought. Phalos was a world all but forgotten by both the Sanctum and the Einhart, conquered in the earlier parts of the war. But the priestesses here all had people who accompanied them. They had teachers who taught them not only the importance of knowledge but its proper application. What matter was it if the food was rough or the beds not as soft? She could've had love here, love from more than just her mother. And as she realized this, her hatred for her father grew.
Izmir interrupted her thoughts. <Child, forgive the empty wanderings of an old mind. I do not have much time left. I have saved the last of my energy to make a request from you. Now that I've awakened, I cannot speak for much longer.>
<A request?> Ashra asked.
<Phalos needs a new guardian to protect it. I have tried, but you saw what happened to Maiden Orana and the children when I sent help at the wrong time. Time moves strangely to me, and my soul is no longer capable of protecting this planet. But yours is.>
<Is that what's required? My soul?> Ashra asked.
<Just a part,> she said. Her voice was fainter with every word. <Just a piece of you, so you can feel the flow of the planet, the animals and the plants, and preserve the balance we have had with nature. So Phalos will never suffer the same fate again.>
Ashra wished she could consult with her mother or Alan. But she was alone with Izmir, so she looked to herself. Was this where she wanted to spend the rest of her life? Could she make a commitment to be responsible for the fate of a territory she had just arrived on? Though her mind was undecided, her heart knew the answer.
<Yes, Izmir. I will do it.>
Izmir's joy filled the grove. Ashra felt the greatest sense of elation from the tree, then an emptying, as if water were being poured from a jug. 
Izmir was no more. The tree, dried and fragile, cracked. It started as a seam from the base, splitting the trunk. The crack continued up, sounding like twigs snapping in winter. It seemed like the pressure of eons had built up inside the tree, and once the crack had reached the top of the trunk, all the sorrow and pain it knew released in one burst. The tree blew apart. In that moment, the vessel was empty, and it sought for anything to fill itself.
The vessel asked and Ashra offered. It was instinct, something she couldn't learn but already knew. She sought the vessel out, sensing that it was nothing more than a shallow bowl. Her fingers brushed its surface. 
She lurched and gasped, feeling like her heart itself was being removed. But it was only a part of it; a small, white gem that floated out of her chest. Still, that part of her encompassed the whole of her being. Her memories and experiences were there, along with the love and hate she knew.
A moment later, there was no more pain, only the fleeting memory of something she once had. 
The white gem settled in the center of the vessel. Light grew around it, protecting it and keeping it warm. That part of her became the new seed. She felt it go below the surface of the grove.
From the branches and twigs of fallen wood scattered about, a small bud sprouted on the center of the island. It blossomed deep inside the crater where Izmir's tree once stood. Its stalk was only the height of a finger and even smaller in width. Two leaves unfurled from the top of the stalk, exposing their green flesh to the sun. Roots dug their way through the soil. As they connected with the earth, Ashra knew Phalos for the first time.
Until now, she had only been a visitor, walking upon its surface. But as a part of her soul tapped into the heart of Phalos, she felt the creatures, from the smallest insect that dwelled in the ground to the great haga that roamed the plains. She could not control them, but she could speak to them, she could appeal to a part of their brain that always felt her. She could ask them to assist those who needed help, and it was their choice to act or not. But they always did, for they trusted the soul of the land, and knew, deep down, that it acted in their best interests.
A soul. Ashra realized she had a soul after all.
Ashra saw one last glimpse of the serpent that dwelled in the moat surrounding the tree. It still roamed the waters, parts of its tail and long body breaking the surface as it swam. It stopped and reared its head out of the water, shaking droplets from its brightly colored scales. It stared straight at her, and then bowed its head.
Ashra's sight dimmed, and her experience of having her own eyes was over.

Chapter 34

"Is she the one?" Brindle asked. After their fight with Orana, all that was left was Killian and another mercenary by the name of Brindle, so called because of the stripes of scars that ran down his face.
"I think so." Killian looked at the other bodies, half man and half beast, nudging them with his boot. He still avoided the corpse of the spider. He was afraid it would rise up again, though more of its innards were outside of it than inside. This girl near the cave was the only one that was completely human. She was unconscious on the rock floor, her white hair framing her like a shroud. Killian checked again and said, "This is the source of the delta waves, alright."
"Even if we get 'er back, is the marquis still alive? I want my reward," Brindle said.
"It doesn't matter if the marquis is alive or not. Seth wants this girl, and the prince's pockets are deeper than the marquis's." Killian leaned over her and put his fingers to her neck, relieved to find a strong pulse. A glimmer of silver caught his eye and he moved his fingers down. Underneath the collar of her white dress and lying on her skin was a pendant in the shape of a crescent moon, fastened by a thin white chain around her neck. A large blue jewel dangled from its center. The pendant glowed in the moonlight.
The silver also caught Brindle's eye, whose hands were faster. He reached down and clutched the pendant. A second later he yelped as it burned through his glove, leaving an imprint seared on his palm. Out of habit, he raised his hand, ready to slap the unconscious girl. Killian caught his forearm before his hand came down. "The prince will pay more if she's undamaged," he said. He threw Brindle's arm to the side.
Killian searched her for any other weapons; he didn't want her waking up and slitting his throat. He had climbed too high up the ladder of rank to lose it all now, now when he could finally prove himself to the First Prince directly. He patted her down and felt something under the intricate cloth belt she wore. He carefully reached down into its folds. His hands brushed against something hard and he pulled out a knife. He threw it to the side. It clanged as it disappeared into the darkness. His hand found one more object: a small opaque sphere no larger than a marble. It looked to be a transponder or receiver of some sort. He dropped it on the ground and crushed it under the heel of his boot. No one would know where they were. No one else would get the glory of returning the child sought by the Voice of the Empire himself. 
Killian tossed her over his shoulder. She weighed almost nothing. Her white hair swung in unison with his steps as he walked towards the levdisk, still on the ground. As he put a foot on its surface it whirred to life, its blue light glowing in the darkness. Brindle followed behind and they took off towards the smoking ruins where the antenna once stood.
 Zava watched through the leaves as they grew smaller and then disappeared beyond the trees. His bright eyes shifted to the marble Killian destroyed, now no more than black dust and various metal parts. A small red light on one of its components grew dim and vanished.

Chapter 35

Alan and his team had made it to the small spaceport inside the facility on Abyssinia. Rows of shuttles were standing by on the launch ramps, waiting for people who would never come. They picked one and boarded.
He sat in the pilot seat with Argus as his navigator. He familiarized himself with the controls and pressed a series of buttons. It seemed like the shuttle was built before light consoles were made standard.
Aki was lain out on one of the beds, the scant medical supplies of the ship scattered around her. Her breathing was shallow but her pulse was stabilized, and she kept a strong grip on her sniper rifle, finding comfort in the hard barrel.
Alan made preparations to leave. The lights on the side of the launch ramp turned from red to green. Four slats opened at the head of the ramp. Loose rubble pinged off the magnetic rail and rain poured in from above. Fren followed, their claws gripping the sides of the hatch as they climbed into the spaceport, their tails leaving wet trails behind them.
Alan craned his neck back to look to at Aki. "Hold on back there!" He slid his finger across the throttle and the shuttle rumbled to life. It was sluggish from lack of use, or perhaps Alan had just gotten used to the response and speed of the Umbra. But the shuttle moved and that was all he needed. With his left hand, he adjusted the magnetic propulsion of the ramp. He only needed a little boost to get out; he wasn't leaving Abyssinia just yet. Electricity surged through the launch ramp and the shuttle shot forward.
A fren jumped out of the shuttle's way as it went up the ramp and out the hatch. As soon as they were out, Alan turned on his radio. "Sylvan, status."
"Still inside the ground floor entrance, sir."
"Get ready to leave." Alan swung the shuttle around, scowling as it oversteered into the somber skies. This vehicle didn't deserve to be called a ship. The visibility was low, but he could still make out the fren as they circled the entrance to the facility, lured by the blood inside.
He looked to his right. "Argus, what weapons does this bucket have?"
Since it lacked a light console, Argus was busy cycling through different options on a screen. His choices included different beverage selections that could be served in the passenger compartment along with cabin light settings which ranged from soft to business. Considering the craft lacked a darkspace engine, Argus wondered if it was just meant to ferry people from one side of the planet to the other. "Boss, if we can kill them with refreshments and soothing music, I think we can win this."
"You're kidding me," Alan responded.
"The closest thing we have to weapons are flavored drinks and hospitality."
Aki's voice was quiet through Alan's com. "Open the hatch."
"Aki, rest," Alan commanded. "You barely survived your encounter with Vijera. We'll get you patched up once we're in the Umbra." He waved for Argus to go back. "Secure yourselves, we're going to do things the old-fashioned way."
Alan got a better look at the area. The dropship Meridian was still in one piece despite the fren that crawled over it. "Sylvan, I'm going to do a wide sweep with the shuttle. Sprint to the dropship on three. Ready?" Alan asked.
"Yes sir."
"One." Alan sent the shuttle into a steep dive, striking a fine balance between speed and control, though the gusts of wind forced him to slow his descent. In the back, Argus braced himself with his legs against a row of plush chairs. He had one arm draped protectively over Aki. She groaned but kept her eyes trained on the window.
"Two." He pulled the shuttle out of its dive only a few feet above the ground, keeping the bottom of the ship level with the rocky ground. The heat of its engines turned the unlucky fren behind it to ash. The momentum he had coming down kept the ship sailing sideways while he faced the entrance to the facility. Small thumps sounded against the fuselage as the shuttle crashed through the beasts. He saw the door Sylvan and his team was waiting behind.
"Three." Alan cleared the door and it burst open. Three figures stumbled out. Sylvan was in the lead, followed by Samson and Deacom. The shuttle's momentum forced Alan to turn and he lost sight of them as he circled around the dropship. He was relieved when he saw Sylvan in the cockpit. The Meridian's thrusters came to life.
"We are onboard sir, awaiting further instructions."
"Glad you could join the party," Alan said. "We have what we came here to find. It's time to go home and see what we can do with it. Lead the way out. We'll follow beneath you."
"Understood, Second Medium." The dropship lifted into the sky, its lasers clearing away debris above it as it climbed into the upper atmosphere. Thankfully, the hole they made through the minefield earlier was still wide enough to fit through.
Alan had just relayed his location to the Umbra for pickup when he saw a small white light flash on his wrist. He hoped he would never see the activation of the emergency beacon he had given Ashra, but there it was, blinking softly. The computer had lost the constant signal that kept track of the beacon's location and reported the event to Alan.
Now that they had the data mine, Claudia would need him more than ever. He knew she would wonder where he was. He knew, after years of fighting, the section of the fleet he would command. In his mind, he was already arranging the ships across the battlefield of his imagination. But there was one thing that took precedence over his duty to the Einhart.
There was no hesitation when Alan made his decision. He opened the com to the back, where Argus still had Aki secured with one palm. "Ashra's beacon has been activated," he said. Argus looked at Aki, and they both nodded. "This is a personal matter," Alan continued, "and you two don't need to get involved. I'll-"
"We'll," Argus corrected. "We'll go. The Einhart can fare without us. But you, well, we're not so sure about you."
Alan smiled. He was glad they chose to stay. He had come to rely upon the two more than he liked to admit. Feelings had no place in war, but it was a comfort to know these two would be there. "Thank you," he said.
Alan took one last look at the storm-roiled surface as they left the atmosphere of Abyssinia. The shuttle struggled against the gravity, but broke through with a final thrust. The Umbra awaited them, an elliptical black silhouette that blocked out the stars behind it. 
It was quick work docking with one of the side ports. Alan walked through the extended vacuum link onto the Umbra, breathing in and relishing the familiar, recycled air of his ship. Argus came in with Aki in his arms and put her in the medbed. He looked over the analysis. There were broken ribs, internal bleeding and a collapsed lung, but these could be healed in darkspace.
Alan sat in his pilot seat, loving the way it hugged his legs. He hailed the Meridian. "Sylvan, how is your crew?" he asked.
"There're three of us left. We're banged up, but we'll live. Thank you for getting us out of there."
"As any teammate would do." Alan paused. "I have a favor to ask."
"Anything, Second Medium. Our lives are yours to command."
"Don't speak like a Sanctum," he said with a laugh. "With the Einhart, your lives are your own. My favor is simple. Dock with the Umbra."
"Yes sir." Sylvan positioned the dropship next to them. Alan allowed the connection with a side airlock, and after a hiss, he went out onto the thin tube to meet them. When Alan first joined the Einhart, he was concerned that only a wobbly cylinder of plastic separated him from the emptiness of space, but he had since gotten used to it. Sylvan still looked apprehensive. His eyes wandered throughout the tube, searching for cracks that weren't there.
"Thank you for doing this," Alan said.
Sylvan bowed. "Anything for the Second Medium."
Alan reached for Sylvan's hand, the skin rough with years of work, and pressed his data mine into it. "I need you to deliver this to Claudia directly." He felt Sylvan's fingers curl around the tube. "It contains the location of Sanctuary, of the throneworld." As he said this, he saw Sylvan's eyes widen. Sylvan stared at the spike as if Sanctuary's position could be gleaned by the myriad little dots on its surface.
"We haven't been able to find it because we haven't been looking in the right places. We always thought it was a planet with a fixed orbit, but all along, it's been in darkspace," Alan explained. "Think of all the scouts and ships we lost on false tips. Every time we entered normal space and there was only an ambush waiting. We can avenge them. We can make their deaths count," Alan said.
Sylvan was hesitant to accept such a responsibility. "This is something the Second Medium should deliver to the High Adjudicant himself."
"I would love to, but I entrust the duty to you. There is another matter that requires my attention. If I know Claudia, she'll be mobilizing the fleet as she as soon as she receives this. Tell her to assign you a warship; you've earned it."
Sylvan was surprised by the honor. "Thank you, Second Medium."
"Alan. Call me Alan. I am a shadow and hold no rank."
"You not only deserve but have earned my respect. You'll always be the Second Medium to me, and to call you anything less wouldn't be doing you the proper honor."
Alan patted him on the shoulder. "Remember, give it to her by hand. We can't risk anything being transmitted through darkspace, or normal space for that matter. The empire can't know we've found Sanctuary."
"Yes sir. It shall be done," Sylvan said.
"Tell Claudia I'll be there when she needs me."
"Understood, sir."
Alan left Sylvan and returned to the Umbra, stopping by Aki's side. She was unconscious as the medbed repaired her broken bones and bruised organs under a green sterilized shield. "Will she be all right?" he asked Argus.
Argus looked up from a scan of Aki's torso. "She took a beating, but it's nothing we can't fix."
Alan nodded. "Prepare for shift to darkspace."
The Umbra guarded the Meridian until the dropship gained enough speed and shifted. Alan put in a slight course correction. After a final boost, the engines attached themselves to the hull. They burned black as the Umbra made the shift into darkspace towards Phalos.

Chapter 36

The marquis wasn't able to see the full extent of the damage until the next day, when the sun revealed all that had transpired in the evening. The antenna, their main source of communication with the rest of the Sanctum, had been reduced to nothing. He hoped the report was an exaggeration, but it was literally nothing. There wasn't a scrap of metal or scaffold or support strut to be seen. It was as if it simply never existed. The only evidence that there had been a tower there was the concrete foundations that the light tree hadn't touched. Other than that, all that remained were holes and tunnels in the ground created by the drasil roots when Ashra brought the tree into the earth.
After scavenging for any materials they could use, which ended up being only dried foodstuffs that had partially rehydrated in the heat and humidity, the survivors headed towards the estate of the Marquis d'Avester. The mansion was situated on a hill and filled with sunlight, built in the Adonan style with curved roofs and wide windows. A manicured garden would have been a better yard than the forest that surrounded it, but despite their best efforts, the Sanctum could never keep the flora away.
The marquis was originally part of the minor nobility on Adona. In his quest for influence, he gladly sold what passed through his ears to the empire, facilitating their takeover. But once a traitor, always a traitor, he knew, and the Sanctum feared what would happen if he knew too much. So they sent him to a place where he had no influence, only time and the illusion of power. But the Marquis d'Avester would redeem himself with this child that Seth wanted.
Though it was hours later, the girl was still unconscious, and he hoped she remained that way. He had a way with politicians and others as slippery as him, but he did not know how to deal with children. They had eyes that could see past whatever faade he put up that day. After they had brought her back, he had that scarred mercenary, Brindle, keep watch over her. He didn't know what these delta waves were, nor did he know why Seth wanted this girl so much, but he knew from experience that fewer questions meant fewer troubles. Still, the prince expected a report from him, and without the antenna that would be difficult. When he didn't check in, would Seth choose to send a ship to rescue him?
The marquis turned to a technician. "How long till we can contact the throneworld?" he asked.
A technician glanced up and stared at the marquis with dead eyes, partly due to the exhaustion of working through the night and partly because his mind was dedicated elsewhere. Wires snaked out of the neural implant at the base of his skull as he interfaced with what remained of the communications mainframe. It seemed hopeless; so little was left of the equipment they needed. In his gloom, he thought that it might've been easier to create a new antenna from the trees that grew around them; there were certainly enough. But the marquis wasn't one for humor. "Sir, the attack destroyed our only means of direct communication with the Sanctum," he said. "What we can do is upload our message to one of the satellites and hope a darkspace probe passes through this area and picks it up. It can then broadcast our message to the nearest planet and hopefully they'll send help."
"No!" the marquis said. "No one else is to know what happened here. What if the Einhart got a hold of it? We'd all be killed!" He whacked the technician on the skull. "Think! Figure it out. I don't have time to waste. Find a way to reach the First Prince or I'm leaving you behind and you can call for all the help you want when I'm gone."
The technician was glad that half his mind was occupied searching for a way to boost the signal or he would've given the marquis an earful. Everyone knew that there was no way off Phalos anymore. The one offworld transport for the outpost had been parked near the antenna, and judging by the hole that now replaced it, he was sure that they would all be getting off at the same time or never. Still, an order was an order, and he took up the challenge of trying to broadcast a signal without anything to broadcast with. If only frustration could power machinery, he thought.
In the nearby forests, Killian stomped around between the trees. He had not been able to sleep after the events of the night, so he spent his time staking out a crude perimeter around the mansion. With a shove, he drove the last of the poles deep into the earth. A clicking came from its base and it synchronized with the four other posts. The pentagonal barrier would detect anything that broke its invisible walls, though it could only warn him about it. Killian would take care of the rest with his pistol. He made the short trek back to the mansion, saluting the marquis as he arrived. "Sir, perimeter has been established," he said, patting the ground with his foot. "If any of those things stick their heads within fifty yards of the mansion, they won't have a head left."
"Good," the marquis responded. "See what you can do about contacting-" The marquis was cut off by the loud boom of a ship entering Phalos's atmosphere. He looked up at the source of the sound. The ship was shaped like an ellipse, black and rounded with four engines tethered to its body with purple electricity. It was bright in the sky, getting larger as it came down through the clouds. The engines shifted position, rotating and moving along the fuselage until they faced the ground, slowing its descent. It was too small to be a warship, but the marquis didn't expect a large rescue craft. After all, he and the child would be the only people the prince would want.
He kept his eyes glued on the ship, never having seen one like it before. Was it a prototype? Was this ship to be his for a job well done? Or maybe this girl, whoever she was, was more than she seemed.
His musings were cut short when he felt something sharp slide into his back. He reached behind himself and felt the spot with his hand. He felt something warm. When he saw his fingers, they were slick with blood. The pain came a moment later, but his scream was muffled by the engines of the Umbra as it flew overhead. Any leftover noise was trapped by Killian's gloved hand.
"Shhhh," Killian whispered into the marquis's ear. He drove the blade in deeper. "It's too bad you died when we battled the natives here. I'll be sure to let the prince know how brave you were." He twisted the knife. "It's the least I could do to repay you for your kind treatment of me."
The last sound the Marquis d'Avester heard was the contented sigh of his assistant of years, and with it the hatred, malice and disdain Killian had for the marquis. For the first time, the marquis had an inkling of how others truly viewed him, but he couldn't ponder it further as the knife went once more across his neck, causing the blood to flow freely from his body and leaving his brain deprived.
Killian's eyes darted back and forth. Satisfied no one else saw, he lowered the marquis's body to the ground and then dragged it through the grass, beyond the perimeter he built. There, he rolled it unceremoniously into a ditch and threw the knife in the other direction where no one would go looking for it. He looked for the ship that had come, his ticket off of Phalos. The ship didn't land near where the antenna once stood, but further to the west, deep in the forest. That was strange, he thought. Any Sanctum ship should have known the location of the outpost, but considering there wasn't much of the outpost left, the mistake was understandable.
He went back to camp to tell the survivors the news. He was sure they would all be glad.

Chapter 37

Alan brought the Umbra down near a cave. While Aki was in the final stages of her convalescence, Alan left the ship and breathed the air of Phalos. Something about it reminded him of his own homeworld of Cybele, of that place where the forest met the field. He found the tracking beacon he had given Ashra near the cave entrance, smashed to bits. He looked for any trace of white hair, but the princess was nowhere to be seen. He cursed and pounded his fist against the ground. A rustling in the trees caught his attention. He drew his pistol and aimed between the leaves. A pair of bright eyes looked back at him. They flattened into slits as they studied him.
The eyes belonged to a creature he had never seen before. From what Alan could see, he looked human, a male child. With the exception of his eyes, the rest of his head and torso could've belonged to any boy. But at the ends of his limbs, instead of hands and feet, were claws, well-worn from climbing up and down trees. Green scales covered parts of his skin like a reptile. He hid most of his body behind the tree, afraid to come forward.
Alan saw the boy and felt only sadness. This wasn't the first time he saw the discarded experiments of the empire. He put his pistol back into its holster and held out his empty hands. "Come out," he said. "I won't hurt you."
The boy took two small steps forward, his claws still on the bark of a tree. "Are you?one of them?" he asked timidly.
"No," Alan said. "I'm not. My friends and I," he gestured to the Umbra, "we fight against them."
"Against them?" The boy took another step closer. 
Alan smiled and nodded. "I'm Alan." He extended a hand, and the boy came forward and took it in his claw.
"I'm Zava."
"A pleasure, Zava." Alan knelt down and looked at Zava's face. "I need to know, have you seen a girl? She's about as tall as you, with white hair." He brought his hand up in an estimation of her height.
"Do you mean the priestess?"
"Priestess? Is that what Ashra's become?"
Zava looked to the east. "The priestess has brought hope to Phalos, hope and the power to win back our land." He smiled. "But after she saved us she had no more energy, and they took her." The smile turned into a line of guilt. 
Alan followed his gaze to the east. "Is that where she is now? We passed over a large patch of dirt and a big house."
Zava nodded. "They took her there. When they left they said something about a reward from a prince." He turned to Alan. "Are you going to save her?"
"I am."
"We need her," Zava said. "Phalos needs her."
Alan took the boy by the shoulders and looked into his eyes. "She will be safe. I promise." He stood up and nodded to Argus inside the ship. The big man had been at his light console scanning for any other movement in the area. With a flick of his finger, the Umbra's engines came to life.
Alan ruffled Zava's hair. "Take care of Phalos, Zava. One day, the priestess will return. I will keep her safe until then."
Zava watched as Alan entered the ship. The Umbra took off. Zava wanted to say that regardless of where her body went the priestess had already become a part of Phalos, deep in its roots, something he always felt. But being a child, he kept silent and waved goodbye from the treetops.
Alan watched Zava's small figure become even smaller. The climber's skin blended in with the foliage, and soon after no more trace remained of him.
"What did he say?" Argus asked.
"Her powers manifested, and there's nothing left of the outpost here as a result. But the Sanctum have her, and I'm sure they're going to take her offworld as soon as they can," Alan responded.
"What's the plan?"
Alan thought. "There wasn't resistance when we arrived, which means either they're defenseless, or they don't know who we are, or both. I'm afraid they know my face by now, and Aki looks too much like Vijera. But you, I don't think they'd recognize you." Alan paused for a moment. "How good's your acting?" he asked.
"For various reasons, I've become proficient. The best actors are the ones who act not for profit, but because their lives depend on it."
"Then this is what we'll do..." Alan said.

Chapter 38

Killian had to shield his eyes from the wind of the black ship as it landed. Its four engines were perpendicular to the ground, each changing its thrust as it brought the ship down for a soft landing. Nothing was visible behind the cloud of dust it sent up. By the time the air cleared and the engines went silent, a ramp had already emerged and touched the ground. On it was the largest man he had ever seen.
The ramp seemed to buckle under the large man's weight as he walked down it. His armor, which would have immobilized a normal soldier, was covered in different colors of dried gore. His gait was firm and measured. Killian was sure that one swing of his massive fists would remove his head, and he made a mental note to not let him get too close. But this man was no brute. His eyes took in everything with a glance, from the small group of survivors huddled off to the side to the technician trying to reach Sanctuary. Killian sensed intelligence behind those green eyes, and his suspicions were confirmed by his voice and diction.
The man cast a shadow over him as he approached. "The princess," he said. It wasn't a question; it was a command. He held out his hand as if he waited for Killian to put her in his palm.
"Welcome to Phalos," Killian responded. He saw no insignia, no sign of rank. His neural implant didn't register any matching facial features with those in the Sanctum's employ. "Your rank??"
"Is none of your concern," the large man answered brusquely. "I am here for the princess. That is all."
Brindle came up. "Did the prince send ya?" he asked.
Without hesitation he responded, "Yes, I was sent by the First Prince. He interrupted my mission just to have me fetch this girl. So if you'll be quick about it, I can get back to what I was doing."
Brindle was unfazed, because of bravado or stupidity, Killian couldn't tell. "Well, mister," the mercenary said, "we'll be glad to hand 'er over. But Seth mentioned a reward, and you're not seeing a hair until I get paid."
Argus raised his eyebrow and looked the mercenary up and down. He spoke to Killian. "Payment? Service to the empire is not defined by credits, but by dedication to our cause and the royal family. You'd do well to teach that to the people you associate with."
Killian shot Brindle a look and pushed the mercenary behind him. "Sir, you speak the truth. But the prince and the late marquis offered us a reward for the capture of the girl, and we hope you can honor it."
"The marquis? What happened to him?"
Killian gestured at the swath of dirt around them. "He didn't survive the night. When we went to retrieve the child, we were attacked by the native inhabitants. They had a new weapon. All they had were rocks and twigs and I don't know how they built it, but it was light-based and killed the marquis in the process. It also took out our only antenna for offworld communications." His eyebrows furrowed. "Speaking of which, how did you know to come find us? We salvaged what we could, but we haven't been able to broadcast any message off Phalos." The technician who had been watching from the ground nodded, hoping he could find some way to send a transmission.
"The prince has his ways," Argus said. "And he will be angrier for every moment I am delayed. His mood will be dependent on what I report to him, so it would behoove you to cooperate."
"Yes sir, of course." With Brindle next to him, Killian started walking towards the forest, towards the spot where he had killed the marquis. "Did you come by yourself?" he asked.
"Yes," Argus said.
Killian looked at Brindle, and they both knew what they were going to do, regardless of this man's connections to the prince. He waved for the big man to follow.
Argus scoffed. "Who do you think you are to waste my time? I'll be surveying the damage and arranging alternate transport for you while you fetch her. Bring her to me." 
"We're not comin' with you?" Brindle asked.
"No," Argus responded tersely. "I have my orders."

***

Alan was sitting beneath his console and monitoring Argus's conversation when he put his hand on the back of his head, feeling like there was an itch he couldn't scratch. But as he rubbed his scalp, he realized the itch didn't come from the nerves of his skin. It was a gentle breeze that rustled through his mind. <Aaaa,> it said softly, like a sigh. <Aaa? Aaaa? Alan??>
Thought it was very quiet, when he closed his eyes and let his mind wander, Ashra's voice became clear. <Alan. Your star is so bright. Why are you here?> Ashra asked. Her presence was faint, nothing more than a whisper.
He was flooded with relief when he heard her. He thought of his response, hoping she could hear it. <Ashra, you called for me, didn't you? Where are you? Are you safe?>
<I am alright,> she said. <I feel as if I've just woken up from a long slumber.> She paused as if clearing her head. When she spoke again, her voice was stronger. <I am glad you are here. It warms me to feel your presence, but I did not call for you.>
<Regardless, it seems like I came at the right time. What happened here?>
<A battle. A battle to reclaim Phalos, my mother's homeworld. It has become my responsibility to take back what was once ours.>
<Responsibility?> How did Ashra mature so quickly? <We can discuss these things once you're onboard the Umbra. The empire knows you're here, and they've undoubtedly sent people to retrieve you. It was only with luck that we arrived first. Please Ashra, tell me where you are. Argus is out on the field and he can come get you.>
<I've become the priestess for this planet, her steward and guardian. I cannot leave.>
<If you don't, they'll find you and bring you back to the Sanctum. Everything your mother did would have been in vain.>
<She wanted me to be here,> Ashra countered.
<Yes, she did,> Alan said. <But I'm sure she wanted you to be happy, and more, I'm sure she wanted you to be safe.>
<How do you know what she wanted?> There was no malice in her words; only curiosity.
Alan sighed. <Because I was once a father, and a father only wants what's best for his child. I can keep you safe.> He looked up and stared off into the gap between the chairs. <In time I'll find a way, I'll find a place where you can grow up in peace. But that'll have to come later. Right now, you're in danger.> He studied some scans of the area. <This place is swarming with Sanctum. I don't see any offworld transmissions, but there are strong residual delta waves. Was that you?>
<Yes, it was me,> Ashra said. <The people here, my people, they have taught me what they know, and I finally feel like I belong.> She paused for a moment. <I didn't ask for this; I didn't want to be a weapon. But it seems like everywhere I go I only bring destruction. I've come to embrace that part of me. I will use it against my father, who has done horrible things to many people. I am still the Princess of the Void, but now I will show him the Priestess of Phalos.>
<You'll have your chance,> Alan said. <We've found Sanctuary, the throneworld. In the little time we have, Claudia is gathering what ships she can to do battle.>
<Weren't you summoned as well?>
<I was, but there's someone who's more important,> he said with a smile.
<A part of me will always remain on Phalos, and that cannot be changed,> Ashra said. <But if you have a chance to stop my father, the root of all the pain across these worlds, I will come.>
<Good,> Alan said. <Once you're aboard, we'll rendezvous with the others. Where are you?>
Ashra felt around. <Grass. Fallen leaves. Cold.> She cast her mind about. <There are two coming towards me,> she said. Her words were shaded with anger as she recognized them. <These two were at the battle. Be wary of them.>
<Remain as you are. Don't let them know you're awake.>
<I understand your reasoning, but I prefer not to hide.>
Alan was taken aback. <When did you gain such courage?> he asked.
<When I learned that courage is what's needed to make change. When I learned that I, and only I, am in charge of who I become.>
Alan wasn't used to being disobeyed, but he was proud of her. <Then stand strong,> he said. He opened a line to Argus. "Did two men leave, heading towards the forest?"
Argus had been surveying the damage done to the outpost, when he suddenly became interested in a nondescript chunk of concrete off to the side. He knelt and whispered, "Yes boss. They asked me to follow but I told them to bring her to me."
"Go with them. Ashra's awake. Lose the two and get her. Claudia is waiting and we need to leave now."
"Understood." Argus got up and jogged into the forest. His big strides covered the ground in little time, and the two were surprised when he came up behind them.
"Did you change your mind, sir?" Killian asked.
"My survey is finished and I want to see the condition of the subject. That will be part of my report," Argus replied.
They went further in. Under the shade of a copse of trees Argus could make out the small figure of Ashra, standing in her white dress. Something had changed since he had last seen her. When she walked towards them, her head was held high. Her footsteps, small and reserved in the past, had turned into proud strides. She marched up to Argus and took his hand. <Thank you for coming,> she said to him privately.
Her familiarity with the big man perplexed Killian, but they were deep in the woods and his muffled screams wouldn't be heard. After they disposed of the body, he thought, it wouldn't be hard to take his ship.
<Be careful of these two,> Ashra said to Argus. Argus said nothing. He held her hand and turned back towards the Umbra. Killian and Brindle followed close behind.
As they started walking back to the outpost, Killian said, "You know, what I don't get is why you landed over there first, in the west. Shouldn't your ship have the outpost coordinates here on Phalos? There isn't anything over there near the caves." He looked at Argus with suspicion. "Sir," he added, without meaning it. 
Not deigning to respond, Argus slowed and put Ashra in front of him. There was no more need for pretense. He waited for them to step closer.
Behind Argus, Killian nodded to Brindle, and they brought out their plasma pistols. 
At the sound of weapons being drawn, Argus spun around and planted a fist into Brindle's face. He felt the man's nose and skull crack underneath his armored hand. The force sent Brindle crashing into Killian, knocking the pistol out of his grip. As he fumbled for it, Argus and the child disappeared, leaving a trail of trampled leaves behind them.
Killian cursed and pushed Brindle's unconscious body off of him. His hands came back smeared with blood but he didn't spare a second thought for his downed companion. He took aim at the fleeing pair and fired.
Argus pulled Ashra into his arms to protect her. He wove between the trees, dodging plasma as he ran. The trees sizzled and toppled to the ground from the blasts, and he thanked whatever gods there were on this planet that the foliage was there to absorb the hits.
His com crackled to life. "Status," Alan said.
"Got her," he said, shielding them from a rain of splinters with his free arm. "Coming back now."
Killian fired off blue bolts one after the other. He was sure his aim was good, but the trees seemed to always get in the way of his shots, as if they bent in and created a shield behind the retreating pair. 
"Good job," Alan said. "Hurry up; sensors show we have company coming in from orbit."
"It doesn't end, does it?" Argus cleared the forest and sprinted across the barren remnants of the outpost. He looked at Ashra as he ran. "You doing alright?" he asked. She nodded and held on tighter. The Umbra was in sight; he would make it.
Killian stood at the edge of the forest and steadied his breathing. He saved all of the remaining charge for this one shot. The man was dashing across the dirt, leaving a trail that was easy to follow. "No trees to save you now," he said. 
He squeezed the trigger. A mass of blue plasma the size of his head sped towards the pair. He discarded the empty gun and watched.
In the Empyrean, Ashra was jumping from person to person, trying to see any threats as they neared the Umbra. When Killian's star was still, she looked through his eyes. She saw the plasma streaking towards them and reacted on instinct. She raised her hand. A bright light erupted where Argus was a moment before. The light turned into a large drasil leaf that unfurled from its stem in the ground. The plasma splashed onto it and disappeared.
Killian cursed. He was about to continue the chase but had to duck behind a tree as suppressing fire came from the black ship. Apparently the man had lied about being alone as well. 
Argus ran up the ramp past Aki. She was covering the area in a hail of bullets from a portable mini-turret she had assembled. As soon as they were inside, she disengaged the tripod and brought up the ramp. She tapped the inside of the hull twice. "Clear," she said.
Alan gunned the engines and the Umbra came to life, covering the area with a layer of dust. Argus settled into his light console next to Alan.
"Is she safe?" Alan asked.
"Safe, sound and strapped in," Argus said.
"Well done. Thank you my friend. We have one more thing to take care of before we leave," he said, and he focused the cameras onto the ship that was glowing red as it entered Phalos. 
"Erudite be damned, is that a Sabre-class?" Argus asked.
"Yep," Alan said. "They sent a Sabre to come get her." The Sabre was a long and slender ship, shaped like a pointed cylinder. What it lacked in firepower it made up for in speed. It came down like a flaming spear through the atmosphere, designed for quick insertions and extractions. The prince sent the fastest ship for the princess. The Umbra rose to meet it.
"How long until we reach shift speed?" Argus said.
"We'll need to escape Phalos's gravity first," Alan said.
Aki came to join them. "I think they noticed us. Energy spike detected along their firing trenches." Ruts that ran the length of the Sabre started to glow.
The three of them felt a whisper in their heads. <It is my duty to protect Phalos,> Ashra said. <Maintain your course and leave the rest to me.> 
The cycle of life and death continued on the planet, her true homeworld that she was leaving behind. She gathered up the free-floating essences and shaped it in the Empyrean. She danced and the seed took root in the air, next to the Umbra and below the Sabre. The tree wasn't large, but its branches were wide enough to cover the circumference of the invading warship. She only needed to keep it still in the air and gravity would do the rest.
The Sabre was no match for the drasil. Its shields dissipated the moment it touched the light. The branches of Ashra's drasil cut through it, turning one of the fastest ships of the empire into long strips of metal as the ship impaled itself on the light and passed through with its momentum. The ship was cut into longitudinal sections, each section burning as it fell to Phalos. 
Ashra did not enjoy the deaths she caused. A part of her heart hated it, wished that there was no more war, no more killing, no more suffering created because of her. But as long as she was alive and as long as the empire existed, they would come for her, if only because she was the emperor's daughter and a princess that they thought belonged to them. So she wrapped up the tenderness of her heart and kept it safe, placing layers of anger and revenge on top to guard it.
They left the atmosphere of Phalos and entered the vacuum of space. As they shifted to darkspace, in her mind's eye, she caught a glimpse of a small bud and the serpent that guarded it. She knew a part of her soul, pure and innocent, would always be there, in that hidden grove. 
It hurt to leave. She felt a tug on her chest as the world shifted from the black and white of space and stars to the hazy realm of darkspace. Yet, her duty as guardian was to defend Phalos, and her actions now, she thought, would protect it from future threats.
Alan called back to her. "Are you hurt?"
<No. I am fine.>

Chapter 39

The water was always cold when Claudia stepped into it, but she liked the way it cleared her mind. By now, she associated the icy feeling with a sense of excitement. She disrobed at the side of the pool, wide and deep enough for only one person. She left her green suit, cravat and undergarments behind. Supported by female attendants, one on each hand, she let the water touch her skin and clear her senses. Tiny threads, invisible to the eye, poked past the surface of her skin and bonded with the nerves underneath. Piece by piece, the status of the Aurelius became clear to her. The thirteen darkspace engines were functioning properly. The hub was in need of three different kinds of extermination. The second biosphere required a new formulation of soil nutrients for what they were growing there.
But these were not the concerns of the High Adjudicant, not after she received the two data mines from Captain Winters. As she fully submerged herself into the integration chamber, the remaining threads in the water connected to her scalp, pushed past her skull and interfaced directly with her brain. The liquid acted as a conduit to accelerate the connections between her neurons and synapses. Other additives in the liquid kept her in a form of minor stasis. They shut down her body, freeing up a larger part of her mind to run the Aurelius. Her fingers became the missiles on their launch pads. Her eyes were the myriad cameras both inside and outside the ship. Her voice was the speakers and the text that scrolled across every screen. Her mind was still her own, but it was augmented by the three AI.
Mercurial glass came up from the edges of the pool, surrounding Claudia and the water inside with a layer of protection. The completed integration chamber slowly rose towards the ceiling. 
She accessed the ship-wide com. "Our years of defending our homeworlds are coming to an end," she said. "Our days of fearing when the empire will strike next will be over. Each and every one of you has contributed to the Einhart, and it is with your unwavering devotion and efforts that we have achieved all that we have." Her face was displayed on the screens in the hub. 
"We are the only combined force that can stand up to the empire, and we shall use all that we have prepared and learned, all of our knowledge and skills and resources to face them. For today, we bring the war to their homeworld." Claudia's avatar, a woman clad in a toga, was projected in many places across the ship, beamed into empty rooms and public areas alike.
"We have all lost much. But now, we stop the bleeding, we stop the hurt. We shall avenge all the family and friends we have lost on this journey. The Sanctum Empire will pay for the pain it has caused. And then, when the dust has settled, we shall have peace."
When she finished and her avatar winked out of existence, all military personnel had migrated to the lower levels of the Aurelius. She directed her thoughts to the assembled Zodiac Council. "We begin the assault on Sanctuary. We shall need the full cooperation of every ship in the fleet. And," she added, "I will need the power to make decisions without debate." It was a formality, for Claudia knew she already had control of the Einhart and no one was in a position to disagree. When there was a need, those that could not would look to those that could. Her temporary emergency powers were granted.
The ones that would be harder to convince would be the AIs. Would they see the value of supreme command under one person? She submitted her request to them. In her mind's eye, three figures, dressed in similar togas with different colors of hair, appeared. They all faced her and bowed in unison. The AI knew their self-preservation would be served by agreeing with the High Adjudicant, who they had gotten to know well over the years.
The bridge of the Aurelius was laid out in a semicircle. Rows of light consoles fanned out in a crescent, each operated by a technician that monitored the ship and surrounding space. 
Near the back, there was a clearing in the center that commanded a view of the bridge. A hole opened up in the floor. The crewmembers turned and bowed their heads. 
From the hole rose a glass tube. Simmons called out, "Claudia Einhart, the High Adjudicant and Prime Medium, is on deck."
Claudia emerged onto the bridge of the Aurelius. She floated inside her tube peacefully, as if she were asleep. Naked inside the integration chamber, her hands were crossed across her chest. Her hair, a golden curtain that billowed around her, protected her modesty. She summoned her avatar. In the center of the semicircle, light gathered to form a woman who looked like her, draped in a toga. She looked to a section of the bridge. "Prepare to separate," she commanded.
"Aye ma'am." In empty halls, strobe lights flashed and klaxons sounded. Pairs of airlocks closed shut throughout the Aurelius. One half of the airlocks were connected to the hub; the other half were connected to the capital ship itself. "The hub is fully isolated from the Aurelius," Simmons reported.
"Detach," Claudia said.
The living quarter towers and three biodomes reflected light from the sun they were left near. The bottom of the ship severed its connection with the top. The warship floated free, taking with it twelve of the thirteen darkspace engines.
The Aurelius, now unencumbered, assumed its role as the Garuda-class supercarrier, the flagship of the Einhart. It left the trappings of civilians and politics behind. Those that remained in the biodomes would find sustenance from the star they orbited. The ones on the Aurelius would continue on to face their fate.
The array of engines propelled them forward. "Preparations for shift to darkspace completed. Destination is the assumed location of Sanctuary."
"Shift."
The Aurelius disappeared into the darkness.

***

Though she had no one to tell, Claudia always enjoyed the shift. Ever since she became High Adjudicant, there were fewer chances to go through darkspace as everything was done remotely. She liked the way the colors glanced off the bubble of normal space they traveled in. And there were things that could only be detected by the ship's instruments; the subtle astral wind that blew with them, the fluctuations of radiation on the bubble border. She felt these through the ship's sensors.
"Receiving encrypted transmission from the Enkidu," a communications tech said.
"Allow," Claudia said.
On the view screen at the center of the bridge a young captain appeared with his crew behind him. "High Adjudicant, we've arrived at the rendezvous point. It's a single red dwarf star without orbiting bodies. A fine place for battle, ma'am."
"Have the darkspace probes found anything?" Claudia asked.
"There are slight disturbances in darkspace of a kind we haven't seen before. It's as if an object was creating waves through reality itself, and we are feeling the first of them."
Claudia kept it in mind. "Hide behind the star to mask your heat and transmission signatures," she said. "We shall be there shortly."
She deployed six ships from the side of the Aurelius. The Libras were agile and fast. They looked like insects, with their small cockpit heads that flared out into a swollen bulb that made up the rest of the ship. Each Libra carried a high density darkspace bomb as its payload. The ships couldn't exist in normal space, where the gravity of the bombs would crush them immediately. But in darkspace, where the rules were different and not yet fully understood, they could maneuver and dash as freely as birds. Due to the nature of their mission, there was one human pilot aboard, each of them a volunteer. They had only one purpose.
The hologram of Claudia saluted each of them as they left the launch bay. She couldn't risk having a control transmission jammed, so these fighters were deployed instead. They were tasked with detonating against the darkspace barrier of Sanctuary, hopefully bringing it into normal space where it would be defenseless. It was a suicide mission, but these six gladly volunteered. She left them in darkspace and ordered for the Aurelius to shift into normal space.
The crew was greeted by blinding white light from their screens. It took a moment for the sensors to adjust to the brightness of the red dwarf. The star dimmed to an orange and red ball on their displays.
"Creating a map of the area," a technician announced. Small cameras streamed out of the capital ship. With the exception of the engine and circuitry on each camera, they were mostly transparent. Shaped like dishes, each of them gathered all the light they could. They arranged themselves in a grid throughout the proposed battlefield and shared their images with each other and the Aurelius.
Through her avatar, Claudia said, "Project onto the bridge."
She felt the material of the bridge as if the reflective polymer were a part of her skin. As they dispersed, the cameras sent individual images of what each saw, and the images were coalesced and compiled by the AI. The computers molded and projected the composite image onto the floor, chairs and walls so that it appeared as one unbroken surface that replaced the bridge. The gray of the floor and consoles turned into the black of space flecked with stars. The bridge disappeared; people sat seemingly on nothing. The only things that disturbed the landscape were the crew, their light consoles, and Claudia. To the left, the red dwarf shone brightly. At first it was a dizzying experience, seeing nothing but the stars beneath and above them, but prior combat experience showed that having a visual of their surroundings could alert the crew to things that the sensors had missed.
All around them, different ships shifted into the rendezvous location. Their entry points were scattered but they adjusted in normal space, firing their thrusters as they positioned themselves in front of the Aurelius.
Claudia factored the red dwarf into her strategy. "Deploy a cluster of warheads behind the star. Keep them directed at the battlefield."
Tiny thumps sounded throughout the hull. "Warheads away," the weapons station reported.
Sylvan Winters, the new captain of the Rainier, appeared on screen. The bandage over his eye was gone and fresh skin covered the wound on his forehead. "High Adjudicant, the ships have all assembled," he said.
Claudia scanned the list of gathered ships for the Umbra, but it was absent and out of range. There was no choice but to continue without Alan.
She surveyed her fleet. All told, over fifty ships had gathered for this battle with the Sanctum. There were ships and agents that were too far away to make it here on time, but the majority of the Einhart was present. A part of her worried about bunching them all here in one location, but another part said that it was necessary. Better to finish things with one decisive stroke than to let it drag on. Some of the ships were pulled out of engagements they had on other planets, and their sudden departure would be noticed by the empire. She needed to act now.
"Ma'am, increase in darkspace disturbance. We've never seen anything its size before."
"Order Libras One and Two to engage," she said. "Stagger their hits and display the video." She was opening the battle by sacrificing two of her own.
Claudia accessed the feed from the darkspace probes. From a distance it looked like a purple sphere, but as the first Libra accelerated towards it, the sphere became a wall. For a second their darkspace fields merged. A moment later, a wave of force appeared as the Libra was engulfed by the bomb it carried on its back. The explosion destroyed one of the probes and Claudia switched to another probe to continue watching.
The Libra punched a hole through Sanctuary's darkspace bubble, revealing glimpses of clouds beneath it, but the bubble was quickly repairing itself. Purple light cascaded over the damage.
The second Libra impacted on the other side of the sphere, much sooner than expected. If the distance the Libra needed to travel was so little, how large was the object? Claudia and the rest of the bridge watched as the same happened again. The force was enough to create another hole, but the damage didn't last.
She noticed something about the process. The waves of purple energy that rebuilt the holes in the darkspace bubble had come from the bottom and streamed up in pulses. 
Undoubtedly Sanctuary noticed the attack. She maybe had enough time for one more stratagem. "Order the remaining four Libras to attack the lower half of the sphere. Split Sanctuary's shield into quadrants and time for simultaneous impact."
One Libra stopped in front of the shield that came hurtling towards it. The other two kept pace to the side and the final one exhausted its fuel to overtake it. She displayed a timer to synchronize their attacks.
The four collided with the bottom of the darkspace shield at the same time. The explosions knocked out the lower half of the sphere. The upper part grew dimmer and faded. The object suddenly disappeared from darkspace.
In its place, a shockwave of gravity rippled throughout normal space, shaking even the Aurelius. Einhart scientists would never have a guessed an object so large could have shifted into darkspace, but they didn't have access to the research done on Abyssinia and other facilities.
There were rumors that surrounded Sanctuary. It was said that those sent as emissaries from the worlds the empire conquered were kept there and could never leave, to guarantee the cooperation of their respective homeworlds. This was true. Others had said that it was a dark place, a land of fire and ash, for the emperor, cruel as he was, could only exist in a world devoid of life. This was not true.
Even though Sanctuary was bombed out of darkspace, its atmosphere was still intact. It was the size of a small moon, but it wasn't round; it was shaped like a disk. On top of the disk was a lush forest that covered much of its surface. Rivers flowed through the trees, dropping off at the edges of the world and disappearing into mist. Concentric circles of buildings cut rings through the forest. They all leaned in towards the center, as if paying homage to the palace and its citadel that rose high above the trees.
The underside of the disk was a mirror image of the top, but in the place of the forest was dull metal. A spire clung to the middle like a stalactite, a reduced reflection of the citadel above it. Smoke poured out of the spire, evidence of the damage caused by the Libras. 
Innumerable launch bays studded the bottom of the disk. Their hatches opened. Sanctum fighters, sleek with forward-sweeping wings, streamed out of them at such a rate that it seemed like an unending river of black. The fighters splashed through the water that cascaded off the side, the droplets freezing into ice as they broke through Sanctuary's atmosphere and entered space.
The ambush had probably caught the Sanctum unprepared, Claudia thought, and it would be a little longer before reinforcements arrived. She would press her advantage. "Launch Vespine fighters and prepare silos A through J. Target their fighters as they approach. Engage closer to Sanctuary and minimize collateral damage." A spear appeared in her avatar's hand.
Second Medium Fitzgerald Simmons recorded the orders and sent it through the chain of command, down to the conductors who would direct each missile individually. War suited his bellicose personality and he found the prospect of revenge on the imperial homeworld exciting. The source of his bitterness would be expunged after this battle, either by the destruction of Sanctuary or by his own death. "Missiles away," he said.
Ten cylinders launched from the Aurelius, along with another salvo from the other ships. The cylinders opened mid-flight and ten fission missiles split from each, each steered by a weapons specialist and guided towards targets marked by the AI for the greatest damage radius.
The individual Sanctum fighters launched their own salvo of plasma. Lines of blue and white streaked across space. They splashed against the missiles, melting them into globs of harmless metal. But a few missiles made it through. When they impacted, bursts of red and white that rivaled the light of the red dwarf bloomed in a row in front of Sanctuary. A large swath of the automated fighters were vaporized in the flash of heat and light, but for each that fell two more came to take its place.
 "Vespines and first wave, engage." Claudia put Simmons in charge of the front lines and left a quarter of her processing power to assist him. The rest she directed to the movement of her ships across the three-dimensional grid of the battlefield. The Sanctum fighters were unmanned drones, and her pilots were far better than any computer. But the empire had the advantage of numbers, and if she let the battle drag on for too long the Einhart would be overwhelmed.
Battle was joined as the Vespines and drones met. Skirmishes changed into individual dogfights as the Vespines peppered the drones with bullets. The Sanctum fighters responded with lines of plasma.
Claudia paid attention to what happened when fallen ships on both sides impacted the atmosphere of Sanctuary. Nothing made it through. Though she saw bits of the forests and palace underneath the clouds, when anything hit the edge of its atmosphere it glanced off with a shimmer and rebounded back onto the battlefield. They would need to find a way past that shield.
"Weapons!" she said, hailing the officer in charge of the armaments. "Take the warheads out of the red dwarf's orbit. Use the star's gravity to slingshot the missiles towards the back of Sanctuary. Notify me when they're ten seconds away from impact."
"Aye, ma'am!"
She continued to monitor the front of the battle. Reinforcements were needed in a quadrant. The last of the Vespines were being shot down there, their hulls gutted and opened to the void of space.
"Enkidu, reinforce. Launch full complement and hold the front line. Repel and push." She marked the location and gave instructions to their onboard AI. 
A large ship, boxy and rectangular, crossed in front of the Aurelius. Ports opened along its four lateral surfaces. "First salvo away," its captain reported. Thin missiles launched from it in waves, leaving trails of white smoke and obscuring the ship from view. While packing less firepower, these missiles dodged around debris with precision thrusts as they approached their targets.
A monitor reported, "Three inbound signatures from darkspace, ma'am."
Claudia turned her mind to the disturbances in normal space. They were appearing in a triangle around Sanctuary. The accuracy of the empire's shifts from dark to normal space was knowledge the Einhart should acquire, she thought. But their tactics were too simple. Why a defensive formation around Sanctuary when they could've deployed behind her armada? What were they waiting for?
"Ten seconds till fission warhead impact, ma'am," a weapons technician said. "Trajectory is warped by incoming darkspace shift."
She would deal with the questions later. "Split missiles into two groupings. For one group, adjust course and keep them on Sanctuary. Keep the second group targeted on the rift in space and reduce their speed."
"Understood, High Adjudicant."
She turned to another section of the bridge. "Monitor," she said, "deploy our remaining cameras in loose formation here." She marked a location near the red dwarf. "Give me a screen."
"Ma'am," the monitor responded, "we've only lost a few cameras and have adequate views of the field."
Her avatar raised her eyebrows once, and the man who dared question the High Adjudicant quickly spun back in his seat, red-faced, and launched the cameras.
The rifts in normal space closed. In their place were three Javelin-class warships that emerged simultaneously. They were the same as the Edict; two diamonds that intersected each other, giving them the shape of two pyramids stacked base to base, their simple form a symbol of the Sanctum Empire and the power it had.
They had already charged their turrets; the trenches where the ship plating intersected brimmed with blue plasma. 
One of them never had the chance to fire. The group of five missiles crashed into its side. They maintained their speed as they blew through the shield and drilled deep into the ship's core. Powerless, the Javelin listed towards Sanctuary, its lights fading to black. The missiles inside detonated. In a shower of metal and plasma, the Javelin exploded. The throneworld's shields glimmered from the force of the impact, but recovered.
Claudia dedicated one AI to the guidance of the remaining five missiles. One was shot down, four of them impacted. Sanctuary's shield lit up in a rainbow of colors around the whole disk, then disappeared. It was down.
"Warships, fire at Sanctuary! Vespines, clear a path." Upon her order, the whole of the Einhart fleet was hidden behind a cloud of exhaust as missiles launched; their numbers like drops of rain, all headed towards the same target. The barrage of artillery was so thick that even the red dwarf was darkened behind the wall of projectiles.
The Sanctum drones split off from their sorties and threw themselves into the trajectories of the incoming missiles. The two remaining Javelin warships unleashed their own counterattack. The plasma they shot wasn't globular, but concentrated and enhanced into fine beams that stretched across the field of combat. With a single burst, the beams cut a zigzag pattern through the missiles, Vespines and drones alike, leaving a wake of wreckage behind them. The reach of a beam extended past even the fighting and hit the Aurelius.
"Maintain position," Claudia said. The plasma beam glanced off the prow shield.
"Shields at 93.6 percent. Recharging from engine three," a defense technician said.
Claudia was more concerned with the damage to Sanctuary. Only two missiles made it through, creating burning craters in the forest. But with those two missiles, she and the Einhart knew that Sanctuary could be breached. A cheer rose throughout the fleet and she felt the morale of every warship and fighter rise.
Their joy was short-lived. The two remaining Javelin-class ships were beginning to recharge their plasma. The buildup along the trenches glowed white and hot, illuminating the spaces in between the trilateral sheets. All the light concentrated on one point on the Javelin and was released. Two beams of plasma sped at the amassed Einhart.
"Evasive maneuvers," Claudia said. The Aurelius tilted to one side as its engines came to life. But the mass of the flagship was great and moving it took too much time. The plasma sliced cleanly through the two ships in front and shook the Aurelius as it smashed into its shields.
"Shields at 13 percent. Lost communications with Enkidu and Pleroma," Simmons reported.
Another flare appeared off to the starboard side as the remaining beam cut through another set of ships. "Verum, Baldur and Delphi aren't responding." The euphemism was unneeded. Claudia knew the moment when the plasma blasted through their shields, tore through their hulls and ignited the oxygen that flowed through them.
"Tighten matrix of extra cameras, concave formation," she ordered. "Remaining ships, fire at will; focus on the Javelins." Sanctuary was their target, but so far it had only deployed individual fighters. The Javelins were a greater threat and needed to be removed first. But how much time did she have? How much time before the shields were up again, before Sanctuary could power its engines, before more reinforcements arrived?
Claudia turned her attention to the cameras. They were scattered loosely in front of the red dwarf. She felt as if each camera was a marble that she could roll and stop across the canvas of space. Each was maneuvered and placed with precision as the ship translated the impulses of her brain into kinetic movement.
She started with the edges, building a large ring of cameras. Each of their lenses faced out, catching and bending the rays of light emitted by the red dwarf. The cameras themselves were stabilized by electric beams between them.
