She built another ring of cameras inside the first, angling the camera lenses in ever slightly, pulling the light into an array that grew ever denser. The light bounced off the scattered cameras, forming a luminous film between the lenses. She continued with the pattern until it was a solid sheet of curved glass.
When she was done, a dome had formed in front of the star. It was a formation of lenses, held in place by electricity, their shared location data, and minute thrusts from their engines. She tilted the formation and outer lenses channeled the sunlight into the dome. The arrangement of curved glass magnified it into a beam that burned through the nearest group of Sanctum fighters that tried to dismantle it. For every camera the fighters melted, another would appear to take its place.
Claudia drew a line on the battle screen shared by the Einhart. She gave her fighters and ships fifteen seconds to escape the proposed path of the beam. The Vespines would make it out; they were designed to move from engagement to engagement and were fast. However, the Pinewell, an older ship that had seen many battles, wouldn't have such an easy time. The bulk of the ship stood in between the impromptu magnifying glass and the Javelin-class ship it was supposed to destroy. The Pinewell's engines glowed, trying to gain speed, but its inertia was too much to overcome in the few seconds they had.
Claudia opened a line to the Pinewell. The captain appeared on the screen; his face was calm and controlled, but a layer of sweat had formed on his brow. "Evacuate and close port side airlocks," she commanded.
"Yes, High Adjudicant." He forwarded the order to his crew. The screen went dark.
She would give them five more seconds. The Javelin she was aiming for would unleash its plasma soon and they would suffer more casualties than just the Pinewell if that happened.
"Orient the lenses and set focus on the Javelin," she said. "Fleet, synchronize attacks. Get past their shields."
The cameras shifted their position, moving in unison, turning into a rounded mirror with the diameter of a starship. As they caught the light, each camera magnified and turned the light towards the center, where it burst forth in a beam of concentrated sunlight.
The light beam vaporized the left half of the Pinewell. The edges of the metal glowed bright orange and then faded. Thanks to its quick-acting crew, there was no vented atmosphere or explosion.
The solar beam hit the Javelin head-on, focusing on one of its side trenches where plasma gathered. The Javelin's shields diffused the light, scattering it into separate rays that spread out behind it in a rainbow. The shields glimmered purple and green as they diverted the attack, becoming thinner with every passing second. When the missiles impacted the other side of the Javelin, the shields shimmered once and then died.
With the Javelin's shields down, the beam impacted the edge of the ship. It melted a hole through its side and pulled the gathering plasma into the inner decks. The light burned through reinforced plating and men indiscriminately. It only encountered resistance as it entered the crystal core that powered the ship. The crystal was the same shape as the ship except in miniature, rotating on its axis surrounded by an electrical field. The field kept the core in place and diverted energy to where it was needed, at this moment to repower the failed shields. The light didn't affect it; the core only refracted the light into millions of diamond dots against the walls of its chamber. But the heat from the rays made it inside. The pillars and containment cages that kept the crystal in place glowed orange. They elongated, dripped, and then flowed, as they turned from solid to liquid. The crystal fell out of place and the light continued on its original path.
From the bridge of the Aurelius, Claudia watched as the beam entered one side of the Javelin and exited out the other. Plasma pooled into the holes, as if trying to patch them, but it was too late. The Javelin tipped over, listing until it was almost on its side. The crystal core was displaced from its stasis field. As it hit the sides of the containment chamber, it released its energy, unchecked and unrestrained, into the rest of the ship. In one brilliant flash of light it appeared illuminated as if it were a second sun, and then it was gone, vaporized.
The battle was now in the Einhart's favor. They sustained casualties from the combined assault of the Sanctum fighters and Javelins, but they had survived with more than half their ships. Their newest priority was to prevent Sanctuary from retreating into darkspace. Considering its mass, similar to a moon or small planet, it didn't have enough time to achieve the speed necessary to make the shift. Then again, the empire had done things with darkspace that the Einhart had never thought possible.
She divided the fleet into two battalions. "First battalion, focus assault on Sanctuary. Disable their shields and darkspace drive. Keep them here." A group of warships detached and moved to their designated positions. These were heavier cruisers, built with copious amounts of plating and additional darkspace engines for shields that could absorb more damage. They weren't fast, but made up for it with weapons that could lay siege from orbit.
"Second battalion, target remaining Javelin. I want to see it crash into Sanctuary."
"Aye, ma'am!" their captains responded.
These ships were agile and smaller, good against the plasma lances from the Javelin. She would leave the rest to them, with one last gift. The cameras couldn't take much more of the heat from the red dwarf; it wasn't how they were meant to be used. But they had enough to sustain one more blast. She adjusted the location of the cameras and shifted the focus of their beam on the final Javelin. The glass and parts of the cameras fused together. The final beam was weaker, but it cut through the fighters defending the Javelin and gave the Einhart the window they needed.
Claudia maneuvered the Aurelius between both battalions. The field of stars in front of her shifted as they veered to the right. She would be able to assist with the fighting on both fronts, but most importantly, it gave her access to the least defended part of Sanctuary. An opening appeared between the Vespines and fighters engaged in their dogfights, between the larger warships as they converged onto their designated locations.
The AIs that were connected to Claudia's mind felt an imbalance in the chemicals that floated between her neurons. This was a degree of emotion they had never detected before in the High Adjudicant, and the AI were wary. They reasoned that Batten, the High Adjudicant's homeworld, still stood, and such emotion wasn't warranted. But the source of her emotion wasn't related to the people she led. It went deeper, rooted in a place the AIs couldn't understand. They informed her that emotions may be clouding her judgment, that her scans were showing abnormally high activity in the amygdalae, where her memories were stored and retrieved. But she dismissed their concerns with a wave of her mind, and the AIs became like pollen blown away by a gust of wind. She had absolute control, as she needed in times of war, and she would see her will done.
All of the launch bays opened on the Aurelius. This was an impressive sight, for seldom were they open, and rarely was the Aurelius seen in its full glory. Flaps that hid the complete armament of the capital ship of the Einhart opened into the vacuum of space. From these hatches poked warheads, missiles, darkspace bombs, and some experimental weaponry Dr. Guren had not had time to fully test.
Though she did not gamble, she would bet it all on this.
"Fire," she told the bridge.
A volley of projectiles, one fired after the other, flew from the Aurelius. The first to hit were the light-based weapons. They pinged off the regenerated shield of the throneworld like scattered rain. But it was weakened with every hit, and as the rest of the projectiles collided, the shield collapsed in a burst of color. It was time for Sanctuary to burn.
The first of the acid-tipped rockets crashed into the fields around the palace, their course diverted and warped by some unknown force. They rendered swaths of land barren as they swept through, melting the trees and soil into smoking puddles. Claudia watched with cold eyes, awaiting the results of the next barrage.
She waited, but it never came. As the missiles approached Sanctuary, each one simply vanished into the clouds. None detonated.
"Ma'am, sensors are detecting a large object rapidly ascending from Sanctuary's atmosphere," a monitor said. "It seems to have a hybrid darkspace and normal space signature."
Claudia's eyes narrowed as her plan was thwarted. "Hybrid? How can it exist between both states at once? How does it get enough speed to shift?" Claudia asked. The AIs didn't know, but they were keen on finding out.
"Incoming transmission from a ship. It calls itself the Divine Will," the monitor said.
"Accept," Claudia said.
Seth, First Prince of the Sanctum, appeared on the screen. Even in battle, he was dressed in blue, purple and black ceremonial robes. His cold eyes and smooth features looked as if they were chiseled from marble. The prince's enlarged head filled up one wall of the Aurelius, though it was still smaller than his ego.
"Welcome to Sanctuary, Claudia," he said. The crew on the bridge winced as he addressed her by name, though their ears were intoxicated by his voice. "And my thanks for bringing the entire fleet of the Einhart here. We could not have asked for a better gift." From the sky of throneworld rose a mass of clouds. It left an empty spot behind it, exposing the palace and its citadel. Claudia saw a flash of purple at the top of the citadel before it became hidden again.
The mass of clouds continued to ascend, seemingly slowly, until she saw the trails of vapor stream out beneath it like a white waterfall. As it broke through the upper layers of the atmosphere, the remaining condensation turned to ice and scattered around the Divine Will.
The ship was like nothing Claudia had seen before. It was visible, yet seemed almost translucent. A gossamer film covered every surface of the Divine Will, similar to the boundaries generated around ships when they shifted to darkspace. It was unlike any other Sanctum ship, which were normally geometric and precise in their design. This ship was round, with staggered sheets of thin plating that served as its armor. Between the plates there were gaps, making it look like a flower that was about to bloom. And from these she saw a sliver of another structure; a thin and long spike hidden in the center like a pistil. Other than that, it seemed hollow on the inside. It was deceptively simple, but all its surfaces were covered in that iridescent sheen that made it seem like it should've been in darkspace.
Claudia wondered how it existed between the two dimensions. And where did her battery of missiles go?
Seth answered. "What I want to show you requires a large amount of matter, which you were so kind to donate. We could always use dark matter for the singularity cannon, but I am one for poetic justice." He smiled with his mouth, yet the mirth did not reach his eyes. "But where are my manners? Let us drink," he said, raising a glass filled with a dark liquid. "A toast, to all the worlds you have damned. To all the worlds you have denied the salvation of the empire." He downed it in one gulp and threw the glass aside. It shattered into a thousand pieces unseen. He gave one more sneer. His face winked out of existence on the bridge, replaced by stars. 
The Aurelius had been exhausted. Its armory had been emptied from the last salvo. Only now was the gravity of Claudia's decision starting to become clear to her. With the knowledge she had at the time, she had made the right choice. But her worst fear, the fear that she was going to let down the Einhart, ate at her. Thankfully, her avatar didn't show it and her body, suspended in fluid, couldn't betray her thoughts.
"Attach probes to missiles and fire one each from ships that have munitions remaining," she said.
A few missiles launched from the assembled ships. All the missiles disappeared as they neared the Divine Will. Claudia kept note of every fluctuation, and when they vanished into the void around the Sanctum ship, she had an idea of what kind of weapon the Sanctum had created.
"Ma'am, darkspace signatures are changing." 
"Prep thrusters for evasive maneuvers. Bridge and crew, prepare." she said. She turned to Simmons. "Do we have any more ships in darkspace? Any more Libras?" she asked.
"None, ma'am. All ships have been deployed and are engaged in normal space," Simmons responded.
The Divine Will oriented itself towards the Aurelius, the spike pointing straight at them. Electricity crackled around its tip, forming a spherical cage. Darkness appeared within the cage, amorphous and fluid. It blocked out the stars and seemed to absorb their light into itself.
"Spacetime fluctuations," a monitor reported. "Isolated readings originating from the Divine Will, ma'am."
The dark mass grew larger, straining against its electric shackles. The empire had managed to turn the black hole into a weapon, and it was aimed straight at the Aurelius. 
Nearby ships saw the threat to the High Adjudicant and arranged themselves in a defensive formation around her. They fired a cluster of their remaining missiles, but when they approached Seth's ship, each veered off course, sucked into the gravitational field generated by the miniature black hole. With every absorbed projectile the black hole grew in size.
The completed black hole detached from the tip of the singularity cannon, suspended like a bubble in the air. A pulse appeared at the tip of the Divine Will. With a surge of electricity, the black hole flew towards the Aurelius and the ships grouped in front of it. It passed through shields, plating and electronics unimpeded; the only remnant of their existence was a final image imprinted on its event horizon.
As it ate through the ships that formed the protective blockade, its radius increased. The void pulled larger swaths of matter into itself. The Aurelius had already shifted position, but the dark orb still clipped its side and sheared a wing off. Claudia felt it as if she had lost one of her limbs; there was a flash of pain before the nerves went dead. In the wake of the black hole, there was no debris or crew that floated out into space; the black hole had sucked those in as it went by.
"Darkspace engines four and five have been lost. Shields at maximum operability of 72 percent," a monitor announced. 
The void had also absorbed a large number of the cameras as it passed through. Without their shared vision, the panorama of space disappeared from the bridge, limiting visibility to what each monitor could see on their screen. The nebulas and astral formations reverted to sterile whites and grays.
Claudia's avatar clutched her arm. "Free formation dispersal. Give it multiple targets and erratic trajectories."
The other Javelin had fallen during Seth's attack, leaving only his ship and the drones. But she didn't know how to counter the Divine Will. Any weapons they threw at it would only add to the size of the black hole, and dodging it would require luck, which Claudia didn't believe in. Achieving the speed necessary for the shift to darkspace wasn't possible either; their retreating ships would be too easy to target.
It didn't matter, Claudia decided.
The Divine Will was preparing another black hole at the tip of its singularity cannon. Claudia came across one name that was not available to the rest of the fleet, the Umbra, belonging to her other Second Medium. Where was Alan now, when she needed him most?

Chapter 40

"I'd really prefer it if you didn't," Alan said. Prefer? He was the Second Medium. He didn't use such words anymore.
<When we left Phalos, you said I could fight. So I will.>
"I know what I said Ashra, but I'm here to protect you. The empire wants you and the Einhart will kill you. I don't know where you'll be safe, but space is vast. We'll find a place; just stay low for now. Please?"
Alan hated the phrase I don't know, but that seemed to be all he could come up with recently. Before he met the princess, the future had been easy to understand and the days had been easy to pass. But with Ashra on his mind, he became uncertain, he doubted. He always imagined the worst scenarios, and was mortified when some had come true, after Ashra had told them of what had transpired on Phalos. Mortified. He hadn't felt such a strong emotion in a long time.
Ashra was standing inside the open comet and didn't respond. He moved his hands over hers. "Thrusters are linked to each hand. In case I can't come back," he said, and Ashra turned her head away, as if she didn't want to see the possibility. He grabbed her shoulder and she faced him. "In case I can't come back," he repeated, "there's a week's worth of supplies at the bottom and an emergency beacon linked to some friends back in the hub. I'm asking you to keep yourself from being noticed, but you are no longer the girl I found on Galea. The choice is yours." He squeezed her hand. "But I'll come back. I promise."
<You promise?> Her face was stern.
"Promise."
Ashra smiled. He kissed her once on the forehead, then lowered the lid, watching it seal with a hiss. Alan slapped the sides of the comet, making sure all the parts were secure. She seemed too small for it; he could barely see the top of her head through the viewport. But she smiled, and he kept that image in his heart as he loaded the rear launcher with her comet. He wanted to send her away now, but he would have to wait until they were back in normal space.
"Fluctuations in darkspace," Aki reported.
"Coming," Alan said. With one last glance at Ashra, he ran to the cockpit and sat down at the center console. "What do we have?"
"It looks like a ship, underneath that huge mess. The computer doesn't know what's going on, but estimates suggest that it's stuck in the shift between normal and darkspace." 
It looked like a dark cloud to Alan. The edges were made of orbs that swirled with the absence of color, flowing along the surface. As they moved back and forth, Alan could make out an iridescent shape underneath, similar to a ship that was making the shift between dimensions. One of the orbs moved to the front of the ship, where it stayed for a moment before being shot off, disappearing into, what Alan guessed, was normal space.
Unbidden, a message appeared across his light console. 

Take it out.
-C

"Yes ma'am," Alan whispered to himself. He turned to his teammates. "The High Adjudicant wants this thing gone. We don't have enough firepower to take it head on, and we don't have weapons that function in darkspace."
"Calculating boarding options," Aki said. Trajectories appeared on her console.
"Leave the weapons to me," Argus said, excited to finally use the one light-based weapon the ship had. He aimed the laser cannon and pulled the trigger. 
The green laser hit the edge of the Umbra's shift bubble. Instead of passing through the bubble, it traveled along an elliptical track as it curved with the boundary between normal and darkspace. He fired multiple shots, each one angled slightly differently. The lasers slowed, turning from streams of light into discrete green blobs, each encased by its own darkspace bubble. 
The end result was a kaleidoscope of green light that encircled the ship, blocking out the darkspace that surrounded them. Argus left a small opening at the front of the ship so Alan could still see.
Aki tried to make sense of the information the computer was displaying. "Those masses seem to be the seeds of black holes. They're stable in darkspace, but activated once they're brought out into normal space."
"Avoid them, got it," Alan said. "How're we getting aboard?"
"We'll need to match their phase," Aki said.
"Like we're shifting?"
Aki nodded.
"That leaves only one option then." He looked at Argus. "Argus, you know what to do. Aim our darkspace engine at their ship bridge, at that spike in the center."
The big man took control of the darkspace engine and adjusted its position. "Do we get to press the big button now?" he asked with a grin.
Alan nodded. "Computer, the Uchida sonatas." He would never have a chance to hear them aboard the Umbra again. 
As music trickled through the cockpit, the three pressed the small hexagons at the bottom right of their light consoles simultaneously. They heard a click come from the lower deck of the Umbra. The darkspace engine shot forward, still tethered to the ship by a tendril of black electricity. It avoided the laser masses while shedding its containment fullerene piece by piece. The black core wobbled as it lost stability and broke through the gap left by Argus. It cleared the bubble and would make contact with the Divine Will in a second. 
"Shift," Alan said.
The darkspace core flashed once then disappeared, expending its energy in a blast that tore a hole through the hull of the Divine Will. A rainbow of colors rippled across the Umbra as the ship crashed into the hole the core made. 
As the world shifted to the solid colors of normal space, a series of comets launched from the rear of the ship. One contained Ashra; the rest were decoys. They jetted away from the battle, objects so small they could've been confused for debris.
The front of the Umbra emerged within the hull of Divine Will as both ships phased in and out of darkspace. The lasers Argus had fired, freed from their dimensional prison, flew throughout the bridge of the Divine Will. Some of the bubbles maintained their form, while others burst as they made contact solid matter. They struck control panels, engineers and soldiers without prejudice. Those that survived ducked under seats and consoles as the lasers scorched the ground next to them. 
A weapons technician looked at Seth. "My Lord, if our shielding is compromised, we will be unable to maintain our position between dark and normal space." His eyes glazed over as he scanned information through his neural implant. "The seeds will be activated once we're forced into normal space. Ground forces report that the darkspace array is almost fixed on Sanctuary, but due to our proximity, the throneworld will be in danger from the seeds until it can shift."
Seth danced across the bridge in his robes, dodging the lasers as they burst around him. "Execute final order for the ship then prepare for reentry into Sanctuary," he said, weaving his body in between beams of light. Deep in his mind, he felt the emperor stir inside his cocoon on Sanctuary. His heart glowed with love for his father; he would do all he could to keep him safe and fulfill his duty as a son.
"Your will be done, First Prince." The technician accessed the network through his neural implant and continued working under his console.
On the floor below Seth, the Umbra's door flew open. After explosives weakened the seal, Argus ripped the door off and held it as a shield. Alan and Aki got behind him. Much of the Divine Will's bridge was in ruins, but as soon as they stepped out, they were pelted with plasma fire by the remaining Sanctum soldiers.
Alan had already primed an Ardor before they came out. He threw the small ball over the door. It hung for a moment, before its silver surface receded and the sphere imploded. The lower level was instantly awash in flames. Argus slammed the door into the ground and leaned into it to keep it upright. They huddled close to each other, Aki sandwiched between Argus and Alan. The fire parted as it hit the door and came back together as it passed behind them.
On the upper level, Seth shielded himself. Distracted by the explosion, he didn't see a laser that came from behind. It splashed upon his back, leaving scorched cloth and flesh. When he stretched to touch the wound, the skin tore and a trickle of blood came forth. He ignored the pain as he watched the last of the black hole seeds launch. One sped towards the Aurelius as a diversion. Another cluster shot past the lines of battle. 
He watched the sea of flames churn below on the lower level. When the bridge was destroyed, the ship would be forced to shift into normal space and its shields would dissipate. Without a way to navigate, he was trapped in a vessel that couldn't move, and the First Prince despised anything that reduced his freedom. As the heat subsided he pushed his guards forward. "Take care of them." He stayed at the master console, trying to divert the remaining power towards reentering Sanctuary.
Behind Argus, Aki looked up and Alan followed her gaze. A flurry of footsteps sounded like rain on metal. They saw a group of soldiers rush down the stairs. Judging from their efficient steps and the way they carried their weaponry, these soldiers were well-trained. Argus pushed the door across the floor and took steady strides forward as Alan and Aki popped out from behind him to shoot. Three guards fell to their bullets, but the others quickly found cover of their own behind the burnt consoles.
Alan had a hand on Argus's hip, guiding him towards the opposite bank of consoles where they could get more solid cover. Aki kicked aside charred corpses as they made their way. Argus's impromptu shield was getting battered as plasma splashed against it.
When they reached the consoles, Alan and Aki went out first and hid behind them. Argus kicked the shield forward, flattening a guard with its weight. He rolled to the side as superheated bolts flew past where he was standing just moments ago.
Alan saw Aki calibrating her sniper rifle. "At this range?" he asked. "Aren't we too close?"
"Not for what I have in mind," she said. "Give me a target."
Alan popped his head up and ducked as blue-white lances whizzed overhead.
"Thanks," Aki said as she tracked their source. She braced herself against the bottom of the console, lying flat on the floor with her head and shoulders up. The rest of the rifle was balanced on the ground between her legs. 
She pulled the trigger. The distance was short but there was a lot in the way. The bullet drilled through layers of metal and electronics and burst out the other side. When the blood splattered on the wall, she knew she hit her mark.
The final guard retreated up the stairs. Though he hated to leave battle, there was no one left to protect the First Prince. He needed to inform the prince of the situation and possibly prepare the shuttle to secure the First Prince's escape.
Alan followed the guard up the flight of stairs. He lost sight of him for a moment as he went up. When he reached the top, the guard seemed to be floating, his feet dangling in the air. An arm held him up by his neck, extending from the back of the captain's chair that stood on a raised dais.
 "I ordered you to fight." The man was raised higher as the figure stood up. With his height, voice, and the ease with which he lifted the guard, Alan knew who the man was in an instant. But before he could shoot, a flurry of bullets whizzed past his head. Argus had already taken the first shots.
The prince spun around and held the guard as a shield. The bullets impacted the man's torso and shook his body. Without a second thought, Seth tossed him over the side of the railing and rushed forward. Alan took aim and joined in the fusillade.
Seth appeared in one place, only to appear in another a moment later, closer than before. But he left a trail of blood as he dashed from spot to spot. Soon his movements became slower and Alan could track him with his eyes. Alan fired a shot, watching as the bullet sailed towards where the prince was standing. It only went through air as he disappeared.
Argus fired another round, anticipating Seth's position by the blood left across the floor. His bullet found its mark, hitting the prince in chest. Argus saw Seth's eyes widen as he felt the pain. A moment later he was gone, knocked over the railing by the force of the impact.
When they peered over the ledge to see where he had fallen, they saw nothing but a pool of blood that disappeared under the stairs. Then they heard a scream.
Unseen by the trio, as Seth fell and his heart slowed, he offered an apology. <Father,> he thought in his mind, <I am unable to fulfill the duty you gave me, to rule in your stead, to protect Sanctuary and to further the empire. I fear you are in danger, and it brings me shame to know I brought this upon you. I sacrifice myself to you in dedication.>
He felt the stirrings of the emperor's mind grow stronger, and he took that as permission. He landed on one of his arms. It broke, but he didn't mind anymore. The guard that he had thrown over was still alive, his breath ragged. Seth grabbed his leg. The guard, barely conscious, was jolted awake by the searing pain he felt coming from his calf.
Merging is a delicate process, requiring mastery of oneself and dominion over the other, Seth remembered his father teaching him. The cocoon protects and contains the merge, and time is necessary. Time is required to organize and place the cells in their proper position, to vanquish the lesser mind, to figure out what to keep and what to discard. But Seth didn't have time. His one heart was losing the blood he needed to stay alive. So he grabbed whatever bioorganic mass he could and began the merge, without a cocoon and without preparation.
The man's calf and Seth's hand melded into each other. The guard's nerves were hijacked one by one. He screamed in pain, but Seth continued, utilizing the ability he gained from his father. The screams stopped when the prince collapsed the vocal chords. The man's heart was used to power Seth's body instead.
Half a man now extended where Seth's hand used to be. Its head lolled to and fro as he commanded the man's hands to latch onto any available biomass. He flung his arm with the attached body around the lower level, picking up the corpses of his guards and former crew. He absorbed their organs, skin, bone and muscle to feed the growth of his new form, discarding the burnt parts he didn't need.
Alan saw the fleshy appendages whip around on the lower level. "We gotta move," he said. 
On the upper level, the three ran past the dais, headed through a set of blast doors, and found themselves in a long corridor that linked the bridge to the rest of the ship. Despite the damage they had done, it seemed like there was still power. Their path down the corridor was guided by lights recessed into the floor and walls. They ran, not knowing where it led, and ran faster when they heard a roar behind them. It wasn't human, yet it still had the booming power that Seth's voice once possessed. It was an amplified howl made from many voices. Beneath it, they heard something wet.
Aki risked a glance back. She saw him slither across a trail of mucus, secreted by glands on his underside. Spinal columns from the bodies the prince used fused together to create a long backbone that undulated back and forth, propelling him forward. His tail left scores on the wall as it whipped around. Two muscular arms ending in sharp bone spikes dug into the ground, pulling him forward and increasing his speed. Errant limbs and unwanted fingers were excreted one by one from his skin, falling to the sides of the corridor as the prince gained on them. A vestige of Seth's face still remained on the creature's neck, its eyes closed and jaw slack. What replaced his head was a maw with rows of pointed teeth and two eyes that shone with fury.
Aki ran backwards and fired into the creature. The bullets hit their mark, but he seemed immune to pain. All they did was fuel his anger.
The three continued running, but the end of the corridor was approaching. Aki guessed that when the ship was breached, all other paths were closed by blast doors in order to seal the bridge and maintain pressure. They would have to fight here before they were forced into the corner.
The creature's hand, a single length of bone molded into a scythe, shot forward, missing Alan's face by inches. It buried itself deep into the plating of the floor. When he pulled it out, it left a ragged hole of exposed metal and wiring. Alan countered with a couple rounds from his pistol, but had to duck as the scythe swung overhead, taking a few hairs from his head with it. From his crouching position he searched, seeking to find anything exposed, anything not yet merged, but in that moment Seth's tail smashed into his torso and he flew headfirst into the side wall. He didn't move after he landed.
Aki saw him go down. Seth hunched over Alan's inert form, about to impale him with a claw. She shot a trio of bullets, shattering the scythe into pieces of bone. Seth turned around to face her. Protrusions slid under his skin and up his arm. They pushed out the bone and began to replace what was broken. She fired a few more shots and dodged his slices by weaving her body and jumping off the wall. She glanced back at Argus. "Whatever you're doing, do it fast," she said.
Argus was at the back of the corridor. He opened a canister, took out a k-mine and slammed it against the wall. "Done." He followed with a burst from his gun and Seth was forced to face him. "You owe me an Erudite," he said. Seth roared in response. Argus sidestepped and tried to flank him, but the prince was fast and turned with his every step.
 With Seth's attention elsewhere, Aki went to Alan's limp body and pulled him back down the corridor, towards the bridge. She used the trail of mucus to hasten her progress. She caught sight of Argus with his back faced towards them. Seth was positioned in front of the wall that separated the ship from space.
Argus fired with his right hand. His left hand held a k-mine firmly in its grasp, his fingers creating indents in the soft plastic. Seth lunged forward with his remaining bladed arm. Argus dropped his gun and grabbed the blade as it came towards him, cutting his fingers as Seth strove to it through his chest.
The force was too great even for Argus to stop. Though he managed to move it away from his heart, the scythe still went through his abdomen and out the other end. Blood dripped from its tip and splashed onto the floor.
Argus didn't move. His other hand was pressed against the chest of the beast. Underneath it, the k-mine slowly spread out on Seth's skin, blending in with his mottled colors. 
Argus smiled, a line of blood running past his lips. He grabbed the bone that protruded out of his body. With a twist, he snapped it off between his hands. Before Seth could react, he dropped to the floor, grabbed his pistol and shot one bullet past the prince. Seth reared up, about to finish him off with his regrown scythe.
The k-mine on the wall exploded. The blast tore through layers of metal until it reached space. The hole expanded as the vacuum sucked out the air inside. The force tore the gun from Argus's hand and it flew out of the breach. 
With his tail streaming behind him like a banner, Seth stabbed the remnants of his arms into the ground, resisting the gale that threatened to pull him out of the ship.
Argus grabbed onto one of the holes in the ground, straining with all his might to keep himself from getting pulled out of the hole as well. But his mission wasn't finished yet. The air whipped around him and made it difficult, but his target was close. He removed the bone impaled through his stomach and threw it at the prince.
The flat side of the scythe collided with Seth's chest, detonating the k-mine glued to his skin. His bone scythes shattered and the prince was blown backwards. With one final screech he was sucked out through the hole and into the emptiness of space. Argus wanted to continue watching, but he heard a voice from above.
"I can't hold him!" Aki was further up, clinging to the grating with one hand while holding Alan with the other. He was still unconscious. He hung limp in her arm, which was quickly losing its grip. With a yell, she aimed him at Argus and let go.
Argus looked up and tracked Alan's trajectory. The wind made it difficult, and Alan fell farther to the side than either of them had predicted. Argus stretched out and extended his arm. He caught the bottom of Alan's shirt as he slid past. Argus pulled him in with all of his muscles, hugging him to his chest.
The nanomachines that scuttled along the interior of the Divine Will were made aware of the breach and gathered there. They patched up the hole molecule by molecule, adding the most basic layer of protection and then reinforcing it.
As the vacuum died down, Alan's eyes fluttered open. He tried moving but found he was trapped in a tight embrace by biceps the size of his head.
Argus felt him stir. "You awake, boss?" he asked. The big man sounded sleepy and his grip grew looser. 
Alan pulled himself away. His hands and armor were slick with blood, blood that wasn't his own. He got to his knees and grimaced as the world came into painful focus. He rubbed his head; there would be a bruise there for some time. 
It was only when he saw the source of the blood that he knew how badly Argus had been wounded. "Argus?" he said. He shook the big man's shoulder. "Argus?"
Argus's eyes were closed and he didn't respond.

Chapter 41

There were cracks within the glass. Drop by drop, fluid leaked out of the integration chamber. The last attack from Seth's ship missed the bridge, but several transport lines that ran along the underside of the Aurelius had been severed by the black holes. Sparks ignited the gasses that leaked out, and the resulting explosion had thrown the bridge into disarray. Claudia focused on sealing off the breached bulkheads throughout what remained of her ship while her crew picked themselves up from the ground. Some were bruised and bleeding from cuts they sustained as they crashed into control panels and seats, but all had the will to continue to fight. This is what it meant to be Einhart, she thought.
"Bulkheads have been sealed, ma'am. Repressurizing lower decks, equilibrium will be regained in two minutes," a technician said as he read the reports with his good eye. The other was covered with a bandage.
Another said, "Ma'am, the Divine Will has shifted into normal space. We've received firing solutions from Hadron and Rainier. They're requesting permission to fire."
She looked closely with the remaining cameras. The back end of another ship stuck out of the Divine Will's bridge, like a bird had wanted a flower too much and dove straight into it. When she saw it was black with four engines attached to its main booster, she knew it was Umbra. With magnification she noticed that the Divine Will had already repaired the hole the Umbra had made in its hull. "Deny," she said. "Alert me if the Divine Will starts to shift to darkspace, or some other strange readings come from it. Otherwise, do not engage."
The technician responded, but Claudia didn't hear for her mind was already elsewhere. The Aurelius managed to dodge a shot from the Divine Will right before it became visible, but sensors recorded another fluctuation in space-time. She followed their trajectory and found her cameras focused on the red dwarf that served as the backdrop to their battle. It seemed like it dimmed. She measured its luminosity. Sure enough, it wasn't as bright as it was moments before. The subtle changes grew more pronounced. In seconds, the displays had to compensate as the star went dark. 
Cracks appeared on the star's darkened surface. The cracks lengthened and shot across from pole to pole, as if dividing the land into countries. Piece by piece, chunks were pulled into the center of the star. Through the gaps, Claudia saw what had happened.
Its core was replaced by the cluster of black holes the Divine Will had shot from its singularity cannon, forcing the star into an untimely end. The outer shell of the star completely disappeared and the remaining mass collapsed and shrunk into an infinitesimally small point. 
All that remained of the star were bits of it spinning in the accretion disc. What replaced it was a black hole. It grew, feeding on the mass of the star and the ship debris that littered its surroundings.
After it had been disabled, the Pinewell had drifted closer to the red dwarf in an attempt to camouflage itself behind the emissions the star had given off. It was now being sucked into the black hole, growing shades redder as it approached the last rings of light that circled the void. Claudia watched the image of the ship freeze as it hit the event horizon; the Pinewell seemed frozen in time, stretched and distorted, but she knew what happened. Though the light couldn't make it back to the cameras, the ship had already been drawn into the singularity and was crushed into oblivion. She raised a silent salute for the fallen. But as she checked the battle log, she realized that the Pinewell still had its darkspace engine when it entered. Its density would be enough-
"Ma'am, gravity field has amplified," a technician reported.
"Channel all remaining energy to thrusters," she said. "Spread as fleetwide command. Escape is the first priority." 
She was glad her features were expressionless, or the bridge would've seen the combination of envy, disappointment, and anger that she felt as she gazed at Sanctuary. Her prize was so close, within firing distance, yet the continued existence of the Einhart depended on how fast they could escape.
The throneworld began moving as well. One half of the disc lit up in blue as its side thrusters fired. Yet it too had trouble escaping the pull of the black hole and could only maintain its position.
Simmons pored over charts. "High Adjudicant, even with the power from our remaining darkspace engines, we won't be able to outrun the gravitational field of the black hole. We might have the speed, but shifting to darkspace isn't possible as we'd be forced to go through the black hole. Our linked darkspace engines would be consumed."
Claudia thought of her options. There was always a way out, always a solution. If there wasn't a solution then it wasn't a problem. She considered countless permutations in her mind and proposed them to the AIs. But the three AIs turned their backs to her, telling her that her solutions wouldn't work.
She continued thinking, but for every moment she did the darkness grew closer.

Chapter 42

Ashra respected Alan, so she wanted to listen to him. Her comet had slowed after it left the combat zone, maintaining its position with minute thrusts from its engines. She gently breathed in the recycled air. She was so still, one might have mistaken her for being asleep.
But she was awake, gazing at her Empyrean filled with debris, more debris than she had ever seen. They were once stars, but many had been shattered. Their dust filled her sky. 
The perpetuals had changed as well. The blue one dimmed and disappeared, leaving another hole in the center of her sky. The purple one grew brighter, so bright it was difficult to look at. There were strange forms on Sanctuary, ones that seemed similar to those on Phalos; two stars forced to merge with one another. She had plucked one of these stars out of the Empyrean, one like the Maiden Orana, but when she held it to her eye she could see nothing.
When she put it back in the sky, she noticed something else. The light of the stars all bent towards a single point in space, as if being pulled towards it. The light pooled around a black disk that swirled with many colors. 
She had never seen such an object in the Empyrean before. When she tried to move it, to gain a closer look at it, it wouldn't budge, much like a perpetual. With her feet in the water, she put both hands around that spot of darkness and pulled, but it was stuck in place. Yet she felt the stars even as they were absorbed into the darkness. She knew she could harness them and grow them into something else.
The remnants of war spiraled into the black hole and were devoured. Even some stars that were whole and healthy were eaten, and brief glimpses showed that they were mostly people that belonged to the Einhart.
She thought back to her time with them. What had the Einhart done for her? They had captured her, imprisoned her and ordered her execution. She owed them nothing. But Alan was an Einhart, and he had become dear to her. Even though he didn't need to, he had protected her when she was defenseless. He had spoken for her when she had no voice of her own. And he had given her a choice, while others had already set out the path she was to follow.
Because he was Einhart, and they were his family, she would do what she could. She offered a silent apology to Alan. She hoped he would forgive her for participating.
She gathered the stardust to herself, forming it into a spherical lump in her hands. There was so much material to work with, more than she had ever seen, but she had a feeling she would need it all. She threw the seed into the black hole and added more and more to it, flinging bits and pieces of glowing star bits with flicks of her wrist. She felt it settle within the black hole and mix with the seed already inside. And then she danced.

Chapter 43

A wave of gravity pulsed from the black hole, and the integration chamber could take no more. The tube collapsed in a spray of glass and a flood of cold water. Claudia lost her connection to the ship and her avatar disappeared from its dais on the bridge.
She regained control of her body, one nerve at a time. She spit out the fluid and shook her limbs, as if they had fallen asleep. Her attendants came forward with a dark green cape and draped it over her nude body. One attendant pulled her hair back and tied it into a braid, while another held a com set in both hands. Claudia took the offered com with shaking fingers and clumsily stuffed it into her ear.
She would command from the bridge. The crew hastily swept away the glass and water as she slowly got up and walked on bare feet. "Report," she said. Though her voice was quiet from lack of use, everyone heard it.
"Fluctuations within the black hole, ma'am. Zeroth radiation levels have increased. A subsignature of delta waves also detected."
"Delta waves?"
"Yes, ma'am."
The starfield tilted as the pull of the black hole became stronger. "Bring remaining cameras as close to the event horizon as possible. Show me what's happening."
The black hole appeared on the viewscreen. The final moments of the Pinewell were still displayed, grotesquely elongated as the light stretched across the dark canvas. Zeroth radiation shot forth from the center of the sphere, visible only to the sensors and instruments. But there was something else there, white light that poked out of the darkness. Claudia knew that physically it was impossible for anything to escape that hole. Yet, there it stood, like a branch above the sea, waving in the wind. The edges of it cracked under the gravitational forces, and the twigs at the end snapped off, leaving behind inky trails of energy that spiraled back into the hole. The branch was swallowed.
But from the pool of the void, another light emerged, one that took a different form. It was just a thin sprout, but its roots were deep, surrounding the singularity and drawing upon the dense mass there. The sprout turned into two small leaves attached to a thin stalk.
"Zeroth radiation has completely vanished, ma'am," the technician said. "It seems like it's been replaced by delta waves. The waves are coalescing, almost like they're feeding off of the black hole."
The leaves turned into branches. What was once a seed was now a sapling. The black hole diminished as the plant grew larger, the hole's darkness absorbed into its roots. The darkness pulsed up the length of the trunk, sometimes spilling out, as if it were too much for the tree to contain. But the drasil held firm, and with every branch, bud, and leaf made of light, the darkness receded.
The light became a tree. The flowers on the drasil's branches bloomed. Pollen made of light drifted as if blown by a breeze.
"Ma'am, we have enough thrust to counter the black hole's gravity."
"Return us to our position over Sanctuary," she said.
For an instant the tree was complete, as if it grew out of a mound of soil. A moment later, the black hole completely disappeared. The roots of the drasil were in full view, compressed into a fibrous ball. 
Then the tree and all of its parts disappeared. It left no trace that it had ever existed, except for the faint scent of flowers in the minds of everyone who saw it.
The crippled Aurelius crawled through space with fewer than half of its original engines. The Divine Will was silent and floated above Sanctuary. The clouds around the throneworld itself had cleared, allowing the Einhart their first glimpse of the entire disk.
Claudia's eyes focused on only one point. Atop the highest tower of the palace floated a purple and blue jewel, larger than the size of a man. It was covered in a layer of frost and a ring of ice rotated underneath it. Ice fell off the jewel, sparkling like diamonds, as something within the jewel stirred.
She considered her options. There were two other ships remaining, but they were also crippled and wouldn't be able to fight. The Aurelius had exhausted its full complement of missiles in the attack on the throneworld. She was sure Sanctum reinforcements would arrive soon, and hers were still in transit. She didn't know if the Divine Will was still a threat. It had stopped moving shortly after the Umbra crashed into it, but she could never be sure of Seth's plans. Though, she could possibly still use it. An idea came to mind.
"What's the status of the sentries?" she asked.
"Still functional and secure in the upper bay, ma'am," a monitor responded.
"Target the Divine Will and deploy."
"Are we bringing it aboard the ship?" he asked with a hint of concern in his voice.
"No. After the Divine Will is secured inside their field, point the sentries' thrusters towards Sanctuary. Our target is that," she said, marking the blue jewel that crowned the citadel. It had lost another layer of ice.
She held the cape to cover her mouth so no one else would hear. "Alan, are you there?"

***

Alan kept a hand pressed on Argus's wound. The large man groaned weakly. Alan sighed in relief, knowing his teammate was alive. "Hang on, Aki's gone to get some medicine. Some of her homebrew," he said, smiling. With barely any power left in the Umbra, the medbed was nothing more than a futon on the ground and wouldn't be of use. Even with their combined strength, he wasn't sure he and Aki could lift him up. Dragging him onto the ship wasn't an option.
His com crackled. "Alan, are you there?" It was Claudia.
"Still alive," he responded.
"Status."
"Seth is dead, blown out of the ship. We have wounded and could use some help-"
"We can't send help," she said, cutting him off. "Get off the Divine Will as soon as you can. I'm sending it back to Sanctuary."
"Argus is about to die, and the Umbra," he said, looking at the heap of wreckage, "isn't in flying condition." In addition to the lives of the members of his team, he remembered the promise he made to Ashra.
"Many people have died today," Claudia responded. "We can destroy the emperor now, while he's still in cocoon, and their sacrifice won't have been in vain."
Alan scowled. "Don't talk to me like a politician," he said angrily. "If you're going to send us to our deaths just say it."
"Enough!" Though it was a whisper, her message was clear. "I make decisions that kill the people that have entrusted their lives to me. You are a Second Medium, but this is something greater than you or me. If he dies, the empire will be without its head and we'll have peace and freedom. I'm telling you to get off that ship in any way possible, and I hope you make it. If you and survive and we are unable to kill the emperor from orbit, take him out from the ground. You have your orders." The com went silent.
Aki came back with a towel in hand. A belt with a row of vials was tied around her waist. She picked out four and laid them side by side; each one was filled with a different colored powder. She took pinches of one, a handful of another and mixed them all in a collapsible bowl with two fingers. After adding a dab of water, she had a thick paste whose smell and color reminded Alan of old moss near a waterfall. She put her hand under Alan's and gently pushed it aside. As soon as she did blood flowed from Argus's stomach. She smeared the poultice over the wound and crammed more of it inside. As she stuck her fingers in, Argus awoke with a howl. Without hesitation, she stuffed the towel into his mouth. As she worked, she asked Alan, "What did she say?"
"We're going to Sanctuary," Alan said.
"On what?" She packed her mixture of herbs in and sprayed the area with an atomizer. A clear, elastic layer of temporary skin held the wound closed. She put her hands under Argus's back and Argus obliged by rolling over, grimacing as he turned. She started working on the other side of the wound. Though the pain was almost enough to knock him out again, Argus didn't complain.
"On this," Alan responded. "We're going down with the ship."
Aki nodded and finished her ministrations by inserting a needle into a vein that jumped out of Argus's forearm. As the syringe emptied, Argus felt the pain diminish until it was only a dull ache. "This will keep you awake," she said, "but not for long. We'll need to get you proper treatment before your guts fall out."
"Thanks," he grunted. He slowly got to his knees, then onto his feet with Alan and Aki's help.
Alan looked at both of them. "Claudia is going to send this ship crashing to Sanctuary in the hopes of killing the emperor. We don't want to be here when that happens."
They looked at each other as the Divine Will shuddered and began its accelerated descent.

Chapter 44

Claudia watched as the sentries guided the Divine Will towards the throneworld. Though the shields on Sanctuary were up, perhaps they would allow one of their own ships through. She thought of Alan and his team on that ship, hurtling towards the top of the palace. She hoped they would live.
The Divine Will passed through the shields unimpeded. The five sentries that boosted the ship towards their target were destroyed and made purple shimmers across the barrier. But the prince's ship continued along its trajectory, its hull turning bright orange as it entered the atmosphere.
The jewel stirred. The last of the ice fell away and its membrane became translucent, illuminating the form of a man underneath it.
Just before the Divine Will was about to impact, Claudia thought she saw something slip out of its hull and disappear into the forest below. She looked back to the top of the citadel. The cocoon split. A second later, she only saw fire and smoke as the Divine Will crashed into the top of the citadel.
The gray smoke disappeared and was replaced by white steam, covering everything in a thick mist. When it cleared, the Divine Will, though burnt and melted at the edges, was still whole. The citadel still stood, hidden behind a wall of ice. The ice stretched past the width of the ship, blocking her view with its glassy surface.
"Switch cameras," she said.
The view from another camera was displayed.
From the waist down, the emperor was clad in a long length of blue silk that deepened to purple near the tip. It was much longer than he was tall, for his feet did not touch the ground. His torso and arms were exposed; their only covering was the ribbon of silk that wound its way behind his neck and under his arms and drifted out behind him, riding on the air. His shoulders and chest had the toned musculature of a young man. The emperor's face showed no signs of age and many would have confused him to be the same age as the First Prince. It was only through his eyes, with their fathomless depths of experience, of lifetimes lived and ended, of endless cunning, that one knew that the emperor was not what he appeared to be.
The ambassadors trapped on Sanctuary would say that he looked the same as before the merge. The emperor had wanted nothing of the Erudite except for the trait the Galean ruling line was gifted with. Once he had it, he discarded the rest. It fell, along with the rest of the cocoon, in a shattered heap of colored ice that was blown off the top of the citadel.
The emperor looked straight into the camera, as if he knew that Claudia and the rest of the Einhart were watching him. He put his hands in front of his chest. A snowflake appeared between his palms, small and spiky, nothing more than a sparkle in the light. Blue light swirled around the flake, increasing in intensity as he wove his hands around it. The light formed itself into a ball, the layers of a blizzard contained between his fingers. With a wave of his arm, he directed the great part of his accumulated energy in a cold burst that radiated outward.
The Divine Will, suspended in a glacier, sped upwards, propelled by a column of ice. Waves of frozen water emerged from the pillar and sunk back down into it. The ice waves gained speed as they entered the colder air, bearing the weight of the ship as if it were nothing but a fish in the ocean. 
Claudia saw the ship speeding back towards them. "Hard to starboard!" she said, but the Aurelius was too slow. The Divine Will crashed into the shields of the flagship and shattered into countless icicles. As the shields dissipated from the impact, the icicles continued with their momentum. They pierced the hull and plating, and then rained down on the bridge. Three attendants immediately covered the High Adjudicant with their bodies. Icicles laden with bits of shrapnel slammed into them. Claudia felt each of them impact as their bodies shuddered with the hits. Glass shards pierced the light consoles and crew, and only those who threw themselves under the bank of consoles found enough protection.
After a while, the crystalline pinging disappeared. Claudia knew the rain of ice was over when the attendants on top of her stopped moving. Risking a glance, she noticed that the holes the icicles tore through the hull were being patched over by nanomachines. As the bridge repressurized, Claudia pushed the bodies of her attendants off of herself. She walked across the bridge and took note of the damage, avoiding the potholes left in the ground from the icicles. They were quickly melting, leaving bits and pieces of the Divine Will in the puddles they made.
"Gather the wounded and send extra staff to the medbay," she said. The assault on Sanctuary would need to wait.

Chapter 45

The emperor watched as the broken form of the Aurelius retreated. The royal guards awaited his advent as he descended towards the top of the citadel. "Bring me my daughter," he said, in a voice that was as young as his face and body. The guards disappeared from the citadel, each headed towards a squadron of waiting drones.
The emperor's feet alighted upon the ground. His covering hung off of the side of the citadel, fluttering in the blustering winds. He breathed deep the air of Sanctuary, savoring the hint of bitterness that the arboreals gave off. This was a fitting start to his return, he thought. He mourned his son, the First Prince, for a moment. But it was Seth's own hubris that brought about his downfall, and as the emperor descended into the palace and heard reports of all that had transpired in his absence, he could not help but feel his son had deserved the fate he had earned. More than anything, the emperor was curious. Who had the ability to destroy both the Divine Will and his son in one short battle? He would find this person and see what made them so special.

***

"Hold on!" Alan said. The three gripped the edges of the Umbra, which was half the ship it was before. As the Divine Will returned to Sanctuary as a flaming wreck, the front half of the Umbra slid out, followed by another half that had separated during the violent shift back to normal space. He watched as the four engines, untethered, tumbled ahead of them into the forests below. Aki grabbed on tight, but Argus looked as if he would lose the contents of his stomach, or that his stomach itself would be lost through the barely-sealed hole in his midsection. Alan knew that even if they survived this fall, Argus wouldn't be in any shape to fight for much longer.
Alan liked the feeling of zero gravity, of his boots lifting up from the ground unbidden. As he floated in freefall, he looked up at the sky of Sanctuary, a dazzling blue despite there being no sun nearby. But his appreciation would need to wait. The ground was coming up quickly to meet them, and he didn't know how well the trees could support the falling tons of half a spaceship. It wasn't just the ground; the trees seemed to want to greet them as well. He thought his eyes deceived him, but with a closer look, he saw the trees straining towards the motion and sound, as if the falling ship was the sunlight their leaves needed. Between their branches he glimpsed rows of gnashing teeth.
The Umbra crashed into the treetops, breaking branches and trunks. Alan slammed against the wall of the ship, breaking his hold. He lost sight of his teammates and tumbled out. The world was a blur until something rough and hard broke his fall. He oriented himself and found whatever it was beneath him was moving, tilting up behind him. 
When he opened his eyes, he knew he had fallen on a branch of one of the trees. The branch was lifting up, forcing him towards its center. As he looked below, he found teeth about to clamp down on his feet. Throwing himself off the edge of the branch, he windmilled his arms before he finally fell to the ground. He landed on his back, knocking the breath out of him. Aki materialized on a pile of fallen leaves nearby and pulled him to his feet. Branches snaked out from the underbrush, trying to tangle and trip their feet. Aki was faster and led the way. While she gracefully vaulted over any boughs, Alan stumbled and plowed his way through the vines and wood. As he broke a stick between his fists, he asked, "Where's Argus?"
She tilted her head towards the edge of the forest. Alan heard pounding on the ground. He heard rhythmic footfalls that shook the trees nearby, accompanied by branches being reduced to pulp. When they emerged at the edge of the forest, Alan sighed in relief when he saw the big man panting and pressing a hand to his side.
"There are many routes, but the destination is the same," Argus said.
"Your wound?" Aki asked.
Argus removed his hand and it was stained with fresh blood. "It seems like I might've overdone it. It's funny, I didn't feel anything."
"It's not funny," she said. "Your senses are heightened and the pain is blocked, but the body isn't designed to be pushed so far. You'll collapse from exhaustion."
"Until then, we have more we need to do," Argus said. The three of them faced the trees and backed onto the white stone that made up the outer courtyard of the palace. As they retreated, the stone cracked as roots shifted underneath the tiles, pulling the trees nearer. 
The trees closest to them bent down. Their limbs arched towards them and shook with anticipation. The jaws at the top of their trunks were covered in a layer of mucous. Alan walked backwards, keeping his gun trained on the swaying branches. His ammo was limited and he didn't know if bullets would stop them. Deciding to try, he fired a pair of shots at the nearest tree. With the exception of some stripped bark, nothing else happened. It kept coming closer.
They continued retreating step by step until their backs were pressed up against the walls of the palace. The smooth alabaster offered no escape. A heavy blast door separated them from the inside of the palace, but no matter how hard Aki searched, she couldn't find an access panel.
The trees came closer, their branches whipping about. Argus snapped off a branch as it lunged forward, but for every branch he destroyed another came to take its place. Aki had unsheathed kujiki and started sliced with furious effort.
Above the trees, Alan's gaze was drawn to the single comet that was entering the atmosphere. It was escorted by five Sanctum drones and two manned fighters. 
Why, he thought, why couldn't they let her go? His anger and despair radiated from his mind. A voice responded.
<Alan?>
<Ashra,> he thought, <Is that you? Did they bring you to Sanctuary?>
<I'll answer you in a moment. Are you surrounded right now?> she asked.
<Yes. How'd you know?>
<Those trees, they talk to me. They call themselves arboreals and they're originally from Phalos. But more than anything, they're hungry.>
<That's good to know,> he said as he swatted away a branch. <How do I kill them?>
<You won't need to. I have spoken to the first cutting. He is old, but he understands.>
As she spoke, the roots stopped their forward march. Reluctantly, they returned the way they came. As they withdrew to the forest, the floor of the courtyard began to repair itself. The stone tiles, cracked and split by the roots, returned to their original positions. The seams between the stones grew faint until they disappeared. It was as if the tiles had never been disturbed. Alan wondered how many times it had happened before, when people tried to leave or enter the palace.
The arboreals were back in the dirt. They steadied their roots, brought their trunks to the sky and closed their mouths. Argus, covered in scratches, looked questioningly at Alan, but he only shook his head, equally confused, and pointed to the squadron of fighters coming down.
<Where are they taking you? Have they harmed you?> Alan asked.
<No,> she said. He felt her detach from his mind, and a moment later a drasil appeared in the sky in front of her escorts. Ashra's comet sped through a small hole in the nest of branches. The other drones and fighters crashed into the tangle of growth and were reduced to nothing. <And they won't,> she finished.
<Come to our position, we'll keep you safe,> he said. He turned to Argus. "Guide her." Argus kept his eyes glued to the comet as it came down. He felt another presence in his mind share his eyes. In response, the comet adjusted its course so that it came straight for them.
<You'll want to slow down now, Ashra,> Alan said, but the comet's speed didn't change.
<You only told me how to steer. Not how to brake,> she said.
<Point taken. Pull up on both thruster handles.>
<I am.>
Alan realized some part of the comet must've shorted out during the entry to Sanctuary. <Brace for impact,> he told her. <Keep your head on the rest and your knees loose.> 
The three on the ground ran back towards the forest as the comet streaked towards them. It landed with a crash and a shower of dirt, throwing tiles and debris into the air.
When the dust settled, the front of the comet popped off. Alan rushed forward to extract Ashra. But when he arrived, she had already broken free of the inflated cushions and hopped to the ground. As soon as he saw her, he lifted her up and hugged her.
"Why did you wait till now to break free? Why did you let them capture you?" he asked.
<I felt you down here, and I thought you may have needed my help,> she said. 
He hugged her tighter. "You shouldn't have come," he said, squeezing her close. "But I'm glad you did." Alan felt her white hair tickle his face. He breathed in that faint scent of drasil flowers that perfumed her skin. Though her arms couldn't reach around his shoulders, she returned the embrace.
After what seemed like an eternity, he put her down. "What do you see?" he asked.
She closed her eyes and cast about the Empyrean. <I have never been here before, but it seems familiar. This place, Sanctuary?it seems to know who I am.> She walked towards the blast doors that had blocked their ingress earlier. The white tiles matched the color of her hair and skin. As she approached, an array of blue lights scanned her, running over her face and white dress. A moment later, the doors separated with a hiss. They were buffeted by the scent of age, of objects and knowledge taken from cultures long forgotten. The scent was replaced by clean, ionized air as the doors fully opened.
Ashra didn't hesitate and stepped inside. The four entered the palace and the doors closed behind them. 
They found themselves in a warehouse. Harsh light came down from above, illuminating the wide space. Its tall ceiling and clean lines stood out in sharp contrast to the rock of the exterior. Boxes of goods brought in from the farthest reaches of the empire were stacked in neat rows. Some were still on their carts, hovering above the ground, while others were organized against the wall. 
Alan heard an electric charge. "Down!" he said. A second later, the box closest to him was split open by a burst of plasma. Cracked and melted bottles tumbled out and shattered on the ground, covering the floor with a blue liquid. 
Argus pushed Ashra behind him and crouched behind a box. He was afraid to draw attention to himself and the princess. Even if he could shoot, he wasn't sure if he could keep his aim steady.
Alan took cover behind another crate and fired at where the plasma came from. He emptied his clip, but the royal guards, handpicked from the best of the Sanctum troops, were cautious and fast. He ducked behind a set of boxes as plasma bolts sped overhead. "I'm out," he said, ejecting the clip and placing it on the ground. As he was searching for a spare clip, a gun slid next to his thigh. He looked up. Argus had given him his own. 
The big man didn't look well. His face was pale and he took shallow breaths. The medicine Aki had given him would keep him standing, but his body couldn't sustain itself for much longer. They needed to get him help. He called back to them. "Ashra, is there any kind of medical facility here?" Alan asked.
She looked through as many stars as she could, but found none. <None that I can see.>
"Damn it. What if any of the royals get hurt?" he asked.
<I believe the royals heal without the help of technology,> she said.
Alan sighed. He could continue the mission. He could seek out the emperor with his team, but Argus would never make it. 
"Alan, you don't have to worry about me," Argus said, as if reading his thoughts. "Seth is dead and my duty to the Erudite is over. I will fight until my last breath, as I promised. Time is short. We must go on." He coughed as he spoke, and then winced as the pain followed.
"Quiet. You vowed to give me your life, and I won't let you off so easily," Alan said. He turned to Ashra. "Tell me where the nearest launch bay is."
Her eyes moved under her eyelids as she searched. <There, that way.> She pointed to a door across the room. Alan followed her finger. They would have to cross a stretch of the warehouse to get there.
Grabbing a cart, he motioned for the others to follow. Aki got behind him. Argus led the princess behind him in a cart of their own. They made their way forward step by step. 
The carts wobbled and boxes exploded around them. Aki fired over the top of the boxes to cause a distraction. Her shots were wide, but the bullets provided them with the cover they needed to get across. Alan was splattered with some kind of wine and Argus was covered with bits of ceramic and plaster by the time they reached the other side. 
As before, the door opened when Ashra approached. Alan waved them all through, barely making it as it sealed shut behind him.
The bright lighting became dim. The concrete floor was replaced by marble with gray and white striations, so polished that it reflected the images of nature painted onto the ceiling high above them. It reminded Argus a little of the Erudite's temple on Galea. But there was no time to appreciate the beauty of the palace.
They moved quickly. The hard floor didn't absorb any sound; Alan worried that their footsteps would be heard. When they came to a fork, Ashra took them down the left hallway, towards the center of the palace and the citadel tower. "Are you sure this is the way?" Alan asked.
<Yes. We're close,> she said. 
After another set of doors, they entered the dock. The ships were unlike anything Alan had ever seen before, and he guessed that this was the dock the royals used to leave Sanctuary. Each ship was different, built unlike any of the known Sanctum fighters. They were small, designed for the comfort of their passengers, but they also bristled with heavy artillery and thick plating. Alan walked past one after the other, not knowing which one to pick, and whether or not he would be able to operate it.
Aki paused when they came across a fighter they had seen before. It was black, with flared wings and a cockpit made of overlapping layers of glass. She recalled seeing it in the clouds, when there was fire on the ground. She had seen it on Galea. Could it be? She put the thought out of her mind. Getting Argus to the Aurelius was their first priority.
Alan decided on a ship with its door open. It looked promising, with a small body and three fins that arched towards the front of the ship. Unlike the Umbra, the fins weren't tethered to the ship in any way; they simply floated in formation around the fuselage.
"Argus, Ashra," he said, "get in."
<Why am I going?> she asked. <I came to confront my father, and he is here.>
Alan was prepared for her question. "One," he said, "I have a feeling that the ship won't work unless you're in it, like those doors. Two, Argus is about to die. I know how much you want to face your father, but Argus's life is at stake. Make sure he gets to the Aurelius in one piece. I need you. He needs you."
No one had ever said that to her before, she thought. No one had ever said she was needed. <His life is more important than my vendetta,> she said.
He knelt and hugged her. "Thank you," he said. "Your contact will be Bri, if she's still alive. She looks like this," he said. From his wrist, he brought up an image of the woman, sitting at her console controlling the gates. Through Argus, Ashra saw her. "Can you find her?"
Ashra searched in the Empyrean. <I see her star,> she said.
"Good. She'll guide you in and take care of you. Stay on this ship after you arrive and don't let anyone else know you're coming."
Ashra stepped into the ship. As Alan guessed, light consoles appeared when she sat down and placed her hands upon the dashboard.
Argus was about to board. With his feet on the walkway, he wrapped his arms around Alan. 

"Nights and days shall pass,
the stars will wheel into eternity.
But your moment of kindness,
can only be repaid
with a lifetime of gratitude."

Bending his head down, he kissed Alan on the forehead. Alan didn't resist. The act was filled with love, and when Argus let him go, Alan knew how deeply he had earned the big man's devotion.
"Go now," Alan said.
Argus climbed into the other seat and started the activation routine for the craft. The ship's door slid into place and sealed with a hiss. The three fins that swept over the ship started to rotate, generating blue thrust along their lateral edges.
Alan felt a tingle in his mind. <The throne is not far,> Ashra said. <I can sense his presence; it's brighter than anything I have ever seen before. You shall need to fight through many, but you will have help. The haga half of the arboreals want nothing more than to exercise their animal side, and the controls the empire engineered into them weren't hard to undo.>
The fins were rotating so quickly that it looked like a blue cone was behind the ship. Argus toggled a switch and a gate opened at the end of the launch bay. The ship taxied out into the sunlight, where a ramp stood raised and waiting. Argus parked the ship at the bottom. 
An electric current ran through the ramp rails. The charge built up, crackling around the ship. With one burst, the charge released, filling the air with the scent of ozone. The ship accelerated up the ramp and was launched into the sky. 
Alan watched it disappear. The gate closed, returning the launch bay to darkness. He accessed his com, hoping the Aurelius was close enough. "Bri, are you there?" he said. "Bri, come in."
He waited, standing next to Aki as she prepared her gear.
A voice came through the other end. "Alan? Is that you?"
"It is, Bri."
"You're alive!" Her voice dropped to a whisper. "When the High Adjudicant gave the order, I didn't know what would happen-"
"We're fine, and I'm glad you are too. Listen Bri, there's a Sanctum ship approaching the Aurelius. It's a friendly and has one of my men inside. When it arrives, let it in and have a medbed ready; he's suffered severe trauma and blood loss." He kept Ashra a secret. "Send a pair of medics to retrieve my team member and no one else. The ship is off limits, by order of the Second Medium, until I return. Finally, keep on the lookout for any signals from the ship; it may try to connect with you through your mind. Some strange Sanctum technology. Feel it, allow it. Second medium out." With these cryptic words, he closed the line. 
Aki tapped him on the shoulder. "Look there," she said. The gate at the end of the launch bay was being pried open. A shaft of sunlight broke through as the two halves of the door were being pulled apart. He heard it first, the sound of rustling leaves, of branches that creaked and moaned in the wind. Except there was no breeze; they moved of their own accord, willed to life by the haga inside them.
With a groan, the gate was pulled apart by grappling roots and then ripped from the wall. The arboreals crossed over the threshold, covering the ground with surprising speed. Their roots had broken free of the soil and squirmed across the floor of the launch bay, pulling the trees closer to the center of the palace. Aki kept her gun aimed at them, but they passed by as if the two weren't there.
Alan heard discharging plasma from behind another door. It seemed like the arboreals had found more than one way in. Alan and Aki went towards the noise, towards the citadel where the emperor sat overlooking the empire.

Chapter 46

<I know it's hard, but please keep your eyes open,> Ashra said.
Argus had his hands in the light console, making adjustments to maintain their trajectory. The Aurelius wasn't far, yet to him, time seemed to slow and stretch. He focused all of his remaining energy on getting this ship to the Aurelius.
The capital ship came into view. He could begin to make out the portions that had been cleaved off, but then his eyelids started to droop. He was jolted awake when the ship suddenly lurched to the side. 
Aki's medicine had worn off. As he was overtaken with drowsiness, he closed his eyes. Ashra saw her one window to the outside world close as well.
<Argus?> she said. She unstrapped herself from her seat. Squeezing into the gap between Argus and the console, she moved a hand to his neck. It was there. Faint, but there. His pulse was alive under her fingers. <Forgive me,> she said. Placing her thumbs on his eyelids, she pulled them up. It was blurry, but through his eyes she could see again.
She sent another part of her mind to the Aurelius, casting about for the woman Alan had mentioned. She found her monitoring the surrounding space.
<Bri.> The voice was a whisper in the woman's mind. Bri shook her head with a start. <Bri,> the voice said again. This time she listened. Was this what Alan mentioned? The voice continued, <This is the ship from Sanctuary, with Argus Volgren on board. He needs help. Where should I dock?>
Though Bri was shaken by the sudden voice in her head, her training took over. She directed her transmission at the incoming ship. "Standby," she said.
