The others gave her funny looks as she talked to herself. She searched for a bay that was still intact. "Dock B, space 17 has been cleared of debris. Our tractors would normally guide you in, but they were destroyed. You'll have to bring the ship in manually." She toggled a switch on her console. "The docking bay should be lit up. Follow the green landing lights and land there. Medics are standing by."
<Ah.> Ashra only had one pair of hands. Taking in one last fuzzy glimpse of the light on the side of the Aurelius, she removed her hands and Argus's eyelids closed. The world went dark. She felt her way down along his arm. When she reached his hands, she nudged them aside, out of the light console. The ship veered to the side as she stuck her hands in his place. She wiggled her fingers and the ship tilted in response, still traveling forward. <Bri, please keep your eyes glued to the screen and don't look away.>
Bri didn't understand the request, but she agreed. She suddenly felt drowsy, as if her mind were numbed.
Ashra looked through Bri's eyes. Using the view on Bri's screen, Ashra made sense of her own trajectory. The only remaining cameras she could access were mounted flush with the side of the Aurelius, making it difficult to recognize the edges of the docking bay. Ashra brought her wrists down, as she had seen Alan do before. The ship slowed, but her view of herself was about to be eclipsed by the side of the flagship. She tightened her body and braced for impact. The ship sailed towards the docking bay, and she was blind. She kept her hands as still as possible, but the rest of her body was tense and rigid.
She heard a loud screech and felt the ship shudder as it scraped the side of the docking bay, but they were still moving forward. They had made it.
Now inside, she sought another pair of eyes. The medics were tense, ready to pick up the wounded. What they didn't expect was a Sanctum ship piloted by a blind girl careening towards them. They dove out of the way as it approached.
The bottom of the ship slammed against the floor. The sound of metal against metal echoed throughout the bay. Ashra pulled her hands back and the ship bounced up. With the moment of vision she borrowed from the medic, she estimated her distance to the ground.
The ship detected the docking bay floor and three landing struts came out. With a pounded fist, Ashra brought the ship down. It landed on two struts; the other half was still in the air. After a moment, the Aurelius's gravity pulled the ship down. It fell on all the struts with a crash.
The ship hatch opened and the medics rushed in. They first came across a girl with white hair. One of them stopped to ask if she was hurt. She shook her head and pointed to the cockpit, where, judging by his size, a Galean lay unconscious. They strained to get him out of the chair. Once they did, the medbed scooped him up and took care of the rest. They whisked him away to the medical bay.
Alone, Ashra sat in the cockpit and took a deep breath. Despite everything that stood in her way, she had survived, and Argus would too. For the first time, she wasn't a force of destruction. She was a person that put the needs of others before herself. When she realized this, she thanked Alan for all that he taught her. She thanked him for the knowledge that she wasn't damned to be a princess of the empire or even the Priestess of Phalos. These were nothing more than titles that weighed upon her. She would always have them, but she would live her life the way she saw fit, helping others avoid the suffering she had endured.
She cast about the Empyrean, examining the stars still on Sanctuary. There were others that needed her help.

Chapter 47

Alan popped his head out, missed a couple of swinging branches, then ducked back in. "A full squad of soldiers, but they have their hands full. Those arboreals are fast, considering they're trees and all."
"What's our approach?" Aki asked. She inserted a spare magazine into the belt around her waist and shook her shoulders, feeling the weight of kujiki on her back. She tossed another magazine to Alan.
He caught it and said, "We can go in behind the cover of the arboreals as they make their way forward. Shoot in between the branches and advance towards the citadel. But, they might become hostile if we miss and singe a branch."
"They passed us earlier without issue, but I wouldn't want to attract their attention," she said, chambering a cartridge. "Any other ideas?"
"Nope."
"Sounds good."
"On three?"
"Always."
"One. Tw-" Alan's count was interrupted by shouts down the hall. His eyebrows furrowed and he took another look. 
The Sanctum guards had disappeared; there was no trace of them anymore. His eyes narrowed and he walked out with his gun ready. Aki followed close behind. To their left, the main entrance to the palace was wide open; the heavy doors made from dead arboreals were pulverized, lying in splinters on the floor. Colored light streamed in from high up the walls; stained glass scattered rainbows on the floor. Alan and Aki made their way across the grand foyer, stepping on scenes from the empire's conquest depicted in tile. The crest of the Sanctum, a diamond with a line through it, stood in relief against the ground.
As they went further, Alan learned what had happened to the Sanctum guards. Shreds of bloody cloth littered the floor. Arboreals that were milling around had some of the same cloth hanging from their mouths. Even after the bark closed over their teeth, the vestiges of the guards' uniforms served as a grim reminder of what the arboreals could do.
The pair cautiously stepped around them as they left the foyer and entered the citadel. The air was instantly cooler. Alan could see his breath as he walked around the base of the tower, his footsteps echoing throughout. The walls were made of roughhewn stone covered in a layer of frost. He put his fingers to it and felt it melt under his touch. Perhaps the arboreals did not come further because of how cold it was. Far above him at the top of the citadel shone a mote of light, like a beacon to guide the lost.
"How do we go up?" he asked. There wasn't any mechanism that led to the top, no lift he could see.
Aki made a similar circle around the perimeter. As she approached the center, a span of golden light shot up from the ground, originating from the middle of another Sanctum emblem. The light was concentrated and bound on its edges; it was a flat and narrow sheet that reached as far up as she could see. Small fluctuations in the light density created swirling patterns within the sheet, making it feel organic and alive. She put the edge of her gun against the light. It stopped as if she pressed it against something solid. "Huh. Hyperdense light."
Alan came over and put his palm against it. His hand was also stopped by the light; it felt like warm glass. It was certainly solid. "Do we climb?" he asked.
She walked around the light. Her finger traced a line across its surface as she considered how it would be used. "Forced to pay respect to the emperor," she said to herself, "they wouldn't climb?no, he wouldn't want their heads up, looking at him. They would walk, facing the light, blinded by it." Instead of her hand, she placed one foot on the light. It stuck to the surface. She put her other foot onto the light and felt as gravity shifted, anchoring her firmly to it. Considering Sanctuary was completely manmade, perhaps the designers had brought their gravity manipulation technology, the same technology used on their ships, to this citadel.
Alan whistled appreciatively as he joined her and felt the gravity shift under his feet. "A light bridge. How grand," he said. He stuck his hand off the side. There was no barrier to protect them from falling.
"It's the same with all monarchs," Aki said. "They always want visitors to keep their heads bowed in reverence. Some achieve it with stairs, but having a bridge without railings is another way to keep people's heads down."
"We'll watch our step, but we need to hurry. I'm afraid of leaving Ashra alone on the Aurelius."
With Aki in the lead, they walked up the light bridge. Alan scanned the walls for traps, but considering the reputation of the emperor, the ruler wouldn't have any need for them. 
Alan didn't know what they were going to do once they got to the top. How could they face the emperor with just the two of them when they could barely manage Seth with three? The emperor's abilities were undocumented since he rarely showed himself, even on the worlds of the empire. He had left his children to do most of the work.
They had made it halfway up the bridge, the spot of light above them getting ever larger, when Aki paused and put her hand behind her. Alan had to stop so quickly that he almost lost his balance. "What is-," but he was interrupted when she held a hand up, asking him to keep silent.
Aki heard it first, the sound of footsteps across the light bridge. The echoes around the citadel made it hard to tell, but it wasn't from behind. No, the sound came from in front of her. A shadow blocked out the light from above. Aki knew that silhouette that looked so much like her own. Without waiting, she brought out her pistol and pulled the trigger.
The shadow drew a blade from its back. The bullet was deflected and fell back to the bottom of the citadel as it left the gravity field of the bridge. Aki realized that Vijera's speed meant that she had recovered from their last meeting on Abyssinia.
Aki fired rounds one after the other as she dashed forward. Alan ran, trying to keep up. She said to Alan behind her, "Vijera is going to open with a straight lunge. I will parry; dodge under it and keep going."
"I'm not going to let you fight her by yourself," Alan countered.
"The bridge is too narrow for three. You'd only get in my way."
"But-"
"This is my fight, Alan. Take care of the emperor and we'll meet at the top when I'm done." She cracked a rare smile.
Alan nodded. The shadow was filled in with color as Vijera approached. Aki saw she was whole again. No burn marks scored her face and her fingers had all grown back. 
Vijera came with a shout. As Aki had expected, she opened the battle with a lunge. Her body shot forward with her arm outstretched, seeking to impale Aki. 
Aki had her hand on kujiki as she ran forward. When Vijera advanced she pulled out the blade and pushed Vijera's attack to the side. 
Alan was close behind. When Aki made the opening, he leapt forward, tucked his body in and rolled past Vijera. Once the pair was behind him he sprang to his feet and continued running.
Vijera snarled when Alan evaded her. She turned around, ready to chase after him, but had to block a blow from Aki that would've severed her head from her body.
"Your fight is with me," Aki said.
"This time," Vijera responded through gritted teeth, "your precious sister won't be able to save you. Father is close. The power he gives me is absolute. Today you die Aki, and when I am merged with your body you can be reunited with your sister."
Aki responded with a kick. Vijera deflected her foot and stepped back, holding murakumo above her head. Aki assumed a similar pose. The two stared each other down.
Aki relied on open space to avoid Vijera's attacks. She knew it wouldn't be possible on this narrow bridge. She shifted her weight onto her front foot and went for a fast kill. 
The frozen garden was a technique she had perfected at the end of her training, a flurry of strikes aimed at vital Meridians across the body, designed to paralyze the limbs. Knowing Vijera, she opened with a feint. Vijera went for the bait, bringing her sword to block the thrust aimed at her chest. But their blades never touched. With a turn of her wrist, Aki changed her grip on the blade and brought it down on Vijera's exposed legs. She slashed through the hamstrings of one leg, then pulled kujiki up and cut through the sinews and tendons of the other. Vijera snarled but still stood.
Aki's next cut was aimed for the underarm, but Vijera wouldn't be brought down so easily. Recovering from the feint, she parried Aki's attack and pushed her away with her fist. Aki lost her footing from the blow and fell with her back on the bridge. She tried to roll to the right to put more distance between herself and Vijera, but her hand was already gripping the edge of the light bridge and there was nowhere to turn. With no choice, she went to the left, scrambling to find any way to get back on her feet. As she completed the roll, she tried to push off the ground, but couldn't. It wasn't only until a moment later that she felt the pain radiate from her right shoulder.
The harmonic blade went cleanly through her shoulder's skin, joint, and then skin again. The lower half of the blade stuck out below the light bridge, disturbing the golden swirls with plumes of red. Aki was immobilized. Even if she could move, she knew her right arm would be useless.
Vijera pulled the blade out and was about to stab it through Aki's chest, but a kick put her off balance. The lady's weakened legs couldn't support the sudden shift in weight and she stumbled backwards. 
Aki reached over and grabbed kujiki with her left hand and planted it into the ground. The sword wobbled as she pushed on it, but she stood up. Her right arm hung limply at her side.
Vijera did the same. The two faced each other as they did before. But Vijera's wounds had already begun to heal; the blood had stopped flowing and the skin was starting to stitch itself together.
It was then that Aki felt it. It wasn't something that could be heard, only felt in her mind. Like the rustling of leaves in the wind, a soft voice said, <I can help. If my father can do it, I can do it. Let me in.>
With Ashra's growing abilities, Aki was sure that the princess could've entered her mind regardless of her training, yet she still asked. If this fight continued the way it did, Aki knew she would lose. She thought of the Auroran secrets she had in her head, then of her sister that she had always loved and wanted to save.
<Come in,> she thought. She didn't know if Ashra could hear her, but her mind was suddenly awash with a new consciousness, as if the world she had been seeing before was only in black and white. The colors were vibrant; her functioning limbs felt refreshed. Even the pain from her shoulder receded.
The greatest benefit was how time seemed to pass slowly. Or perhaps she was faster. She didn't know. She noticed a drop of her blood fall from her fingertips. She stooped down and caught it in her outstretched palm before it landed on the ground.
Through Aki's eyes, Vijera moved as if she was underwater. The flaws in her technique and form couldn't be masked by speed anymore. Because of the lady's hubris, she would never make full use of Rin's training.
Aki dashed forward with her katana in her left hand. Vijera brought her sword up to defend. Aki spotted a gap and aimed for it, shifting herself into a lower stance. Their swords met. With one twist of kujiki, murakumo was swept aside. Aki continued forward, only stopping when her elbow impacted Vijera's chest. She felt the coarse patterning of Vijera's camouflage suit through her arm. She felt the strong pulse of Vijera's blood weaken and slow.
Without looking, she knew her sword had pierced Vijera's heart. With this one thrust, Aki had avenged her sister and Ashra had avenged her mother.
Vijera managed one more laugh. The emperor, feeling his daughter's life coming to an end, withdrew his mind, and with it, the protection and control it offered. Vijera fell to the ground with Aki on top of her.
Unfettered, Rin swept Vijera aside. Within her mind, the trembling child was banished into oblivion, and she retook control of the body, part by part. 
Aki saw the eyes soften. The smile, the one she remembered from Aurora, returned to those lips. She put her hand on the face that was becoming more like the one she remembered with every passing moment. "Honorable sister, it has been too long," she said, in her native Auroran.
"I'm sorry, sister," Rin replied. "I could see everything, but I couldn't stop it. I couldn't stop her from hurting you." Her voice was weak.
"No more talk of the past, Rin. There was, and only ever will be, what we have now." She clasped Rin's hand tightly. "I had hoped, in my heart of hearts, that there might've been a way to save you. To have you back."
Rin chuckled. "The frozen garden almost cost you your life. But I thank you, Akiko, for releasing me."
"As any sister would've done." She smiled, even as the sides of her eyes became moist.
With effort, Rin rolled onto her side and pulled the scabbard off her back, handing it to Aki. She then lifted murakumo and also gave it to her sister, who promptly sheathed it. "Make good use of it," Rin said.
Aki pulled off the harmonic device on the grip and threw it over the side of the bridge. "I will."
"One last thing." Her voice was so faint that Aki had to lower her ear to Rin's lips.
"Anything, Rin."
"Tell me, what were we like?"
Aki smiled at the memories. "We were two sisters playing by a pond," she said. "Two girls finding their place in a world of men, and we found it before they did. We were two agents sent to opposite sides of the galaxy and its conflict, but we always found a way to love each other. To care for each other. To remember where we were and where we'd go. We have seen wonders only a few get to see. We have played a hand in shaping the fate of empires. But in the end, we were two sisters, sitting with our feet in the pond, watching raccoon-dogs splash as they chased dragonflies."
When Aki was finished, Rin's face was wet. It wasn't until Aki wiped the tears away that she realized they were her own, mixing with Rin's blood as they fell. Rin's chest was still and her pulse was silent. She died with a smile. Aki was glad she could give her sister that.
With a sweep of her hand, Aki closed her eyelids. "Goodbye," she whispered. She sat for a moment more next to her sister, when she noticed Ashra's presence was no longer there.
<Ashra?> she thought, but there was no response. She was suddenly lightheaded and had to steady herself with her hand. When she stood up, the throbbing pain returned to her right arm. She had to clutch it tightly to keep the blood from flowing out. The light at the top of the citadel seemed far away.
With murakumo in her hand, Aki's mission was over. She could head back down, find another ship in the spaceport and get off Sanctuary. Her contract with the Einhart came to an end once her business with her sister was finished. But she had only one thought on her mind.
"Alan." She headed up the light bridge as fast as her battered body would let her.

***

Ashra sat alone in the darkness of the ship, but the Empyrean was bright. Aki's mind was unlike any other she had ventured into before. Ashra lent her being, the full power of her mind to the assassin. The princess remained focused as she sat upon the cold floor with her knees tucked underneath. Her senses had become Aki's. The smells of the interior of the ship were replaced by the cold bite of the citadel.
She heard the sound of steel against steel and steel against flesh, so she never noticed the footsteps that entered the ship. When a hand that smelled of ether closed over her nose and mouth, her connection to Aki was broken, the Empyrean went dark, and she slumped over, unconscious. A pair of arms scooped up her and brought her deeper into the Aurelius.

Chapter 48

Alan neared the top of the citadel. With a raised hand, he shielded himself from the light as it grew brighter the higher he went. He swallowed and felt relief as the pressure left his ears.
During his run up, he remembered all the intelligence the Einhart had gathered on the emperor. Because of his constant merges, no one knew what he looked like, or the shape he would take once he left the cocoon.
The worlds the Sanctum Empire sought out were led by strong people. The emperor had consolidated his power base after taking their leaders and demanding tributes, hostages in reality, Alan thought, to prevent uprisings in the new territories.
In the last decade the emperor had not surfaced. But when he had appeared in the past, he would always start with a message, saying he hoped to avoid bloodshed if the target world would join the empire peacefully, for all subjects were important. Some worlds joined without a fight, most didn't. But once the battle began, the emperor would retire from the field and his son, Seth, would command the forces. The Sanctum destroyed most civilizations with their advanced weaponry, military strategy and sheer numbers. Alan's homeworld of Cybele was no different. He felt a pang of sadness and regret, the likes of which he had not felt in a long time.
Alan decided he would need to win by surprise. He hoped the emperor was still weak after his emergence. In preparation, Alan adjusted one of the plasma pistols he had found, channeling its full charge into one shot. The end of the bridge was near and the nebulous light at the top had become a circle. Though it was faint, he could make out the edge of a chamber above it. He crouched down and tightened the muscles in his legs, ready to enter.
He jumped off the end of the light bridge. He immediately felt a weight on his back as the gravity shifted and pulled him towards the ground. While in the air, he caught a glimpse of purple fabric hanging off a crystal throne. He fired. When he hit the ground, the plasma discharge was a bright blue ball that spanned his entire field of vision. He covered his head, expecting an explosion and debris. Instead, the room became covered in steam. Quickly pushing himself up, he got to his feet in the mist. It was so thick he couldn't see his hands in front of him. Stepping to the side to avoid falling into the hole behind him, he replaced the Sanctum weapon with his own, but the sound of the plasma pistol hitting the floor gave away his position. Something hard and cold hit him in the chest. It knocked the wind out of him and forced his back into the wall. Before he could fall to the ground, ice wrapped around his wrists and ankles, shackling him to the stones he was pressed up against. They were cold and sharp, their edges biting into his skin.
The mist started to clear. Stepping over what remained of a wall of ice were two bare feet followed by a train of silk. Though he was older than everyone else, the emperor looked young, with an unlined face and a head full of dark hair. He was lean; muscles rippled underneath his skin as he came closer. Alan thought he recognized some of those features; maybe it was the curve of his cheek or the shape of his nose that reminded him of both Ashra and Seth. The emperor's eyes were the only thing that betrayed his age; they were dark pools that reflected at least a century's worth of knowledge and experience. It seemed as if galaxies swirled behind them.
"So you're the one that's stolen my daughter's love," the emperor said.
Alan struggled against the ice that held him, but with every jerk the cold seemed to spread until he couldn't feel his hands anymore. Yet he didn't fear this man. "I didn't steal anything. She chose herself who to give it to."
The emperor smiled at his response. "Before she met you, I could always feel her presence; I could always see what she was doing, what she was thinking. Now, her mind is closed to me."
"Good for her," Alan said. "Emperor or not, she didn't need a father like you."
"Need? Her needs are no concern of mine. She is my daughter. She was made to serve the empire and to further my cause across the stars."
"Your cause has only brought death to every world you've set foot on."
The emperor looked saddened. "Death? Only to those who chose to resist. You make it sound as if I enjoy destroying." He walked closer to Alan; the ribbon of silk weaved around his shoulders as if it had a life of its own. "I do what I do for one goal and one goal alone," he said. "Peace. Peace is my motivation. There have been countless battles between all the worlds who would think to rule the other. Ceaseless bloodshed, hatred, vendettas that spanned across generations. I bear that burden now. My empire and I have taken that upon ourselves so that in time we may know peace. So that the fighting will stop. So that there will be no more pain. No more suffering." He put his hand on Alan's shoulder. His palm was smooth and cold, as if no blood circulated through it. "Tell me, my friend, how come you have so much hate in your heart?"
Alan felt a shiver run up his spine as the emperor entered his mind with far more control and power than Ashra ever had. The emperor engulfed his thoughts like air, meandering and swallowing all. Alan was forced to watch as memories, memories he thought he had locked away, were brought to the surface and opened again like old wounds.
"Ah," the emperor said. "Alan Belmont, from Cybele. That would explain it." He rifled through Alan's past and came across golden fields that stretched as far as his memory could see.
"We fought till the last man," Alan said. "And killed two for each one you took of ours."
The emperor closed his eyes and remembered the battles. "It was a valiant effort. Your fields ran red with Sanctum blood. Cybele put up a fight, and you're proof of that. But you got your vengeance didn't you? When I couldn't feel Seth anymore and you tumbled out of the Divine Will, I knew it was you."
"My vengeance won't be finished until you are dead, the empire is nothing but dust, and every world you have conquered is free again," he spat.
"Is that what Claudia promised you?" the emperor said. "Be careful of people in power, Alan. What we say and what we do are not always the same thing."
Alan glared at him. "Enough. If you're going to kill me, kill me." His words were full of conviction, but they rang hollow in Alan's mind. He wanted to live. He wanted to see tomorrow, if only to give Ashra the life she deserved.
"I'm not a wasteful man," the emperor replied. "You are talented and brave. You'd make a fine addition to the Sanctum. Many who were with the Einhart are here now; you even know some of them. Think of it, instead of Second Medium, you'd be commander of your own fleet. You could rebuild Cybele; make it the bountiful planet it once was, a land with full harvests. You'd be loved by your people, and they would remember you as the hero who brought them together, the one that saved them from their exile. You, Alan. You." Ice crystals swirled above the emperor's hand. They compressed into a sphere, studded with peaks and valleys. A miniature of Cybele floated before his eyes, tempting Alan.
"Why should I believe anything you say?" Alan said.
"A prosperous empire is a good empire. That is what I seek to build." He pointed to the shackles around Alan's wrists. "Your fate is in my hands. I could've killed you when you entered, but you are still alive. I see value in you."
"I don't see any value in you," Alan responded. "You speak of peace but your method has always been war."
The emperor scoffed. Another chill went through Alan's mind as the man dug deeper into his past. Images of a young girl floated up through his memories, like a pearl uncovered in the sand. It was a girl with long blonde hair, something she got from her mother. Yet she had Alan's nose and his lopsided grin, the same grin that he had not shown anyone in years.
The emperor sighed. "I concede defeat," he said. The miniature of Cybele in his hand crumbled to crystals. "My daughter was right to trust you. A parent who has lost a child can never forgive. And I suppose Ashra was a suitable replacement for what I took all those years ago. But it's time to return her to me."
"Leave her be. You have plenty of people to do your bidding."
"Ashra is?special," the emperor said. "I kept her secluded and away from those who would influence her and force her to consider the role I wanted her to play." He took his hand off of Alan's shoulder and his presence disappeared from his mind. "She was never meant to be more than an instrument, a tool for my use."
The emperor gave the skin on his own forearm a tug. It stretched like putty and extended further than any human skin should have. When he released it, it sagged and hung limp. A moment later it flowed back to its original position and the creases disappeared. "This is the problem of centuries of merging. DNA mixes and degrades. While I have kept the damage to a minimum, my body is not what it used to be." He turned to Alan. "Ashra can change that. She's a child with the ability to see into the minds of others, farther reaching than even my own. She can shape light itself to her whims, and in time, she'll be able to destroy entire planets with just one tree. I rely on the energy Sanctuary generates, but she, all she needs is death to fuel her. And she will never grow old. Her ability with plants extends to her own being, and with the right guidance, she can be immortal. She will never have the need to merge. She will never have the problems I do."
"She will always be out of your grasp," Alan said. "You can't reach her anymore. She is strong enough to stand against you. And she will destroy the empire you built."
"You are right. She is closed off to me. But not to you." He came close to Alan again, this time with a hint of malice in his eyes. "Do you know why I invaded Galea?"
"The Erudite."
"The ruling family of Galea had a special talent. What I and my children can do with our bodies, the Erudites could do with their minds. They valued knowledge above everything else, and that is a good thing. They sought to keep that knowledge from ever disappearing, so they transferred the entirety of their minds from one Erudite to the next, keeping their traditions and prejudices alive. It came with problems; some people never want to die," he said with an ironic smile. "I purged their presences after the merge, so now it's just me." He put his hand on Alan's chest. "Call to her, Alan. Reach out to her mind with yours."
The cold spread throughout his chest. Alan spoke through clenched teeth. "Never. I will die before that."
"As I assumed. You are a good father. But I'm afraid you'll be losing another daughter today." Alan squirmed against the emperor's palm on his chest, but it didn't help. The cold seemed to seep through his skin and into his heart itself, and with every beat colder blood pumped through his veins. He wanted to curl up into a ball to conserve whatever heat he could, but the shackles held firm as he strained against them.
"Call her," the emperor said.
Alan's lips turned blue and his face lost color altogether. "No."

Chapter 49

Ashra was lying on something soft and warm. If she wasn't careful, she would fall asleep again in its comfortable embrace. She tried to move, but it was as if her body was paralyzed during the deepest parts of sleep. When neither her arms nor legs responded, she thought of just moving one finger. When no digits moved, she decided to save her physical body for later. There wasn't any pain. Or if there was pain, she couldn't feel it.
There were more pressing matters. While her body may not have responded, the Empyrean was there for her. When she opened her mind's eye, she was underwater. With a kick, she sped upwards, her head creating ripples across the top of the water as she emerged. She continued to rise until her bare feet rested upon its liquid surface. She walked towards the island, planning to sift through the stars to see where she was, when her eye was drawn to the perpetuals above the tree. It was the pale yellow star, Alan's star, which was paler than usual. She could not see through his eyes, normally an issue associated only with her blood relatives, so she spoke to him instead.
<Alan?> she asked. <What's wrong?> Alan was there. She felt him, but he didn't answer. Then?there was another presence as well.
She clutched her head as a flash of pain ran through it. Mirroring her feelings, a fissure ran across the sky and divided the stars, as if the Empyrean were nothing more than a cracked egg. Behind the crack she heard faint cries. An object appeared from the fissure, streaking forth like a meteor. It was only when it slowed and the purple shroud loosened around it that Ashra noticed the purple perpetual had also disappeared. In its place was a man, radiant and young.
"Who are you?" she asked.
He strode across the water as easily as Ashra did. "You may call me father," he said.
This was the first time Ashra had seen him. Her mouth hardened into a line. "I only have one father, and he is not you." She recalled what Aki had worn and tried to imitate it. The white dress tightened against her body and hexagonal armor scales appeared across its surface. It was not black, but rather the gold, red and purple hues that Lydia had favored. In her hand appeared a staff hewn from the trees of Phalos.
The emperor looked amused. "Child, you would raise your hand against your own father?"
She gripped the staff tightly and held it out. "I am no longer a child. I have learned to think for myself and to do what I know is right. I will undo the pain and suffering you have caused." She dashed from the island and across the water.
"Never forget," the emperor said, "that like you, this world is my creation as well." He lifted his hand. What looked like a giant pane of glass appeared in the heavens, distorting the stars behind it. Ashra continued charging forward.
"You have no idea how the mind works," he said. "Learn your place, child." The glass cracked and fell in a hail of crystal shards, blown towards Ashra's direction. Each shard bloomed into a flower made of ice when it touched a surface, freezing anything it landed on. Small icebergs appeared across the water. Ashra knocked them away as they came, but they stuck to her hair and clothes and feet. She gritted her teeth and struggled against the cold. Her hands were becoming numb and her arms were sluggish. She tried to move forward, but the shards snared her feet, encasing them in ice and rooting her to the growing glacier. With every swing more ice grew across the staff and her body until she could no longer move. Icicles drooped from the tip of her nose. Her chest was bound so tightly in ice that she felt like she couldn't breathe.
The emperor walked across the frozen lake and placed a hand on the frost that encased Ashra. He effortlessly picked her up and began walking to the island with her. 
She struggled against it. She wished there were fire, wished he were banished from her mind, but no matter what she did, the ice remained. He continued dragging her closer to the tree.
"You should be proud," he said. "Out of all my children, I have chosen you to be my vessel. It is your body that will ensure the continuation of the empire. It is with your flesh that we shall have peace." He threw her against the tree and put his hand on the bark. The wood behind her turned soft, almost fluid. Before she could react, she sunk into the tree, as if into a warm embrace. When the wood closed over her face, she was completely blind, both in the real world and within the Empyrean. But she could still hear her father.
"Be a good girl," he said. "This tree, more than any other manifestation, is your true self. You know this. If you break out of it, if you destroy the tree, you will die. If you are quiet and you cooperate and show me how this body works, I will not raze it to the ground?for now. It is the least I can do as your father."
She couldn't respond because her mouth was sealed by the wood, but she knew he spoke the truth. She would, however, not cooperate.

Chapter 50

The emperor awoke inside his new body. When he opened his eyes, all he could see was darkness, and when he tried to speak no sound came forth. He felt the layout of his limbs, willing his fingers to move. With some effort, he tapped the bed he was on.
"Ashra, are you awake?" a voice asked.
<This is no longer Ashra,> the emperor said.
"My Lord." The voice adopted a formal tone, and the emperor heard a knee drop to the ground.
<Where am I?> he asked.
"Aboard the Aurelius, hidden in my quarters. The Einhart are too busy containing the damage from the battle to be concerned about this section of the ship. It was all as you planned, Your Majesty."
<Well done, Guren. Give me the mutagen. I should like to see and speak with my own eyes and voice,> he said. 
Years ago, in an effort to accelerate the development of her abilities, the emperor had engineered Ashra's lack of senses inside the womb. His plan had worked, and Ashra was in command of a destructive force that he could never have found through conventional weapons alone. But now it was time for his investment to pay out.
Guren pulled out a syringe from his drawer. It was filled with a clear liquid that he had prepared in advance. The medbed the emperor lay on was activated and green lights shined down on him.
"My Lord," Guren said, "this will hurt as your genetic code is rewritten and the eyes and voice box are built."
<A moment of pain for an eternity of perfection. A small price to pay.>
Guren injected Ashra's body with the mutagen. The medbed performed a scan and began to build the parts outlined in the new DNA. The emperor, forged from the fires of war and family, didn't flinch.

Chapter 51

Alan was curled upon the floor of the citadel. He didn't call to Ashra, he didn't succumb. It was she who came to him in his moment of need, and in doing so, allowed the emperor to gain access to her mind. "I'm sorry," he whispered to no one. "I'm so sorry. I failed you."
He had a headache that shot daggers through his brain every time he moved, so he kept still. When Ashra made the connection, the emperor used Alan as a bridge and tore a hole through his mind to reach her. The emperor channeled the entirety of his being through that hole; his experience, knowledge and personality that had been cultivated over a span of years Alan couldn't fathom because he hadn't lived even an eighth of that time. Alan glimpsed Ashra's world through the tear. Though he had tried to close it, his efforts did no more than a pebble against a wave. The last thing he remembered seeing was the emperor coalescing into a purple blob inside his mind and then falling through the hole. Alan saw only Ashra, standing defiant and proud, before the hole disappeared and he was alone again. Despite the pain, he had wanted the tear to stay open so he could jump through and save her, but it had closed.
He was alone, with only his guilt for company. He risked opening his eyes. When the light was too bright he shut them again. With each second that passed, his body seemed more his own. He put one palm on the ground followed by the other. His nerves were confused, but after some time he managed to push himself onto his knees. His head bowed towards the crystal throne.
Opening his eyes again, he saw what had become of the emperor. The purple silk no longer flowed and danced; it hung still, draped across the chair. The body of the emperor was underneath it; a husk devoid of life. The cheeks were sunken, the neck was bent in an unnatural position and the mouth was frozen as if in mid-scream. His entire body had turned to the color of ash. As Alan watched, the skin became pale and transparent, like glass. Clear, jagged points erupted from the emperor's heart and worked their way towards the extremities of the body, carving the flesh into glittering valleys and peaks. The facets refracted the light into rainbows around the chamber, and his remains looked as if it were part of the throne itself.
Alan looked at it with a mixture of curiosity and repulsion, as if he knew that body far better than he should have. Memories flashed through his mind, of worlds he had not been to, of people he had never seen before. These were not his; they belonged to the corpse that sat there. But the repulsion was his own. 
He heard footsteps approach from behind. They sounded clearer than anything he had ever heard before. He knew they belonged to Aki. He heard the blood trickle from her shoulder and he knew she was hurt. Alan stood up, turned around, and started to dig inside his pockets for anything to heal the wound.
She shook her head and turned her shoulder away from him. "I'll live," she said. She looked over at the body and asked, "Is that him?"
"What's left of him." Alan's shadow covered the sparkling form. He put a finger to its forehead and pressed. With a clarion tinkle, it split and crumpled under his touch. The shoulders and the rest of the body followed, turning into a pile of diamond dust that dispersed and scattered. All that was left was the violet cloth. But this was no victory.
"How're we going to get back to the Aurelius?" Aki asked. "Even if we get a ship it won't start. Neither of us are royals."
"I?I think I know how." He rubbed his hands together to get rid of the dust and stepped around to the back of the throne. "Come close," he said.
The pattern came to his feet as if he had known it for years. He tapped a sequence of fifteen stone tiles behind the crystal throne, each tile indistinguishable from the other. His movements were controlled and precise. With a final tap of his toe, the throne and the surrounding floor lowered into the ground, descending through a shaft built into the side of the citadel.
"How did you know?" Aki asked. Her hair flew up around her as they went down.
"He used me to get to Ashra," Alan said. "I saw his life, the memories he had and the things he knew. It was so vast and spanned more years than I could ever live. It was like a dream; I forget all the details and it's harder to remember when I try to grasp it. But when it's in front of me, I know what to do."
"Did he leave anything else behind?" Aki asked. The worry was clear in her voice.
"Maybe. We can figure it out once he's dead and we have Ashra back."
The lift was quick. Their descent was lit by lights spaced evenly around the corridor. The stone floor going down and the walls of steel that passed them going up made for a strange contrast. 
The throne went into the lower levels of the palace. When they stepped through the doors at the bottom, they entered the launching bay for the emperor's personal armada. Starships were lined up in neat rows. Far in the back, Alan could make out the top of a capital warship that neither he nor any other Einhart had ever seen before. He realized his vision had improved as well.
"Which one do we take?" Aki asked. They walked down the rows of ships, each one different from the last, each one designed for a different purpose. There was one for stealth, reminding him of the Umbra. There was another showy one in the shape of the Sanctum emblem, like a miniature Javelin, used for diplomatic visits to conquered worlds.
He settled on a ship that was designed for speed and range. As his eyes moved over the curves of its hull, one word floated to the top of his mind. Leidenfrost. The Leidenfrost wasn't particularly large, but he knew it had the equivalent of a medbed inside it. "This one," he said. As he approached, the door automatically slid open and a span of light lowered to the ground, acting as a ramp. He went in first, checking to see if it was empty. When nothing came from the shadows, he helped Aki climb aboard and led her to the medbed in the back. 
"The controls for the medbed should be similar," he said. "Once I start up the ship it'll be active."
Aki nodded. She secured the pair of swords before lowering herself onto the cushion.
In the cockpit, Alan pressed his palm to the dashboard. The lights turned on and the engines hummed with life. He was both relieved and worried that the ship recognized him. His hands glided effortlessly across the three light consoles, toggling switches for the shields and engines. As the engines powered up and the ship rose from the ground, a memory of designing the consoles themselves flashed briefly in his mind. He shook his head, clearing it of the vision. Bringing the ship around, he dialed in the sequence to open the blast doors that faced the last known position of the Aurelius. The sets of doors opened, revealing Sanctuary's shield and the stars beyond. Black space beckoned to him.
"How're you doing back there?" he asked.
Aki watched as the machine rebuilt her joints, bone and muscle. "Never been better," she shouted to the front.
"Good. Hold on, it's going to be a bumpy ride."
Aided by magnetic accelerators, the ship shot forward and cleared the shielding of Sanctuary.

Chapter 52

When the emperor opened his eyes for the second time, he saw an unfamiliar ceiling above him. He lifted his hand. He marveled at the skin, supple and smooth, maintaining its shape without any effort on his part. Strands of white hair flowed between his fingers.
He used his voice for the first time. "Let us begin," he said to himself. The body's real voice was much younger than the voice Ashra had used in the past. "Guren," he called.
"I am here, My Lord."
"Prepare a ship for me in the dock. The Einhart will be graced with my presence. When I am finished, I shall leave and expand the empire to worlds we have not seen."
"Your will be done, Your Majesty. Where would His Highness like to begin the assault?" Guren spoke with his head bowed.
"Where is Claudia?"
"On the bridge, sire. The great forces of the empire have defeated the Einhart, but their reinforcements will be arriving soon. The Aurelius has left the battlefield and, unfortunately, there may not be enough essence for your needs. In addition, Ashra has been here before, and they have studied her light trees and have devised defenses against it."
"But I have not been here before." 
"No, My Lord, you have not. They will be in awe of your power."
The emperor hopped off the medbed and walked with bare feet across Guren's office, getting a feel for the body. He looked at the white dress he wore and thought of different colors that would be more suitable.
"Would the emperor like a map of the Aurelius?" Guren asked.
"No need," he said. "Ashra, and now I, can see any human in the area. I shall find each place with ease. Once you are finished securing me a ship, meet me on the bridge. I shall be there shortly."
"As you command." Guren headed out the door.
"It's time to test this body out," the emperor said to himself. A small dish of ice appeared in his hand. On top of it, a seed of light.

Chapter 53

Since her attendants were either dead or incapacitated, Claudia had dried off and donned the suit of the High Adjudicant by herself. There was solace and comfort in its weight and the way it hugged her body. She had never retreated from battle before, but Sanctuary's defenses were greater than she or her strategists predicted. 
When they ran out of medbeds, they took to treating the wounded on the bridge. Claudia organized the injured in accordance to the severity of their wounds. She even lent her own hand, giving injections, wrapping bandages and comforting those who had no treatment options left.
She brushed the hair out of a young man's eyes and wiped the sweat from his brow. He held a hand against his stomach, where a jagged piece of metal, once a part of the ceiling support, was embedded. He was still star-struck and in awe as she tended to him personally, and perhaps her presence was enough to block the pain.
The bridge doors opened. Claudia stood up, ready for the next wave of medbeds to come down. Instead, a single figure stood in the doorway, framed by light. Claudia recognized her immediately. "Ashra?"
The figure stepped forward onto the bridge. He looked over at her and spoke. "This is Ashra no longer." He appraised the bridge and those standing by the High Adjudicant. "You've done well for yourself, Claudia," he said with a smile.
In that moment, she knew. "Open fire!" she ordered.
Those around the High Adjudicant didn't know who it was, but they obeyed. A symphony of explosions rang out around her and a hail of bullets followed, all directed towards the walkway that led to the bridge. But when they hit, the sound wasn't that of metal tearing through flesh. 
Thick slabs of ice surrounded the emperor. The bullets barely penetrated them before they were stopped; they only left cracks on their surfaces. Since the ice was free from impurities, it seemed like Claudia was viewing the emperor through sheets of glass. He looked at them all, passive and bored.
"You've left Sanctuary," Claudia said. "There's no power for you to draw on. You can stay in your shell but you don't have enough to mount an offense. You've boarded the wrong ship," she said.
His voice was muffled through the wall of ice but all heard it clearly. "Have you not seen the new me? There've been some?upgrades," he said, examining his own hand.
"Ashra's abilities are nullified here." Claudia glanced back at the young man she had been tending to. He was weak but still alive, staring wide-eyed. "You have no death to use," she continued. "Either way, you've lost. Give up now and your end will be quick. Draw this out, and I will ensure that every representative from every world you've been to will have a chance to defile your living corpse."
"Hmph. You never could see three steps ahead, Claudia."
He looked at a corner of the room, where a scientist had been standing in shock. "Guren, if you would."
The surprise left the scientist's face, replaced by a neutral stare.
Claudia looked at the doctor. "Guren?"
Guren ignored her. He pulled out his gun. Those closest to Claudia formed a shield around her. Aiming the gun at his own head instead, he said, "My life for the Sanctum." Those near him tried to stop him, but he had already pulled the trigger. A single report rang out. He was dead before his body hit the ground.
In the Empyrean, the emperor pulled the light from Guren and held it in his hands. He played with it, pulling it and molding it into different shapes, but it didn't take any form in reality. "Tell me how you do this," he said to Ashra inside the tree. "Show me how you bring the drasil into the world."
Trapped within the tree, Ashra heard but didn't respond.
"Make it easy for them," he continued. "A swift death is a form of compassion." When she still remained silent, he walked over to the tree and broke off a branch. The whole of the Empyrean shuddered at the event. Ashra felt a piece of her world slip away, replaced only by pain.
"I will do it myself then," he said. It was by no means a tree, but the light he held in his hand was enough. Layering the Empyrean over his view of the bridge, he saw the seed of the drasil take form, though it was a misshapen blob that struggled to find shape.
"Stay away from it," Claudia said, holding her arms out as if to protect her crew. 
The emperor waved his hands and the seed moved forward, though it was hampered by the shielding throughout the bridge. He hurled the seed towards Claudia, who jumped out of its way with surprising speed. The injured young man behind her, however, didn't have the energy to move. The seed went through his chest and continued through the bowels of the ship. He gasped once and was still. The emperor, however, had lost his one weapon.
"If I can't kill you here, I'll do it from outside," the emperor said. He had backed up through the blast doors. They shut in front of him. With a wave of his hand the ice slabs that surrounded him became fluid. The liquid seeped into the crevices and base, solidifying and freezing the mechanisms that opened and closed the doors. That would buy him enough time to make it to the dock and destroy the Aurelius once and for all.
This new body, while young, did not have the stamina he used to have. Ashra's attempts at impeding his control also took energy to oppose. His limbs were uncoordinated and he made slow progress. But the ship Guren had prepared for him wasn't far. He formed a spear of ice and made his way down the corridor.

Chapter 54

Alan steered with one hand as he activated his com with the other. "Argus, you there?" he asked.
Argus was startled awake by the sound in his ears. "Boss! I'm glad to hear your voice. Did you finish-" There was grunt from Argus as he turned away to talk to someone else. "Thank you madam, but I am fine. Leave this bed for someone who needs it." There was some arguing and then a thud as Argus landed on his feet. "Sorry about that."
"Argus, are you really okay?"
Argus glanced down at the new flesh, indistinguishable from the rest. All that remained of the wound were two holes in his armor. "It went deep but the actual surface area that needed repair wasn't much. Wounds of the body are easy to mend; it is the mind that carries the scars," he said. "The medic just wanted to me stay longer since the order came from you."
"Your health is most important. Can you run?"
"I can sprint," he said.
"Good. Get to the docking bay and wait for us there."
"Gotcha. Hold on a sec-" He was silent as he read a message broadcast ship-wide. "This couldn't be referring to Ashra could it? Kill on sight?"
Alan's fears had come true. "She isn't Ashra anymore," he said. "If you see her, be careful and?just let me know where she is," he finished.
"Sure thing boss," but Argus didn't sound so sure. "I'll see you in Dock B."
It would take some time for Argus to reach the launching area; the medical bay was on the other side of the Aurelius and the pipe transports were down.
During his approach, Alan had trouble finding Dock B because he didn't recognize the Aurelius anymore. The damage had been severe. Burns covered the armor plating, and in some parts the plating was completely missing. He passed through where one wing should've been. All that was left was a deep groove in the shape of a crescent moon. He circled half the ship when winking green lights caught his attention. 
He guided the Leidenfrost inside. In the middle of the dock, he saw the ship Argus and Ashra had taken, resting at an odd angle.
The cruiser landed smoothly, and he barely felt it when the struts took on the weight of the ship. He passed Aki on the way out and looked at her shoulder. A major artery had been severed and she lay unconscious within the medbed as it repaired her. It was funny, he thought. Though the technology was different, they were all human, and they hurt and healed in the same way. He removed his hand from the blue cover and headed out the door.
Inside the Aurelius, the docking bay was eerily quiet. The majority of the fighters had been deployed in the fight against Sanctuary. It was empty except for a few ships that were under repair and couldn't fly. The sound of his hurried footsteps echoed throughout the bay. As he ran past Ashra's ship, he wondered where she was. Her body was on this ship, controlled by the emperor. But her mind, he knew, was still somewhere inside that body. He heard a shout come from near the entrance and turned midstride.
When he got there, the mechanic that cried out was already dead, a shaft of ice sticking out of him. 
<Watch out!> Ashra said. Her presence immediately disappeared from his mind as she was yanked away. Her body came into view, stepping out from behind a row of armory crates.
Alan gasped when he saw what the princess had become. The emperor looked at him with piercing eyes. The voice was the voice of young girl, right for the size of the body. But it sounded wrong to Alan's ears.
"Still alive?" the emperor said. "Even after your mind was torn apart?" The slightest trace of surprise etched itself across his brows.
"I have something to live for," Alan responded. He pulled out his gun and aimed it at the emperor.
He smiled. "Would you? Really? She's still here," he said, tapping his head. "She misses you."
"Enough. Release her."
"Even if I did, I'm afraid there's nowhere for her to go. The body is mine. And in a short time, the mind will be as well. Say your farewells while she can still hear them."
Alan's face betrayed no emotion, but he couldn't pull the trigger. The emperor lifted his hand and another spear of ice appeared, floating above his raised pointer finger. He arched his back and then whipped his arm forward. The ice spear flew towards Alan. 
Alan dodged to the side with a roll, though the tip of the spear tore a hole through the side of his pants.
The emperor was prepared and pulled the essence of the mechanic out of his body. He shot it towards Alan, who was just getting to his feet. 
Alan was going to block it with his arm, but he knew it was useless. He fell backwards onto the floor hoping it would fly over him. But the light followed, and was about to run through his head.
In the Empyrean, Ashra had seen enough. She burst forth from inside the tree that imprisoned her, turning the trunk and branches into nothing more than kindling. With her staff in hand, she charged forward. The emperor only had enough time to turn around when he felt something pierce his heart. He looked down at the wood protruding from his chest. He followed it to the trembling hands that clutched it, to the girl with white hair, to the child who did what no one else could.
"Everything I am," Ashra said, "is because of you." The hate and pride were clear in her voice. The staff glowed with the energy of the stars of the Empyrean. The emperor shuddered as the light ran through him. It found any outlet it could to escape, shooting out of his fingertips and mouth, until he was only a bright silhouette of a man with his arms outstretched. With one final burst, the emperor exploded in a brilliant shower of light. 
Ashra sighed and collapsed onto the island. Motes of light, all that remained of the emperor, drifted around her like snow.
She watched as the light touched the water. They disappeared into the depths, and she expected them to shine on their way down. But instead, what was once clear water became black and murky.
There was no source, but a disembodied voice whispered, "You will never be rid of me, Ashra. As long as you are alive, I shall live on through you." It was an echo of an echo, a murmur she could barely hear over the quiet waves that lapped upon the island. But it was there.
As much as she wished it wasn't true, she knew the emperor was right. His blood coursed through her veins. That bond would be with her for the rest of her life. It'd be enough to sustain his existence, however faint and pitiful it would be.
"I will decide the course of my life, not you," she said.
With the tree gone, the Empyrean lost its foundation. The stars started falling from a sky that was quickly getting dimmer.

Chapter 55

A moment before touching his skin, the light seed stopped between Alan's eyes, filling his view with white. He blinked once, and it was gone. Putting his hands on the ground, he stood up slowly and looked at Ashra. She was standing still and her face was blank. Her hands hung limply at her sides. She let out a breath, as if releasing all the energy in her body, and collapsed. Alan dove forward and caught her just before she hit the floor. 
She seemed heavier than when he first held her in the quarantine chamber. Perhaps it was the strength of her will that weighed more in his arms, or maybe it was the confidence she had found. He didn't know what it was, but out of habit and instinct, he pressed his forehead against hers and kissed her between her closed eyes.
His vision tilted and spun. When the world righted itself, he was no longer in the docking bay, but within the Empyrean. 
He had never seen it as dark as this. The stars seemed to be fading. Even the perpetuals were becoming transparent, losing their color to the night sky. The tree was no more; it was split into scattered branches, twigs, and matchsticks.
Resting upon what remained of its trunk was Ashra. Flower petals from the drasil swirled around the center of the island, covering her like a blanket. Alan hurried to reach her, the sand flying behind his boots.
The scent of the drasil became stronger as he neared. He knelt on the ground when he reached her and pulled her to him. "Ashra," he said. "Ashra, I'm sorry. I never meant to hurt you."
She lifted her head and smiled weakly. "There is nothing to apologize for, Alan. I couldn't have wished for a better outcome."
"The tree," he said, looking at the empty space. "It's gone."
"Yes. Well, it had a good life."
"Is there a way to save it? To save you?" He wanted to hold her closer but was afraid he would crush her.
"My heart says that what I did cannot be undone. And even if there was a way, I wouldn't do it." She gazed at the sky as more stars faded out of existence. The water that surrounded the island had turned completely black. "The emperor is still here. No matter what I do, my father will always haunt me. He'll always be a part of me. As long as I am alive, he can come back. I know it. I feel it." When she said it, Alan felt a sinister presence in the skies and in the water, slowly encroaching upon the island.
Despite that, he still said, "I don't think that's true. There's always a way. We'll find it."
She shook her head. "I was born to be a tool, a weapon, an immortal vessel. But now, because of the choices you and my mother made, I have the power to decide where my life will go and how it will end."
"Don't talk like that." He sat with his back to the stump and balanced her on his legs. He cradled her and said, "You don't have to do this." But even as the words came out, he knew that she did.
Alan's uniform disappeared, replaced by a simple shirt and linen trousers. He had not seen these clothes in years; they had been lost back when Cybele fell. But he remembered them and loved the way they felt against his skin. They even smelled the same, reminding him of a time in his life that was so painfully beautiful that he had tried to forget it. Yet it was a time that he never really wanted to forget. "You're safe," he said.
She curled into the warm embrace of his arms. "I know."
They held each other for what seemed like an eternity, though it may have only been a minute. Rousing herself, she used the last of her strength to push herself up. "I need to do this before he comes closer," she said.
"No, Ashra. You don't need to," Alan said softly.
"I do."
Alan felt an invisible force grip him around the shoulders and immobilize him.
"I'm glad I finally got to see you with my own eyes," Ashra said with a smile. "Goodbye Alan. Take care of yourself, and go with all my love." With a wave of her hand, Alan fell unconscious and disappeared from the Empyrean.
When he came to, he was still holding Ashra. She opened her eyes. When she saw him, she tilted her head up and kissed him on the forehead between his eyes. A moment later, a blast of cold radiated from her body, knocking him to the ground. Shackles made of ice appeared around his wrists and ankles, binding him.
"No, Ashra. Don't do this," he pleaded. She only smiled as she floated up off the floor of the bay. The unused essence from earlier reappeared as a small seed that hung in the air between her feet and the ground. It thinned and flattened out into a long sheet, like a length of fabric. The last thing Alan saw was her smile.
The light cocoon sealed itself around Ashra. It began to shrink steadily. The sphere grew smaller and smaller. Alan didn't want to but forced himself to watch, feeling the tears pool around the bottom of his cheek. The light receded, leaving nothing behind it, until it was as bright and as small as a star in the night sky. Then it disappeared.
Ashra was no more. All that was left was a pendant in the shape of a crescent moon, its silver chain gone. It clattered to the floor. 
The ice that bound him melted to water. Alan slowly got to his knees and raised his hands as if she were still there, as if he could still touch her. But when there was nothing to fill his fingers, he put his hands over the pendant and dragged it to his heart. He crumpled into a ball, pressed his head into his chest, and wept. He had failed as a father, twice. 

Chapter 56

The first thought in Argus's mind was, how could a man like Alan look so small? He slowly walked up to him and put his hand on Alan's back. He felt Alan quiver and shake as the man grieved harder under his touch, a touch that was meant to heal.
Alan unburied his head and looked at the docking bay, at the Aurelius, at all the memories he had here. He thought of how each memory always led back to Ashra. Claudia had thrown their lives away in an attempt to enter Sanctuary, and though he didn't hate her for it because it was her job, he wondered how she could have so little compassion. He wondered if his life was meant to be more than what it was now. He looked up at Argus. "I have to go," he said, between long and shaky breaths.
"Where will you go?"
"I don't know, but I can't stay here anymore. I'd love to have you by my side, but this is asking too much. The rules of the Einhart are unbending and I can't risk your life."
"You needn't say anymore. Desertion only applies to those who are loyal to an institution. I am loyal to a person." Argus offered his hand and Alan took it. "My life's task is done," he said. "In time I will return to Galea, but for now, there are more pressing matters."
The two walked back to the edge of the dock. The Leidenfrost was where he had left it. Aki leaned against the doorframe, waiting for them. "We can head to Aurora for supplies. And you may need more protection after you leave. The Einhart have quite a few contracts with my worldmen," she said, heading into the ship. 
"With you watching my back, no man in the galaxy could be safer," Alan said. He looked at both of them. "Thank you." He took his seat in the middle of the console. With a few deft strokes, two more chairs appeared and Argus and Aki sat to either side of him. At his touch, the cruiser activated. The landing struts retracted and the ship hovered inside the docking bay. 
His wrist buzzed. Claudia was trying to reach him, but he ignored her and turned the device off.
They took off and left the Aurelius behind.
The vastness of space, cold and empty yet filled with promise and opportunity, engulfed him. Which way do I go? Alan thought. Left, right, up, down, these directions mean nothing in space.
As he stared at the star charts and maps of known planets and territories, he caught the faintest scent of drasil flowers. A gentle breeze rustled through his mind and a voice said, <Left.>
Alan looked left. There was a planet that was covered in green, with two or three moons, depending on who was asked. Alan clutched the pendant and set the coordinates on the light console. The Leidenfrost began to pick up speed.
A black halo surrounded the ship as it shifted into darkspace. Alan would find redemption among those stars.
###
Afterword

Dear Reader,

Thank you for making it to the end of my first book, Ashra, or as I like to think of it, My Daddy Issues In Space (trademark). I hope you enjoyed this romp through the galaxy, and in the moments between the violence, I also hope you may have found some deeper connection to the characters and words.
I had the idea for this novel back when I was in Japan, and in the months between jobs, I wrote it out. It was a pleasant experience, filled with midnight runs followed by daytime sleeping, and it was as I was writing it that I knew, without a doubt, that this is what I wanted to do for the rest of my life. 
This work is a work of love. I understand if some of you found a pirated version of it somewhere online. It happens. Y'arrrrr. While I'd like to live off writing novels like this one in the future, I am honored by the simple fact that people took the time out of their busy lives to read it. And if you found it for free, please do me a solid and post a review or tell some of your friends about it.
If you did pay for it, I am deeply grateful beyond words. You've helped me survive another day, and you've given me encouragement and assistance towards making my dreams come true.
My request, Dear Reader, is that if you enjoyed Ashra, please give a copy or two or five to your family and friends that may enjoy reading this sci-fi monstrosity with an overabundance of the word explosion. As an author with a day job in something that's not marketing, I have no clue how to market books, so I can only ask kindly and hope for the best. If you're feeling up to it, you can also leave a review at your favorite retailer. If there's something you'd like to share with me personally, feel free to email me at jonlang108@gmail.com. I'd love to hear your feedback and thoughts.
Like all endeavors, this book could not have been finished without help, and I have had plenty along the way.
The first order of thanks would be to my editor, Rachel Tiderman. If you need top-notch editing, send her an email at: rachel.tiderman@gmail.com. Because a stationery turret would've been hilarious.
The second would be to my cover artist, Ivan Hobbs. With a pen, I can only put words to paper, but give this guy one and he'll create a magnificent piece of art. You can find his work here: www.ivanhobbs.com.
Finally, thanks to Greg, for going through the manuscript and pointing out an additional number of bugs, to Adam, for being the first to read it, and to Subo, my literary partner in crime. 
As for future books in this series, everyone is busy, yes, but I would feel incomplete if I did not see Ashra and Alan's story to the end. Alan's ex comes back in the next one!
Again, thank you for reading. I hope you enjoyed the journey as much as I did.

With eternal gratitude,

Jon Lang
About the author

I'm not pretentious and/or famous enough to write about myself in the third-person for the author bio, so I'll stick with what I know. I was raised deep in the Midwest, where the land is sold in acres and the horses, cows, and chickens outnumber people. I fled as soon as I could by going to UC-Berkeley, and ended up graduating with a degree in Japanese with a few years of molecular cell biology on the side. Fleeing even further, my travels took me to Tokyo, where I discovered the best sushi and the worst weather. The wind has now blown me to Seattle, where I can be found running down Pike St. yelling, "Go Seahawks!" at the top of my lungs, in turn scaring small animals and children.

Apparently people tweet. I should get on that. Follow me here: http://twitter.com/jonlang108
